# **THE HONEYMOON**

---

# **CHAPTER ONE: THE GOD GIVEN GIFT OF A CLITORIS AND HOW TO USE IT**

---

## **INT. BEDROOM – PORTSMOUTH, OHIO – EARLY SUMMER MORNING – JUNE 1990**

The room breathes before she does.

It’s a second-story space in a modest house — not rich, not poor. Just lived in. A poster of *Chariots of Fire* is curling at the corners above a battered desk. A pair of well-used running shoes rest beneath a bookshelf sagging under the weight of paperbacks, devotionals, and one dog-eared copy of *Song of Solomon*.

The light from the east window filters through lace curtains — soft and golden, like it’s decided not to intrude.

The bed is unmade but clean. A simple quilt, faded from washes. A cross hangs above the headboard — plain wood, no ornamentation.

**JEN SPARKS**, 18, lies in the center of the bed — half-curled, one leg drawn slightly up. She's barefoot, wearing an oversized white cotton tank top and a pair of men’s boxer shorts, frayed at the waistband. Nothing clingy. Nothing styled. Just comfort.

Her body is not displayed. It is rested. She’s not posing. She’s not aware of being seen.

Jen has the frame of a runner who hasn’t trained in months — lean, but unpressured. There’s muscle in her calves that doesn’t ask for attention. Her shoulders slope like they’ve earned rest. A faint tanline traces across her neck, the mark of a cross she only takes off to sleep.

She shifts slightly. Exhales through her nose. No alarm clock. No outside noise. Just her own rhythm. Her own time. She opens her eyes slowly, like someone surfacing from a deep, contented dream.

And then she does nothing.

She just lies there, blinking up at the ceiling. No rush. No task list. No name to respond to. This is the beginning of the day. Her day. She reaches out and touches the journal on her nightstand — the leather cover familiar, like skin.

A pencil mark.  A verse.  *Psalm 139*, circled lightly in the corner.

“*You knit me together in my mother’s womb*…”

She smiles. It’s not performative. It’s not even happiness. It’s peace.

She lays back again. Breathes. Her hand rests on her stomach for a moment, then moves — unhurried — up along her side, over the slope of a ribcage she doesn’t judge. Just… familiar.

She isn’t thinking about anyone. There is no image. No fantasy. Only sensation. The morning is warm. Her body is warm. The room is still. And so, she moves her hand lower.  Not with tension.  Not with shame.  Not with need. With curiosity.  With trust.  With full knowledge that this moment belongs to no one else.

---

## **INT. BEDROOM – CONTINUOUS** – JUNE 1990

The room is still wrapped in morning light. Outside, a mourning dove calls once, then goes quiet. A breeze stirs the lace curtain and dies again. Jen’s hand rests lightly on her lower stomach, fingers curled like she’s holding a prayer. She shifts slightly — not for comfort, not for theatrics. Just because her body told her to.

Her eyes are open, unfocused, gazing at the ceiling. She’s not trying to imagine anything.

But then… she remembers something.

A shot from *Dead Calm*.  Nicole Kidman standing barefoot on the deck of a sailboat, hair whipping in the wind. Still. Calm. Capable. Jen exhales through her nose.  If she could be anyone…

It wouldn’t be for the fame. Or the attention. It would be to walk through a room with that poise.  To know how to carry herself — like she was already whole.

She tilts her head slightly on the pillow.  Her hand moves again — just a little lower.  She doesn’t rush.  She doesn’t perform.  She adjusts.

A part of her wonders — would Nicole do it this way? No. Not Nicole Kidman, the person.  The idea of her.  That ease. That confidence.

Jen isn't imagining anyone else in the room.  She’s imagining who she wants to be — the kind of woman who knows where her body ends and her mind begins, and treats both with joy.

She lets her legs part just slightly.  The sheet folds with her.  Her left hand grips the fabric at her side — a grounding gesture, not drama. This isn't an act of rebellion.  It’s an act of ownership.

The rhythm begins — barely perceptible. Her fingertips trace the outline of sensation, no destination in mind. Her mouth is slightly open, but no sound escapes.  She breathes evenly. Shallow. Then deeper.

The breeze picks up again. The curtain lifts.  The light hits the corner of the *Dead Calm* poster on the wall. Her breath catches, just once.  A tiny gasp, like she surprised herself.  She smiles — not broadly.  But enough to know it mattered.

Her fingers still.  Not because she’s done.  Because she’s arrived. And she stays there — still, centered, breathing.  Hand resting softly against her skin.  Eyes open now. Focused.

---

## **INT. BEDROOM – MOMENTS LATER – JUNE 1990**

Jen doesn’t hurry. She doesn’t chase climax like a finish line. She inhabits it — the space before, the slow build, the ripple between pulse and prayer. Her right hand moves in small, knowing circles — not friction, not function. Invitation. Her hips shift just slightly, enough to follow her own rhythm. Not theatrical. Not effortful. Just honest.

The breeze outside lifts again, like it’s keeping time. Her hair fans out across the pillow. One curl sticks to her temple with sweat. She doesn’t brush it away.

She exhales — longer this time. There’s no sound of struggle.  No breathy, exaggerated panting.  Just a body, cooperating with itself. She closes her eyes. Not to escape.  To stay inside the moment. Her jaw flexes slightly. A toe curls under the blanket.

The room smells like lavender lotion and old paper and sun-warmed cotton. Her childhood trophies still line a shelf. A Polaroid of her sister, crooked in the frame. The corner of a Sunday school bulletin poking from under a stack of books. All of it — her.  And she is not divided from it now. She is with herself.  Fully.  Gently.

She presses a little deeper.  The tension in her belly coils, then loosens.  Not pain. Not pressure.  Just… promise.

Her breath changes — a short inhale, then stillness. Eyes flutter open, then close again.  Her fingers move in a rhythm that knows itself. She doesn’t cry out. She smiles. And when the release comes — when it finally breaks through her spine and ribs and throat — it isn’t loud. It’s grateful.

She exhales like someone laying down a burden she didn’t even know she was carrying. She holds herself there, in the stillness.  Not reaching for anything.  Just being.

The wind outside shifts. A bird chirps once. The world keeps going. But Jen stays exactly where she is — hand resting gently over her pelvis, chest rising slowly, peace settling like a blanket.

She doesn’t reach for her clothes. She reaches for her journal. She writes one line — in pencil, in the corner of a clean page. “Felt like grace.” She underlines it once. Nothing else. And then she closes the book, rolls onto her side, and watches the curtain dance.

---

## **INT. BEDROOM – MOMENTS LATER – STILL JUNE 1990**

Jen lies on her side, knees drawn gently up, her fingers still resting across her abdomen. The journal lies open next to her, the words barely dry: “Felt like grace.”

The light in the room has shifted — just slightly. A sunbeam now spills across her foot, catching the dust in the air. The breeze smells faintly of cut grass and warm tar from the road.  She exhales through her nose — long, luxurious. She shifts. Her left knee straightens slightly. Her heel drags the sheet down an inch. She pauses. Smiles to herself. Knows.  This isn’t about need anymore. It’s about the invitation of a second wave.

She turns slowly onto her back again, both hands now resting on her stomach. She waits. No urgency. No countdown. Just listening. Then — one hand moves lower again.  This time, she doesn't hesitate. She already knows the map. She’s just revisiting the best parts of it.  Her breath catches sooner. Not rushed — remembered.  This isn’t escalation.  It’s exploration.

A finger drags a slow line down her inner thigh — just because it feels good. Just because she can.  She tilts her hips slightly. Re-centers herself on the mattress. This time it’s not a climb.It’s a reverberation.  Her lips part — not in a moan, but a soft hum.  Like she’s tuning into a station that only plays her song.  The second climax builds differently — not higher, but deeper.  A pulling sensation, soft and low, like a bowstring being drawn in her spine.

She reaches that place again —  not with struggle.  Not with pressure. With ease. With welcome.  With permission. This time, when she comes, her mouth opens, but there’s no sound — just a long exhale, like she’s releasing light. Her toes flex. Her back arches slightly. Her hand holds still at the final moment — not pressing, not pulling — holding the note. 

And then stillness again.

She falls back into the bed, arms spread slightly. Her breath is deeper now. Her smile is wider — not triumphant, just content. This is the difference. This is arrival, not collapse.  Jen lies there. Sweat slicks one strand of hair to her cheek. She doesn’t wipe it away. She likes it.  Her journal stays open, but she doesn’t write again. She already said enough.

Instead, she pulls the sheet up to her waist. Rolls onto her side again. And for the first time this morning — she laughs. Just once. Quiet. To herself. Not from embarrassment. From joy.  Then she closes her eyes. And rests.

---

## **INT. BEDROOM – FINAL MOMENTS – JUNE 1990**

The journal lies open, unread. The pen’s uncapped, ink drying. The sheet is half-kicked, caught around her ankle like an afterthought. Jen exhales. The kind of exhale you only earn after knowing yourself fully.   She closes her eyes — not because she’s drained.  Because she’s done.  Because rest is allowed. Welcomed.

Outside, a lawnmower coughs to life two houses down. A dog barks. A truck backfires.  She doesn’t stir. The room breathes with her. Still. Light. Clean.

**FADE TO BLACK.**

---

# **CHAPTER TWO: INVITATIONS**

---

## **INT. JEN’S PARENTS' KITCHEN – EARLY EVENING – JULY 1994**

The fridge hums. The ceiling fan clicks slightly on each rotation. A pile of RSVP cards sits between a half-eaten tuna casserole and a worn King James Bible.

**JEFF CREMEANS** (23) sits at the table, in a pressed short-sleeve shirt, neck pink from mowing the lawn earlier.  **JEN SPARKS** (21), hair pinned back, flips through a notepad full of circled names, side notes, and anxious underlines.

They are surrounded by calm and tension, like two people trying to throw a wedding and manage an emotional airstrike at the same time.

**JEN** (reading from the list)  
So that’s forty-seven from church, plus my cousins, plus the Browning girls…

(pause)  
And you still want to invite all of Commuted?

**[[5.2. JEFF CREMEANS MODERN REVIEW|Cremeans]]** (slowly)  
They’re my guys, Jen.

**JEN**  
They’re also on the cover of Spin right now with their shirts off and “SEX SAVES” airbrushed across their chests.

**CREMEANS**  (to himself)  
I told them that was a bad idea.

**JEN** (smiling, barely)  
Did you? Because I seem to remember you laughing when Bill mailed you that picture.

**CREMEANS**  
It was a nervous laugh.

**JEN**  
It was a full-body wheeze.

He shrugs, caught. She sets the pen down and sighs.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
I’m not mad. I just… want this to be ours. Quiet. Meaningful.  Not a photo op next to a guy who once lit his shoe on fire for a crowd of sorority girls.

**CREMEANS**  
Bill was drunk. And that was an accident.

**JEN**  
It was also on purpose.

They sit in silence for a beat. A cicada screams outside.

**CREMEANS**  
Jeff’ll behave. He knows how important this is.

**JEN**  
Jeff I trust.  Kathy… I know of.

**CREMEANS**  
She’s not what the papers say. She’s complicated, but she’s not…

**JEN**  
A hurricane with lipstick?

**CREMEANS**  
That was one time. And she apologized to the furniture.

**JEN**  
I don’t want her to behave. I want her to not come.

He doesn’t say anything. She exhales, softer.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
I’m not threatened. I’m just… protective.  Of this. Of us.

**CREMEANS**  
She won’t make a scene.

**JEN**  
She doesn’t have to. She is the scene.

(pause)  
Invite her. But don’t seat her near my Aunt Laurel. That woman senses trauma.

**CREMEANS**  
If we don’t invite Kathy… the rest won’t come.

**JEN**  (sighs)  
Because they’re afraid she’ll roast them behind their backs?

**CREMEANS**  
Because she’s the core. The mouth. The heart, sometimes.  They orbit her. Always have.

**JEN**  
You don’t.

**CREMEANS**  
No. I escaped the orbit. But I still send postcards.

He reaches across the table and covers her hand.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Thank you. For making room. I know it’s not fair.

**JEN**  
I’m not looking for fair. I’m looking for peace.

(pause)  
And no fog machines.

---

# **CHAPTER THREE: NAKED AND UNAFRAID IN A BAPTIST CHURCH**

---

## **INT. FELLOWSHIP HALL – WEDDING DAY – AN HOUR BEFORE CEREMONY**

The band walks in like a minor crime scene: half ironed, half unsure, all trying very hard not to be themselves.

- [[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|Jeff]], in a muted gray suit, already buttoned up like he’s bracing for impact.  He accessorizes like a Viking.  
- Jeremy, wearing the exact outfit the invitation suggested. Probably with a backup tie in the glove box, just in case.
- Bill, chewing gum and adjusting a bolo tie he swears “counts as formal.”
- Gilley, holding a Bible he found in the back of a pew because he didn’t know where to put his hands.
- Jim, sunglasses still on. Inside. At a wedding.
   
They pause at the entrance. The room smells like sheet cake and nervous forgiveness.

**[[4.1 BILL DAVENPORT character bible|BILL]]:**  
Wait — is that Kathy?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Yes. Keep your voice down. And your opinions down.

**[[4.6 JEREMY EVANS character bible|JEREMY]]:**  
She looks… really put together.

**[[4.2 JEREMY GILLEY character bible|GILLEY]]:**  
Which means something is about to explode.

**JIM:**  (grimly)  
Not in this room. Not today.

**BILL:**  
Okay, but is it really a wedding if I can’t dance or drink?

**JEREMY:**  
You can eat. Quietly. That’s the Baptist way.

**GILLEY:**  
Did you bring a flask?

**BILL:**  
I brought restraint. It’s in my other pocket.

They shuffle to the back pew, trying not to trip on floral arrangements or each other. Jeff lingers, eyes scanning the room — not for trouble, just to remind himself that this is real. That Cremeans made it here. That he made it here.

Kathy catches his eye. She doesn’t smile. She just nods.  And somehow, that’s enough.

---

## **INT. CHURCH BASEMENT – HOLDING AREA – THIRTY MINUTES TO CEREMONY**

It smells like rose potpourri fighting mildew hymnals. There’s a metal fan humming in the corner, doing absolutely nothing. The band is sweating, and not because it’s hot.

- Bill is chewing gum like it owes him money.
- Jeff is staring at a wall like it just insulted him.
- Gilley is trying to figure out if he’s supposed to stand or kneel at any point.
- Jeremy is the only one who has read the program and is therefore the only one breathing normally.
- Jim is praying, or maybe asleep.

**BILL:**  (whispering)  
Is it too late to fake a seizure?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Yes. And if you twitch near a deacon, they’ll lay hands on you and quote Corinthians for six minutes straight.

**GILLEY:**  
What if I just say I have a headache?

**JEREMY:**  
That’s fine. Just don’t say it in the sanctuary. That room hears everything.

**BILL:**  
This is the longest I’ve ever gone without a cigarette, alcohol, or sarcasm. I’m pretty sure I’m turning into a librarian.

**JIM:**  (eyes still closed)  
Librarians are underpaid and deadly. Watch your mouth.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
No dancing. No bar. No music. We are the music. And we are…muted.

**BILL:**  
Muted and moisturized. That’s the real tragedy. I’ve never smelled this clean in my life.

**GILLEY:**  
Why do Baptists love fake flowers?

**JEREMY:**  
So they don’t have to water them on Sunday.

**BILL:**  
This is psychological warfare.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
This is marriage warfare.

**JIM:**  
Marriage is just a well-catered truce.

**GILLEY:**  
How long is the ceremony?

**JEREMY:**  
Thirty minutes, give or take.

**BILL:**  
And we’re not allowed to heckle?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Correct.

**BILL:**  
Not even gently?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
You want to go to hell gently?

They all pause as a CHURCH LADY passes by the open door holding a stack of hymnals. She stops. Looks in.

**CHURCH LADY**  
Y’all behave now. The Lord is watching.

**ALL**  (in unison)  
Yes ma’am.

She leaves.  They collapse slightly.

**BILL:**  
I miss sin.

**JEREMY:**  
You miss beer.

**BILL:**  
Same thing.

---

## **INT. CHURCH HALLWAY – FIFTEEN MINUTES TO CEREMONY**

The air smells like lemon cleaner and suppressed panic. The wedding party is assembling in the corridor behind the sanctuary. Floral arrangements shiver slightly as an A/C unit clunks to life.

**JEFF EVANS** has changed into a tux that fits but feels like it was designed to shame him, is adjusting his cuffs when Bill stops dead in his tracks.

**BILL:**  
Dude. Dude. Why do you have chains on your tux?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
They’re…part of the look.

**BILL:**  
The look? Bro, you’re in the wedding. You’re not emceeing a Nine Inch Nails tribute concert in a planetarium.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
They’re subtle. Decorative. Tasteful.

**BILL:**  
There are three. And one of them’s connected to your wallet. You look like a Victorian bouncer.

**JEREMY:** (to Jeff)  
Are those safety pins?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
They’re…symbolic.

**BILL:**  
Of what?  Your ongoing resistance to joy?

**GILLEY:**  
Honestly, he still looks better than Jim.

**CUT TO:** Jim, sitting in a folding chair, staring dead ahead like he’s awaiting trial. His tie is on sideways. He has no socks. No one knows where he got a carnation.

**JIM:**  
I found it. I kept it.

---

## **INT. CHURCH VESTIBULE – JUST BEFORE CEREMONY**

Cremeans is standing in the small space where grooms wait and overthink their entire lives. The door to the sanctuary is cracked. The organ is playing something docile in C major.

Jeff adjusts his tie — the chain clinking slightly as he tries not to sweat directly onto the boutonniere.

**CREMEANS**  
You’re looking mighty sharp, man.

**[[4.5 KATHY ESPICH character bible|KATHY]]** appearing from the shadows like the ghost of past misbehavior.

**KATHY:**  
He’s wearing chains, Cremeans.

She gestures to his jacket with theatrical concern, as if he’s walked in covered in crime.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
They’re vintage.

**KATHY:**  
They’re probation-chic.

**CREMEANS** (smiling, unbothered)  
So did the Apostle Paul. And look where that got him.

**KATHY:**  
Imprisoned and eventually beheaded?

**CREMEANS**  
Yeah, but inspired some great letters on the way.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
So what you’re saying is — I’m halfway to canonization.

**KATHY:**  
More like halfway to community service.

---

## **INT. VESTIBULE – JUST BEFORE THE CEREMONY BEGINS**

The organ hums low. The pews are full. Somewhere, a deacon is whispering stern things about unity candles.  Cremeans steps away from the doors for a moment and turns to Jeff. Everyone else is buzzing around like bees in ties. This is a quiet pocket.

**CREMEANS** (quietly)  
Hey.

Jeff looks up, instantly alert.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
You look good. I mean that.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
I feel like a kid at a funeral.

**CREMEANS**  
That’s exactly the energy I was hoping for. Listen… when we take pictures, if Jen’s in the shot —  could you maybe… lose the chains?

**JEFF EVANS:** (nods)  
Yeah. Of course.

**CREMEANS**  
Otherwise? You’re good. I’m glad you’re here.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Wouldn’t be anywhere else.

They nod — that male nod that somehow means ten thousand feelings were acknowledged and filed properly.

**CREMEANS**  
We’re almost there.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Better be. Bill’s running out of things to compliment that aren’t alcoholic.

---

## **INT. BRIDE’S ROOM – TWELVE MINUTES TO CEREMONY**

Chaos.

The air is thick with perfume, static electricity, and the sharp hiss of interpersonal tension. A half-eaten tray of mini quiches sweats beside a curling iron. Every surface is covered in bobby pins, prayer cards, and lipstick tubes with no caps.

**JEN**, standing in the center of the room in a white corset, garters, and carefully selected underwear that no one was supposed to see, is trying very hard not to panic.  Fifteen women — aunts, cousins, friends, a former babysitter, and her mother — are fighting the dress.

**MOM:**  
Where’s the hook? I swear there was a hook!

**COUSIN 1**  
It’s under the flap!

**AUNT LAUREL:**  
That’s not a flap, it’s decorative! Don’t pull that, you’ll break the—

*SNAP*.

A collective gasp. Silence.

**MOM:** (sweetly, tightly)  
If one more person touches this zipper, I will lose my salvation.

**JEN** (quietly)  
Mother. Language.

**MOM:**  
I am using proper language. You don’t want to hear the alternatives.

A bridesmaid dives under the dress like she’s defusing a bomb.

**BRIDESMAID**  
We need the crochet hook! Where’s the crochet hook?

**JEN**  
Why do we even have a crochet hook?

**COUSIN 2**  
To button the tiny satin buttons down the back. It’s a whole thing.

**JEN**  
That’s what fingers are for.

**MOM:**  
Fingers are clumsy. This is sacred. And expensive.

Jen exhales. Deeply. Looks at herself in the mirror — flushed, radiant, surrounded by people who love her loudly and with extreme tactile enthusiasm.

**JEN**  
I was going to say something profound in this moment. But my underwear’s been in a fistfight for twenty minutes and I’m starting to lose feeling in my thighs.

---

## **INT. BRIDE’S ROOM – TEN MINUTES TO CEREMONY**

Still chaos. Jen is halfway zipped, breathless, arms slightly lifted like she’s being fitted for emotional armor. Her mother is praying, cursing, and counting buttons all at once. One bridesmaid is fanning herself with a church bulletin. Someone else is using a bobby pin as a weapon.

*KNOCK KNOCK.*

A calm male voice from outside the door:

**CREMEANS** (O.S.)  
Hey, is it okay if I come in for a sec?

Instant, deafening, simultaneous:

**ALL WOMEN** (shrieking in unison)  
NO!!!

It’s so loud it hits like a cymbal crash.  The room shakes. A floral arrangement falls over.  In the sanctuary, every head turns.

**PASTOR:** (in the distance)  
…We’re gonna need a few more minutes.

---

## **INT. SANCTUARY – CONTINUOUS**

Bill leans over to Jeff, eyes wide.

**BILL:**  
Is she okay?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
She’s fine.

**BILL:**  
You sure?

**JEFF EVANS:**   
That was the sound of women handling things. God help whoever knocked.

---

## **INT. BRIDE’S ROOM – EIGHT MINUTES TO CEREMONY**

Jen is almost dressed. The dress is on. The final clasp is being fastened. Angels are weeping. But the air is still thick with unresolved tension.

**MOM:** (squinting at her)  
I still don’t understand why you couldn’t wear the full coverage bra.

**JEN** (sighing, without turning around)  
Because it looked like orthopedic scaffolding, Mother.

**MOM:**  
It was supportive.

**JEN**  
So is Jeff Cremeans.

**MOM:**  
It wasn’t…flesh-colored.

**JEN**  
It’s nude. That’s literally the name on the tag.

**MOM:**  
Nude implies…nudity. I don’t want your nude showing through your dress.

**JEN**  
It’s a wedding gown. Not a wet T-shirt contest.

**MOM:** (sotto, for the fifteenth time)  
That bra leaves too much to open inspection.

The room pauses. One bridesmaid stifles a laugh with her hand.

**JEN**  
Mom, if anyone at this wedding is inspecting my chest, they are no longer in the spirit of the day.

**AUNT LAUREL:**  
Amen.

**MOM:**  
Well. I just hope the Lord looks past your neckline and sees your heart.

**JEN**  
That’s the plan.

---

## **INT. BRIDE’S ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

The final button is looped. The dress is secure. The corset is obeying physics. The chaos is retreating. Jen, now almost celestial in silk and quiet fury, turns slowly.

**JEN** (softly)  
Thank you, Aunt Laurel. That was kind.

**AUNT LAUREL:**  
You’re welcome, sweetheart. You look beautiful.

**JEN** (beat; pointed)  
Some people in this room should take notes.

She turns her eyes — not just a glance, a full-body glare — on her mother, who is adjusting an invisible thread on her blouse like it’s the thread holding the whole moral fabric of the universe together.

**MOM:** (small voice)  
I’m just trying to help.

**JEN**  
I know.  Please stop now.

The room holds its breath.  Then someone quietly offers mints. Tension evaporates like steam from a hot iron.

---

## **INT. BRIDE’S ROOM – FINAL MINUTES BEFORE THE CEREMONY**

The room has gone mostly still. Final touch-ups. Lipstick checks. A gentle hush.  Jen faces the mirror. She looks like herself — not transformed, not masked. Just… elevated. Her eyes meet her mother’s in the reflection.

**JEN** (quietly, evenly)  
In forty-five minutes, I’ll be Mrs. Cremeans.

**MOM:**  
I know, sweetheart—

**JEN**  
No. Listen…I won’t be your little girl anymore.  I’ll still be your daughter. I’ll still love you.  But you’re going to have to cope with the fact that I’m not yours in the same way.

Her mother blinks. That hits.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
You raised me to be strong. To make good choices.  You should trust the version of me you built.

**MOM:** (softly, finally)  
You’re right.

Jen turns. Takes her mother’s hands.

**JEN**  
Let me go, Mom.  Let me walk out there whole.

Her mother exhales — long, shaky — and nods.  Aunt Laurel hands Jen her bouquet like it’s a baton in the longest, most complicated relay race ever run.

---

# **CHAPTER FOUR: LENNY BRUCE WASN'T AFRAID, EITHER**

---

## **INT. VESTIBULE – FINAL MOMENTS BEFORE THE CEREMONY**

The room is humming with the low, nervous energy of a courtroom before the verdict. Cremeans, hands only slightly shaking, adjusts his tie one last time. He’s already sweating. His soul is humming like a tuning fork.

And then from down the hallway comes the cry:

**GILLEY:** (O.S.)  
GROOMSMEN! ASSEMBLE!

The door swings open.  Bill enters like someone trying to pretend his socks match.  Jim is somehow holding a candle and a program and no one knows how or why.  Jeremy looks like the one person who read GQ on How to be a Groomsman and took notes.  Jeff Evans enters last. Chains now discreetly removed. Eyes steady. Suit sharp. Silent but present.

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
Nice of you to join us, Avengers.

**BILL:**  
We were outside. Praying.

**JEREMY:**  
He was trying to open a Gatorade with his teeth.

**GILLEY:**  
Which is a form of prayer.

**JIM:**  
I blacked out for a minute. Did I miss anything?

**CREMEANS**  
Just my last ten minutes as a single man. Thanks for being here, guys.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
You’re not doing this alone.

**BILL:**  
But you are doing it without beer, dancing, or escape routes.  That’s real love, my friend.

They form a loose line. Straighten ties. Wipe palms on pants.  A hush spreads.  From inside the sanctuary: the organ swells.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
She’s coming.

They all look toward the door.  Cremeans exhales.

**CREMEANS**  
Bring it!

---

## **INT. SANCTUARY – MOMENTS BEFORE JEN ENTERS**

Everyone is standing. The pastor has positioned himself. The crowd is quiet, breath held.  Cremeans is at the altar, hands clasped, trying to maintain composure while his groomsmen whisper like middle schoolers on trial.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Why does this feel like a jump scare?

**BILL:**  
You’ll see.

The organist gestures to someone in the back — a subtle nod.

And then—***BOOM.***

Mendelssohn’s “*Wedding March*”…but not as God intended!  A synth-heavy, punked-up, 148 BPM remix kicks through the church’s dusty sound system like someone jammed a Joy Division tape into a Sunday school cassette deck. The crowd blinks. One grandma gasps.  The pastor blinks slowly, internally asking the Lord to grant patience.

**CREMEANS** (blinking, stunned)  
Is that…?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Yes. Yes it is.

**GILLEY:**  
Bill. It’s Bill! This has Bill’s fingerprints all over it.

**BILL:** (grinning)  
With Jen's permission.

And then the doors swing open—**JEN** steps in. Dressed. Composed. Glowing.  The song surges behind her, distorted and divine.  And she is walking to him.  To this music. To this moment.  To the life they’re choosing — not despite the noise, but because of it. Cremeans laughs. He can’t help it. He covers his mouth, eyes welling up, because this is her. This is them.

He whispers under his breath:

**CREMEANS**  
Of course she did.

---

**PASTOR:** (soft, steady)  
Jennifer Marie Sparks…  
Do you take this man — Jeffrey Cremeans —  
to be your lawfully wedded husband,  
to have and to hold, from this day forward,  
for better, for worse, for richer, for poorer,  
in sickness and in health,  
to love and to cherish,  
as long as you both shall live?

Do you take this man?

Jen looks at Cremeans. He is standing there, rumpled but real.  No pretense. No armor.  Just a man who has fought through noise, memory, and uncertainty to end up in her line of sight — right now, right here.  She smiles — not big, not small. Just certain.

And she says:

**JEN**  
I do. And I’d do it again.

---

**PASTOR:**  
Jeffrey Lee Cremeans…

Do you take this woman — Jennifer Marie Sparks —  
to be your lawfully wedded wife,  
to have and to hold, from this day forward,  
for better, for worse, for richer, for poorer,  
in sickness and in health,  
to love and to cherish,  
as long as you both shall live?

Do you take this woman…?

---

And for a half-second, Cremeans doesn’t speak. Not because he’s uncertain — but because he is trying, and failing, to process the full force of this moment. The girl who once wrote “Felt like grace” in her journal is now standing across from him, eyes locked, breath steady, heart open. He takes a breath.  And not just a breath — a lifelong inhale.

Then he says:

**CREMEANS**  
I do. With everything I’ve got.  And everything I don’t yet know how to give.

---

**PASTOR:**  
Then, by the power vested in me by the State of Ohio…and the Lord High God —

(he smiles, lets that one land)
…I now pronounce you man and wife.

It echoes. Not loudly. Not in volume. In meaning. Every seat exhales. Someone sniffles. A child drops a juice box. Cremeans is staring like he’s seeing color for the first time.  Jen is breathing like someone who just crossed the finish line of a four-year marathon wearing lace.

The pastor continues:

**PASTOR:** (CONT’D)  
You may kiss your bride.

And that’s the moment. Not flashy. Not cinematic. Just earned. He kisses her.  It’s not rushed. Not showy. Just certain.  Two people who waited, who wanted, who knew.  Not just who they were kissing — but why.

---

# **CHAPTER FIVE: EYE OF A HURRICANE**

---

## **INT. CHURCH SANCTUARY – POST-CEREMONY – DAY**

The pastor is trying to collect his Bible.  The flower girl is eating her petals.  The best man’s boutonniere has wilted like it just heard about taxes.  And Kathy?

**KATHY:** (arms raised, joyous)  
PICTURE TIME, PICTURE TIME, PICTURE TIME, PICTURE TIME!

**CREMEANS** (whispers to Jen)  
She said it four times. We can’t stop it now.

**JEN**  
No one can.

**CHURCH LADY WITH A CLIPBOARD**  
The bride and groom will now please remain at the altar while we call up everyone who has ever known them since birth.

---

The photos begin.

- Bride and groom. Done. Easy.
- Bride and mother. Passive-aggressive shoulder squeeze.
- Groom and band. The group that tries to behave and ends up photobombing the unity candle.
- Jeff Evans, looking like he’s auditioning for Moody Mannequin Monthly, is asked to smile more naturally.
- Bill tries to flash a peace sign in every picture until someone physically lowers his arm.
- Gilley is never looking at the right camera.
- Jim, deadpan, appears exactly the same in every photo. Eyes like a haunted portrait.
- Jeremy is perfect. Of course.

**CHURCH LADY**  
Now let’s get the bride’s family…  
Now let’s get the groom’s family…  
Now let’s get “just the girls”…  
Now let’s get “just the guys”…  
Now let’s get “the one with the cousin who brought the baby”…

**KATHY:**  
Okay now one with me, the groom, the band, and Jen doing finger guns.

**JEN**  
No.

**KATHY:**  
Fair.

---

Eventually, the photos wind down.  Everyone’s cheeks hurt. Half the bouquets are fraying.   Someone is definitely holding a cup of punch in the background of a deeply serious family photo.

**CREMEANS** (whispering to Jen)  
Think we’ve earned some cake now?

**JEN**  
We’ve earned everything.

---

# **CHAPTER SIX: IT'S THE END OF THE WORLD AS WE KNOW IT**

---

## **INT. CHURCH CAFETERIA / GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – DAY**

The basketball hoops are retracted to the ceiling, but their presence is still deeply felt. The walls are beige. The tile is shinier than it has any right to be. And every folding table is dressed like someone’s aunt gave it one good hour of her time. It seats 200, and every chair is filled.  The air is a mixture of cheap flowers, deviled eggs, and air conditioning pushing its limits.

The band members are already sweating.

- Bill is eyeing the cake like it’s a test of moral endurance.
- Jeff Evans is quietly sipping iced tea and hoping no one asks him to give a speech.
- Jeremy is helping a small child fish out a piece of rogue confetti from their cup.
- Gilley has found a half-inflated balloon and is inexplicably afraid of it.
- Jim is standing next to the water cooler like it’s a confessional.
    

The food?

- Chicken. Somewhat dry but holy.
- Mac and cheese that burns the roof of your mouth like the Holy Spirit intended.
- Punch. Electric red. Probably illegal in several European countries.
- And of course — the sheet cake. White with buttercream. “<font color="#245bdb">God Bless Jeff & Jen</font>” in blue script that slants like the person writing it got tired halfway through “Bless.”

**KATHY:** (to no one, holding her punch like a martini)  
This room is a metaphor.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
How so?

**KATHY:**  
It’s holy, sticky, over-lit, and extremely humid.  Much like marriage.

Music is provided by a CD player. There is no dancing. A slideshow running on an old projector screen — showing childhood photos, most of which are blurry and suspiciously beige. At one point, Cremeans’ fourth-grade school portrait appears and Aunt Laurel audibly sobs. Jen and Cremeans make their entrance. The room erupts in applause. Not cool applause. Church applause. Rhythmless and sincere. They wave. They laugh.  They sit under a balloon arch so off-center it should be arrested.

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – MOMENTS LATER**

The reception slideshow is well underway. Some soft instrumental version of “Great Is Thy Faithfulness” is looping in the background. A few slides back was Jen at age four, grinning with a missing tooth and holding a frog.

And then—

***BOOM***.

There it is. Projected on the screen in glorious, faded, early-'90s photo paper glow: Middle school Cremeans and Jeff Evans. Awkward. Skinny.  Both wearing oversized graphic tees with something painfully era-specific on them — probably Tasmanian Devil in sunglasses or X-Wings attacking the Death Star. They’re standing in front of a middle school science fair tri-fold, haircuts deeply regrettable, arms crossed in an attempt to radiate confidence but absolutely radiating pizza rolls and undiagnosed anxiety.

The entire room erupts.

**BILL:** (loud)  
***YES. THIS IS WHAT I PAID NOTHING TO SEE.***

**KATHY:**  
Oh my God. Who let that haircut happen?

**GILLEY:**  
He had braces and a rat tail? This is a war crime.

**JIM:** (quietly)  
That’s the friendship right there.

**CREMEANS** (burying face in hands)  
Take it down. Take it down.

**JEFF EVANS:** (flat, deadpan)  
Burn the originals.

**JEN** (smiling at the screen, proud)  
I love it. You were already best friends.

**CREMEANS**  
We looked like we were auditioning for the role of “Before.”

**JEN**  
And now you’re the “After.”

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – CORNER BY THE PUNCH TABLE**

The crowd is milling. Kids are chasing napkins. Bill is monologuing to someone’s uncle about frosting-to-cake ratio.  Jen has just finished hugging a third cousin. She turns and sees Jeff Evans, momentarily alone, fidgeting with a paper plate.  She approaches calmly, punch in hand, the skirt of her dress swishing like divine fabric discipline.

**JEN**  
Hey.

**JEFF EVANS:** (smiling, soft)  
Hey. You look amazing.

**JEN**  
Thank you. You look like someone who almost didn’t get to be in the photos.

**JEFF EVANS:** (grinning)  
Yeah. That’s fair. I liked them though.

**JEN**  
So… the chains. Was that a last-minute thing? Or part of a long-term personal branding initiative?

**JEFF EVANS:** (beat, eyes drop)  
Half habit. Half armor.

**JEN**  
Armor?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
It’s…dumb. They make noise. They catch the light. People see them and make assumptions.  Which means they see that instead of everything else I’m trying to hide.

**JEN**  
You wanted to misdirect them?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Honestly?  I didn’t want to stand next to him looking like a mess.  So I figured if I looked like a different kind of mess, it’d be easier.

**JEN** (beat, kind but unblinking)  
You weren’t a mess, Jeff. You were a groomsman.  You were his best friend. And you stood there like someone who knew what that meant.

He doesn’t reply right away.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
I still brought the chains.

**JEN** (soft smile)  
And you took them off for the photos.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Because he asked.

**JEN**  
Because you listened. That’s not a mess.  That’s maturity dressed up in questionable metalwork.

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – CAKE & PUNCH TABLE**

The punch is radioactive red. It glows like it’s powered by the blood of VBS volunteers. Floating inside: a sacred and mysterious sherbet iceberg slowly melting into glory.  The cake is massive.  Rectangular.  White frosting.  Blue piping.  A tiny plastic couple on top looking like they just got stuck in traffic.

**KATHY:** (staring at the punch)  
I’ve seen this color in horror movies.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Tastes like sugar and unresolved trauma.

**BILL:** (holds cup to light)  
It’s got notes of cherry, battery acid, and…holy water?

**JEN** (approaching, bright)  
Y’all gonna drink it or declare war on it?

**BILL:**  
I’m both drinking it and declaring war.

Now: the cake moment. Cremeans and Jen stand together, plastic knife poised. The crowd gathers. Cameras come out. The church lady with the clipboard gives a discreet nod.

**CREMEANS** (quietly to Jen)  
Do we go sweet or savage?

**JEN**  
Let’s be honest. If you smear frosting on me, we will be abstinent another three to five business days.

**CREMEANS**  
Copy that. Surgical precision it is.

They slice. They feed each other politely.  Minimal crumbs. Zero smearing. The crowd claps with enormous relief.  

**BILL:** (to Jeff, mouth full of cake)  
I thought you said this place was dry.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
It is.

**BILL:**  
Then why is this cake so moist?!

---

## **INT. GYMNASIUM – DURING THE CAKE SLICE**

Jen and Cremeans feed each other the cake with dignified joy. In the second row, Aunt Teresa, the lone Catholic in the crowd and undisputed master of potato salad theology, watches with misty eyes. She raises her hand and quietly crosses herself.  A nearby Baptist woman gasps.  Someone drops a fork.  A hush falls.

**BILL:**  
Did she just—

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Yup. That’s a full rosary reset right there.

**GILLEY:**  
Do we… do we have to do something?

**JIM:**  
No. Just let it pass. Don’t make eye contact.  It’s like a liturgical deer.

---

## **INT. GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – CONTINUOUS**

Jen leans in and kisses Aunt Teresa on the cheek.  There’s a pause — soft, vulnerable. The sound of a chair scraping in the background. Someone giggling over spilled punch.

**AUNT TERESA** (quietly, eyes glossy)  
I’m sorry. I got carried away. That’s just…exactly how I feel.

Jen doesn’t flinch. Doesn’t scold. Doesn’t try to fix it.  She just smiles. And says:

**JEN**  
I know.  I know. And that’s enough. That’s everything.

They hold hands for a moment longer.  Jen stands, the train of her dress barely brushing the floor, and walks back into the room — into her new life — leaving behind a trail not of glitter or confetti, but peace.

---

# **CHAPTER SEVEN: PINING FOR THE TACO BELL NEXT DOOR**

---

## **INT. GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – LATER**

The music is down to a whisper. The crowd is starting to thin.  Kids are running laps under the balloon arch. The punch has gone flat, and nobody trusts the remaining deviled eggs.  But at one table — a round one, off to the side — they sit. Jeff Evans, Bill, Gilley, Jim, and Jeremy.  Each with a heavily frosted slice of wedding cake, because somehow they managed to get the corner pieces.

**BILL:** (low whistle)  
This is it. This is the icing.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
You can always tell. Cane sugar. Buttermilk. Not from a can.  This is grandma-tier icing.

**GILLEY:**  
My mouth is confused and grateful.

**JIM:**  
This is what love tastes like.

**JEREMY:** (quietly)  
I would commit minor crimes for this icing.

They all eat in silence for a second.  Eyes closed. Forks scraping paper plates reverently.

**BILL:**  
You think they’re gonna make it?

**JEFF EVANS:**   
Jen and Cremeans?

**BILL:**  
Yeah.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Absolutely. Anyone who serves this icing believes in joy.

**JIM:**  
And anyone who can survive this wedding without cursing or combusting is spiritually fortified.

**GILLEY:**  
I was gonna say the same thing but with more cake in my mouth. 

They clink their plastic forks like wine glasses. The lights dim slightly. Not romantically — the janitor just hit the switch by accident.

---

## **INT. GYMNASIUM – WEDDING RECEPTION – CAKE TABLE**

The guys are halfway through their second slices. Bill is attempting to make a third slice “look like a tasting sample.” Gilley is trying to remember if he’s lactose intolerant too late.

**JEFF EVANS:** (glancing around)  
Hey, uh… have you seen Kathy?

**JEREMY:** (pause, thinking)  
Yeah. I think I saw her step out with Jen. A little while ago.

**JEFF EVANS:** (slowly lowering fork)  
Wait — what?

**JEREMY:**  
They were talking. Kinda serious. Then Jen grabbed her bouquet and they just… slipped outside. I don’t know what they’re up to.

**JEFF EVANS:** (staring toward the exit)  
That's either very good… or apocalyptic.

**BILL:**  
They’re probably just comparing notes on your many personal flaws.

**GILLEY:**  
Or plotting a double elopement.

**JIM:**  
Or summoning something.

**JEFF EVANS:** (standing)  
Okay, great. Now I have to find out.

**JEREMY:**  
You’re not going out there, are you?

**JEFF EVANS:**  
They left together. Voluntarily.  That’s never happened in the known timeline of this universe.

**BILL:**  
Take your cake. If it turns into a fight, you’ll want the carbs.

---

# **CHAPTER EIGHT: LET'S TALK ABOUT SEX, TO GET THROUGH THE DAY**

---


## **## **EXT. BACK LOT – BEHIND THE CHURCH – EARLY EVENING**

The sun is lowering. The air is cooler.  There’s a concrete bench, a few cigarette butts (unholy!), and the faint smell of sheet cake trailing in the breeze.

**KATHY:** leans against the brick wall, arms crossed, trying to look casual but failing. She watches Jen adjust her dress, sit with all the dignity of a newly minted wife, and breathe deeply.

**KATHY:**  
So. You did it. You married the square.

**JEN** (smiling)  
I married the love of my life. And yes, he does file your taxes early.

**KATHY:**  
Look, I’m not here to stir anything.  I just wanted to check in.  Ask… how you’re feeling.

**JEN**  
Tired. Happy. Full of cake.

**KATHY:**  
You nervous? You know… about tonight? I mean, it’s your first time, right?

Jen slowly turns her head. Not offended. Just bemused.  She leans back slightly, expression calm, predatory even.

**JEN**  
Oh, Kathy. I’ve had this night planned for three and a half years.

**KATHY:** (blinking)  
Wait, what?

**JEN**  
I have a list.

**KATHY:**  
You—what?

**JEN**  
It’s categorized.  There are tiers, Kathy.  Some are spiritual. Some are athletic.  All of them are deeply consensual and scheduled with care and precision.

**KATHY:**  
You’re joking.

**JEN**  
Cremeans has a laminated itinerary in his suitcase.  It has bullet points. Estimated times. Recovery snacks.

**KATHY:**  
…You made a sex spreadsheet?

**JEN**  
With footnotes.

**KATHY:**  
Oh my—wait. Wait.  Are you the world’s horniest woman?

**JEN**  
I have been patient. I have been prayerful.  And now I have legal, spiritual, and emotional clearance.  You better believe I am going to stew in that marital blessing until the Lord Himself tells us to knock it off. And then we’re going to do that too.

Kathy is stunned. Speechless. Hands raised in surrender.

**KATHY:**  
I…okay.  Wow.  Okay. I came out here thinking you might be shy, maybe needed a little pep talk.

**JEN**  
What you found was a woman with a Go Bag and three kinds of flavored lube.

**KATHY:**  
You are terrifying.

**JEN**  
Thank you.

---

## **## **EXT. CHURCH LOT – MOMENTS LATER**

**KATHY:** has now fully lost control of the conversation. Her eyebrows are somewhere near orbit. Jen sits calmly, dress fanned out like a queen, flipping through a small, spiral-bound notebook like she’s announcing an apocalypse of pleasure.

**JEN**  
Would you like a preview?

**KATHY:**  
I feel like I should say no, and yet…

**JEN**  
On the third day—

**KATHY:**  (V.O)
Oh God, she’s giving it to me in chapters.

**JEN**  
On the third day, after breakfast and rehydration,  he shall bend me over the couch,  and claim me from behind, and I shall know the glory of his rod.

**KATHY:** (whispers)  
Are you possessed?

**JEN**  
Possessed by devotion. And also a very detailed understanding of pelvic angles.

**KATHY:**  
Okay. Okay, I’m gonna be honest. I didn’t see this coming.

**JEN**  
None of you did. That was the point.  You all saw the church dress.  You didn’t see the armory underneath. I have cross-references, Kathy. I have notations.

**KATHY:**  
I feel like I’m talking to a horny librarian in a Renaissance fair.

**JEN**  
I’m a homeschooler. We don’t do things halfway.

**KATHY:** (softly)  
I need a nap.

**JEN**  
I’ve scheduled one. For him.  Not me. I’ll be prepping Act Fifteen.  I've bought this swing.

---

# **CHAPTER NINE: YOUR PRECONCEPTIONS ARE INVALID**

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION TABLE – CONTINUOUS**

The gang is halfway through a second round of cake. Punch levels are dangerously low.  **KATHY:** returns to the table, moving like someone who just walked through the veil. Her hair is slightly windblown. Her eyes… changed. She sits down slowly.  Very slowly.

**JIM:** (casually)  
You look like someone who saw a ghost.

**KATHY:**  
I have seen the end of days.

**BILL:**  
You were gone for five minutes.

**KATHY:**  
Time means nothing now.

**GILLEY:**  
Did you get raptured?

**JEFF EVANS:**   
What happened?

Kathy stares at her cake. Pushes it slightly away.

**KATHY:**  
I met a woman who is hornier than I am.  Who has never had sex.  And who somehow — somehow —  has a more authentic sex life than anyone at this table combined.

**JEREMY:**  
Wait. Jen?

**KATHY:**  
Oh yes. Your blessed bride of purity?  She has diagrams, Jeremy.  Bullet points.  There was a reference to “Act Fourteen” and a quote that involved the phrase “the glory of his rod.”

**BILL:** (snorts punch through his nose)  
The what?

**KATHY:**  
Don’t make me say it again. I am already spiritually compromised.

**JIM:**  
So what you're saying is… She’s better at it than you and hasn’t even started.

**KATHY:**  
She’s orchestrating it.  We’re all out here freelancing.  She’s composing a symphony.

**GILLEY:**  
She out-hornied you?

**KATHY:**  
I am gobsmacked.  Emotionally. Theologically. Anatomically confused.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Are you… impressed?

**KATHY:**  
I don’t know what I am. But I do know one thing:

(leans in, voice low)
She’s going to destroy that man.

They all sit in stunned silence.

**JIM:** (quietly, sipping punch)  
Godspeed, Cremeans.

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – WEDDING RECEPTION – TABLE OF BAND MISFITS**

**KATHY:** finishes her apocalyptic monologue.  The table goes quiet.  Jeff Evans looks like he’s processing a lifetime of side comments in a new light.  Jeremy is just blinking, trying to remember if he packed earplugs.  Gilley is trying to imagine the phrase “glory of the rod” but can’t get a grip on it.  Jim just sips. Stoic. Eternal.

Then—  Bill snorts.

**BILL:**  
You know what?  Here’s to them.

(holds up punch)
To the Cremeans family.  May their walls hold.  May their neighbors forgive them.  And may no furniture perish in the next seventy-two hours.

**KATHY:**  
Amen.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
To their marriage.

**JIM:**  
To their stamina.

**JEREMY:**  
To their CATV not going down during scheduled recovery periods.

They all raise their cups — full of red punch and bad decisions and new beginnings.

**ALL SIX** (in joyful, horrified unison)  
To the Cremeanses! They’re gonna need it!

They clink cups, slosh punch, and howl with laughter.  Loud, unfiltered, unapologetic. Across the gym, someone’s folding chairs.  The bride is radiant. The groom is glowing.  And the band? The band is a mess. But for once, they’re a mess in sync.

---

# **CHAPTER TEN: DOES JEN HAVE BIRTHING HIPS?**

---


## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – RECEPTION – BAND TABLE – CONTINUOUS**

The laughter from the toast has just barely died down when Jim, who’s been silently demolishing his cake with existential calm, speaks.

**JIM:**  
Anybody want to bet she’s pregnant by, like, week six?

The table goes still.

**JEFF EVANS:**   
I’m not touching those odds.

**BILL:**  
That’s not a bet, man. That's a prophecy.

**GILLEY:**  
She probably already knows the baby’s name.

**JEREMY:**  
And their homeschool curriculum.

**KATHY:** (leans in, deadly serious)  
She told me… She wants three kids. Three. And they’re gonna “*get the kids out of the way early*,” her words.

**JEFF EVANS:**  
Like it's a Kroger errand.

**KATHY:**  
Tighter. Like it’s a military operation. She said, “*That way I can start homeschooling by the time the oldest turns four*.”

**BILL:**  
That’s…that’s 1998.

**GILLEY:**  
Four years from now.

**JIM:**  
A whole academic institution. Built by then.  Probably has uniforms.

**JEFF EVANS:**    
Curriculum printed on dot matrix.

**BILL:**  
She’s gonna run a classroom, a household, and probably a black-market co-op of Protestant geniuses.

**KATHY:**  
Oh, and one of them is definitely going to be named after a theologian.  Or a gemstone. Or both.

They sit in awe. No jokes now. Just respect.

**JEFF EVANS:**    
She didn’t marry Cremeans.  She enlisted him.

This is it. The final moment of quiet acknowledgment. Jen’s not starting a marriage.  She’s founding a dynasty — complete with lesson plans, fertility charts, and monogrammed lunchboxes.  And these six ragtag messes?  They raise their cups again.  Not in mockery.  In surrender.

**ALL** (quietly)  
God help him.

---

## **INT. CHURCH GYMNASIUM – BAND’S TABLE – DUSK SETTLING IN**

The night ended with tenderness, prayer, and mutual joy. Now, at approximately 6:00 a.m., they lie naked in bed, with Jeff awake, aroused, and experiencing a biological urge to initiate sex again. Their relationship dynamic is evolving — last night Jen guided and received; this morning Jeff is poised to lead. The tone for this second encounter is shaped by urgency: they are due to catch a flight out of CVG airport, just across the river in Boone County. The hotel room is quiet, sun barely rising, with a flat bottle of Mountain Dew on the nightstand and a bed that carries the warmth of their first union. What comes next is driven by spontaneity, emerging confidence, and the intimate freedom now taking shape between them.

## **INT. RENAISSANCE HOTEL – HONEYMOON SUITE – BATHROOM – 6:42 A.M.**

## **EXT. I-71 SOUTHBOUND – “THE CUT IN THE HILL” – 7:11 A.M. – DECEMBER 1994

The car creeps.

The sun is up, but barely. The freeway is a parking lot made of steel, exhaust, and broken commuter dreams. Brake lights flicker like dying Christmas lights. Cincinnati looms ahead, beautiful and smug, just past the bend—but it might as well be Narnia.

Inside the car: Cremeans drives.  Eyes forward. Jaw tight. Fingers drumming the steering wheel like he’s playing a very slow funeral march.  Jen, in the passenger seat, is radiant. Legs crossed. Hair still damp. Lip bitten—not from anxiety, but from remembering. She's the only person in this entire traffic jam glowing.

**CREMEANS** (gritted)  
I thought we’d beat rush hour.

**JEN** (softly)

Recline. Stretch. Push the button that makes the footrest bless you.
