Her eyes go wide. Her legs lift.  
She reclines 160 degrees into a full sigh.

**JEN** (whispering again)  
This is like a La-Z-Boy that got its Ph.D.

A steward places a hot towel gently in her lap like she’s royalty. Jen watches him go.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
They’re… nice here.

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
Welcome to First Class.  
Where no one gets elbowed in the kidney and your drink doesn’t arrive already open.

**JEN**  
And you’ve been doing this? For years? While I’m back home wrangling church bake sales and scraping burnt chili off CorningWare?

**CREMEANS** (carefully)  
You always said it was okay.

**JEN** (leaning close, eyes narrowed)  
It was. But now that I’ve had the good stuff?  
You better believe I’m flying coach again over my dead, blissed-out body.

**CREMEANS**  
Well… you are my wife now.  
That means elite status, pre-boarding, free food, and enough legroom to do Pilates.

**JEN** (wry)  
So this is what a six-figure Wright State BA gets you.

**CREMEANS** (modestly smug)  
With four years of guilt, yes.

She takes his hand. Leans her head on his shoulder. Her seat adjusts again—perfectly. A steward passes and offers her a second hot towel. She takes it just because she can.

**JEN** (softly, amazed)  
This isn’t a seat.  
It’s an apology for everything that ever went wrong in a waiting room.

**CREMEANS**  
Wait until they bring the warm nuts.

She grins, curls her fingers through his.

**JEN**  
You’re still not getting sleep on this flight.

**CREMEANS**  
Worth it.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF CHAMPAGNE POURING AND A MARRIED WOMAN FALLING IN LOVE WITH AIR TRAVEL FOR THE FIRST TIME AT 30,000 FEET.

  

INT. AIR TAHITI NUI – FIRST CLASS CABIN – 6:24 P.M. – DECEMBER 2, 1994

A flight attendant, serene and efficient, glides down the aisle with a tray of champagne flutes like she’s distributing small golden halos to the worthy.

She stops at Seats 2A and 2B, where Mr. and Mrs. Cremeans are seated in what can only be described as reclining spiritual favor. Jen’s curled slightly sideways, basking in the softness of it all. Cremeans has already scoped out the seat controls like they’re a new pedalboard.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT (pleasantly)  
Would you care for some champagne before takeoff?

Cremeans raises a hand gently, but firmly.

**CREMEANS**  
No, thank you. We’re Baptists.

Jen nods, echoing the sentiment with a polite smile.

**JEN**  
Dry Baptists, not… social Baptists.  
If that makes sense.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT (smiling, unphased)  
Of course. What may I bring you instead?

Cremeans leans forward just slightly—this is his moment.

**CREMEANS**  
What carbonated drinks do you have on offer?

The flight attendant does not flinch. She has clearly handled both chaos and vegetarians on long-haul flights.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT  
Let me see… we have Coca-Cola, Diet Coke, Sprite, Schweppes tonic, ginger ale, Perrier, and… Tahitian vanilla soda.

Cremeans blinks. Jen arches a brow.

**CREMEANS**  
Perrier’s just church water with bubbles.

**JEN** (to attendant)  
Do you have Mountain Dew?

FLIGHT ATTENDANT (soft chuckle)  
No Dew, I’m afraid.

Cremeans nods, solemn.

**CREMEANS**  
That’s okay. We’ve already communed.

**JEN** (whispering to him)  
We brought a bottle in the backpack.

**CREMEANS** (back to attendant)  
We’ll take the ginger ale. On ice. Two. Tall as it comes.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT  
Of course. Would you like a lime wedge?

**CREMEANS**  
Ma’am, we’re flying across the planet in pajamas.  
Yes, I’d like a lime wedge.

Jen stifles a laugh.

The attendant nods and glides off.

**JEN** (quietly)  
It’s official. We’ve become fancy Baptists.

**CREMEANS**  
It’s not fancy. It’s… carbonated stewardship.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF ICE CLINKING IN GLASSES AND A MARRIAGE THAT HONORS GOD, EACH OTHER, AND THE RIGHT TO DECLINE BOOZE WITH EXTREME POLITENESS.

  

INT. AIR TAHITI NUI – FIRST CLASS CABIN – 6:36 P.M. – DECEMBER 2, 1994  
(Taxiing now. The lights dim. The hum of engines rising.)

Jen grips the armrest—not from fear, just pure, awe-struck wonder. Her ginger ale sits untouched, lime slowly sinking. Her eyes are wide, her posture alert, her whole being tuned to the miracle of scale she’s currently seated inside.

Cremeans glances at her from his reclined cloud-throne. Smirks softly. This is his third 747 this month—but for her? This is a revelation with wings.

**JEN** (stunned)  
I knew it would be big.  
But I didn’t think it’d be… a cathedral.

She cranes her neck back, peering down the impossibly long aisle stretching through business, premium economy, and into the distant land of coach, where knees go to die and snacks are theoretical.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
This thing’s like… a shopping mall with jet engines.  
You could host a revival in here.

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
Boeing 747.  
They call it the “Queen of the Skies.”  
Carries over four hundred people.  
Two decks. Four engines.  
She’s not just a plane. She’s a floating county fair.

Jen whistles low.

**JEN**  
I once flew from John Glenn to Reagan in a plane so small the flight attendant had to squat sideways to serve peanuts.  
This? This is Noah’s Ark for Methodists.

**CREMEANS**  
Yeah. The puddle jumpers are more like faith-based lawnmowers with wings.

**JEN**  
This is like… air luxury.  
Like the Titanic, but hopefully without the drowning.

**CREMEANS** (deadpan)  
We don’t say “Titanic” on a plane, babe. That’s like yelling “freebird” at a funeral.

Jen smirks. Leans back in her seat again, stretching out, her socked feet just barely brushing the padded footrest.

**JEN** (softly)  
It’s humbling.  
All these people. All these bodies.  
And we’re flying.

She looks around the cabin—children fidgeting, older couples smiling, young honeymooners not as in love as she feels right now. Everyone in their little pod of anticipation and exhaustion.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
God made metal float.  
How wild is that?

**CREMEANS**  
He made it lift.

He leans over. Kisses her forehead.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
We’re not defying gravity.  
We’re living in its loopholes.

The plane begins its roll toward takeoff.

Jen grips his hand. Not out of fear. Just connection.

**JEN**  
I trust you.  
And I trust this… monster air chapel.

**CREMEANS**  
Amen.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF ENGINES ROARING AND A WOMAN DISCOVERING THAT FLIGHT IS LESS ABOUT SCIENCE AND MORE ABOUT FAITH WITH A TURBINE.

  

INT. AIR TAHITI NUI – FIRST CLASS CABIN – 8:07 P.M. – HIGH ABOVE THE PACIFIC

The cabin lights are dimmed. Outside, the stars are scattered across the sky like spilled sugar. Inside, it’s quieter now. A cocoon of whispers, movie glow, and the soft clinking of cutlery in tiny porcelain dishes.

Dinner service begins. A flight attendant approaches Jen and Cremeans with a professionally strained smile—the kind only 11 hours in a metal tube can shape.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT  
For your dinner selection tonight, we have two options:

Option one is a pan-seared mahi-mahi with ginger-lime coconut foam, passionfruit reduction, and taro root purée.

Option two is a mushroom risotto with black garlic drizzle, grilled endives, and sweet onion confit.

Jen pauses.  
Looks up.  
Blinks.

She glances at Cremeans.  
He’s already making a face that says “I tried to warn you.”

**JEN** (softly)  
…Foam?

**CREMEANS**  
Not the kind you put on a latte. The kind that makes you miss ketchup.

**JEN** (politely, to the attendant)  
We’ll both have the risotto, please.

FLIGHT ATTENDANT  
Excellent choice.

She disappears with the speed of a trained escape artist.

**JEN** (under her breath)  
Where’s the third option? Like, I don’t know… “hamburger”?

**CREMEANS**  
That was the Fatburger. That was the final meal of clarity.

Jen eyes the table setup. Cloth napkin. Real silverware. A bread roll that feels like it was baked out of compromise. The tray table hisses into place with the weight of responsibility.

**JEN**  
I just don’t think I’m spiritually prepared to eat anything with a “drizzle.”  
Or “confit.”  
Or endives.  
What even are endives?

**CREMEANS** (knowingly)  
They taste like guilt and leaves.

Their dinner arrives. Small, polite portions. Garnished with twigs and aspirations.

Jen pokes the risotto. It glistens like it’s been baptized in abstract art. She takes a bite. Pauses.

**JEN** (stiffly)  
Mm. Very… earthy.

**CREMEANS** (deadpan)  
Translation: like mushroom paste on a sponge.

She forces a few more bites.

**JEN**  
This is why I married you.  
For the foresight.  
The Fatburger foresight.

**CREMEANS**  
Blessed are the husbands who know their wives will need meat and salt before boarding a French flight.

She nods solemnly. Takes a bite of the endive.  
Immediately regrets it.

**JEN**  
Nope. Nope. That tastes like regret salad.

**CREMEANS**  
Just hang on. Breakfast is in eleven hours and usually involves croissants and judgment.

**JEN**  
Eleven hours…

She leans back in her seat, patting her belly like she’s survived something.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
Next honeymoon? You pack Slim Jims in your carry-on.

**CREMEANS** (smiling)  
Already did.  
Back pocket of my jeans. Emergency meat stick.

She stares at him.  
In awe.  
Again.

**JEN**  
God, I love you.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF RISOTTO REGRET, SPOUSAL WISDOM, AND THE MUTED RUMBLE OF A JET FERRYING TWO WELL-FED BAPTISTS INTO THE MOONLIT UNKNOWN.

INT. AIR TAHITI NUI – FIRST CLASS CABIN – SOMEWHERE OVER THE PACIFIC – THE UNGODLY HOURS  
(Approximately 2:47 A.M. Body Time / 8:47 P.M. Tahiti Time / All Hope Lost Time)

Outside the window, it’s pitch black.  
No stars. No moon. Just void.  
An inky, silent stretch of sky above an even more inky, silent stretch of ocean.

Inside the cabin? Dim, drowsy tranquility.  
Overhead lights off. Reading lights flickering like the final gasps of people trying to finish John Grisham before their Ambien kicks in.

Jen sits bundled under her blanket, flipping through the in-flight magazine like it’s a sacred scroll of overpriced Tahitian excursions.

Cremeans looks at his watch. Then the little digital screen on his seat console. Then the tiny bag labeled “COMFORT KIT” on his lap.

**CREMEANS** (softly)  
Alright.  
We’ve crossed into the “middle of nowhere.”  
Time for pajamas.

**JEN** (groggy)  
It’s not bedtime.  
It’s eternity.  
We left time zones an hour ago and entered the Book of Ecclesiastes.

**CREMEANS** (holding up his kit)  
It’s in the rules.  
You eat a meal you didn’t enjoy, you watch fifteen minutes of a movie you didn’t understand, and then you change into state-issued pajamas like you’re in a luxury cult.

**JEN** (suspicious)  
They gave us pajamas?

He opens the kit. Inside:

- Soft, navy blue pajama set
    
- Eye mask
    
- Slippers
    
- A pair of socks with grippy bottoms that look like they were designed by a Swedish minimalist with a foot fetish
    

Jen holds up the pajama top.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
This feels… unreasonably comfortable.  
Why does it smell like lavender and budget?

**CREMEANS**  
Because it’s made from a blend of cotton, polyester, and absolution.

**JEN** (snorting)  
Are we really changing clothes on an airplane?

**CREMEANS**  
Yes. In the bathroom. Like civilized sinners.

---

INT. AIRPLANE LAVATORY – MOMENTS LATER

Jen changes in the absurdly small space, elbows knocking into walls, one sock flung onto the sink, hair doing its best to exist in three time zones.

She catches her reflection in the mirror.

**JEN** (to herself)  
Married.  
Flying over the Pacific.  
Wearing government-issued pajamas.  
Living the dream.

She smirks, opens the door.

---

INT. FIRST CLASS CABIN – RETURN TO SEATS

Cremeans is already changed. Pajama shirt buttoned. Hair mussed from trying to do anything in an airplane bathroom. He’s slipping his wedding ring back on with care, like it’s armor.

Jen returns. Sits. Sighs. Pulls her blanket up to her chin.

**JEN** (settling in)  
You know what?

**CREMEANS**  
Hmm?

**JEN**  
We look like two adults who made excellent life choices.

**CREMEANS**  
We look like cult members waiting for the spaceship.

**JEN** (softly)  
Same thing.

They clink their plastic water cups like monks in a monastery designed by Boeing.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF JET ENGINES, SOFT BREATHING, AND TWO PEOPLE WHO JUST PUT ON MATCHING PAJAMAS TO SLEEP SOMEWHERE ABOVE OBLIVION.

  

INT. AIR TAHITI NUI – FIRST CLASS CABIN – SOMEWHERE BETWEEN TIME AND TAHITI – CRUISING ALTITUDE

The cabin is nearly silent now. A few seatbelt signs flicker. The occasional shuffle of a weary flight attendant moving like a ghost. Most passengers have succumbed to sleep, their little pods cocooned in darkness and half-hope.

Cremeans is settling in, pillow fluffed just right, eye mask perched on his forehead like a Baptist ninja preparing for spiritual REM. He's just about to drift off, body heavy, soul calm, when—

Jen, curled next to him under her blanket, leans close.

Closer.

Closer still.

So close her lips barely brush his ear.

**JEN** (whispers)  
I spent a hundred bucks on my honeymoon lingerie set.

Cremeans doesn’t move.  
Doesn’t breathe.

He blinks once.  
Twice.  
Stares into the darkness in front of him like it just got louder.

**JEN** (CONT’D, softer now, wickedly gentle)  
Try sleeping now, big boy.

Cremeans inhales sharply, like someone just hit him with a verse from Song of Solomon they don’t let you read in youth group.

**CREMEANS** (hoarse whisper)  
You’re weaponizing intimacy.

**JEN** (innocently)  
No. I’m just disclosing financial information. You love that.

He turns to face her, squinting in the dim light, eyes wide, jaw slack.

**CREMEANS** (muted panic)  
Is it… under the pajamas?

**JEN** (smirking)  
Wouldn’t you like to know?

He groans quietly. Shifts. Adjusts the blanket over his lap with very intentional care.

**CREMEANS** (strained)  
We’re at thirty-five thousand feet.  
I have no exits.  
No privacy.  
No recourse.

**JEN**  
You have imagination. And a strong marriage.

She kisses his cheek.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
See you in Tahiti, husband.

And with that—she closes her eyes like nothing happened.

Cremeans lies there, wide awake, now intimately aware of both his love for her and the grueling distance to a private hotel room.

**CREMEANS** (muttering to himself)  
The Lord is testing me.  
And her.  
But mostly me.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF JET ENGINES, A MAN SWEATING IN SILENCE, AND A WOMAN WHO KNEW EXACTLY WHAT SHE WAS DOING.

  

INT. **CREMEANS**’ DREAM – SOMEWHERE BETWEEN TROPICAL BLISS AND SINFUL GRACE – NONSENSICAL DREAM O'CLOCK

The waves crash in slow motion. The sky is absurdly blue, like it’s been painted in Photoshop by a sentimental weatherman. Palm trees sway like they’re sighing. Seagulls cry out somewhere off-screen like unpaid voice actors in a 90s Christian beach movie.

And there, on the sand, illuminated by divine sunlight and pure marital right, is Jen.

Topless.

Yes, topless.

TOP.  
LESS.

She’s laughing. Running. Romping.  
Romping in a theological sense, of course.  
Romping like Eve on vacation, but with better sunscreen and legally binding paperwork.

**CREMEANS** (in dream voiceover)  
Oh, yeah.  
This is it.  
This is the dream.

He chases after her, slow-motion bouncing across the beach like an emotionally fulfilled gazelle. Her laughter is like windchimes and whispered Bible verses. Her bikini bottom clings on bravely, but Cremeans starts to wonder…

**CREMEANS** (V.O.)  
Wait a second.  
Am I lucid dreaming?

He pauses.  
Looks down at his hands.  
Then back at Jen, who’s now splashing in the surf like a righteous nymph of wifely affection.

**CREMEANS** (V.O.)  
Can I dream her bikini brief off?

He concentrates.  
Squints.  
Points with his mind like Moses at the Red Sea.

And just as the fabric begins to—DING.

ANNOUNCEMENT (tinny, very real)  
Ladies and gentlemen, we are beginning our descent into Papeete…

Cremeans bolts awake.

The blanket is twisted. His eye mask is halfway up his forehead. His heart is pounding with the violent injustice of untimely awakenings.

**CREMEANS** (groggy, furious whisper)  
No.  
NO.  
I was so close.  
I had powers.

Jen, beside him, still groggy, peeks an eye open.

**JEN** (murmuring)  
Hmm?

**CREMEANS**  
Nothing.  
Just… international betrayal.

She closes her eyes again, unaware that she starred in the most sacred dream a man has ever had at altitude.

**CREMEANS** (quietly)  
We’re gonna need to find a beach.  
Immediately.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF LANDING GEAR, UNFINISHED FANTASIES, AND A HUSBAND WHO KNOWS HE'S ENTERING TAHITI WITH A PURPOSE.

  

INT. FIRST CLASS CABIN – FINAL APPROACH – 8:59 P.M. TAHITI TIME  
(Cabin lights up. Shade open. The ocean glows moonlit and mocking below.)

Cremeans is still staring blankly ahead, eyes glassy, emotionally destroyed by the cruel divine timing of a flight attendant’s descent announcement interrupting what may have been the apex of marital fantasy logic.

Jen’s now sitting up, brushing hair out of her eyes, stretching like a cat who slept on clouds. She yawns, sips what’s left of her water, and glances over at her husband—who is clearly mourning something spiritual.

She tilts her head, smiles faintly.

**JEN** (softly, with sleepy curiosity)  
But why, lover?

He turns to her. Slowly. Like a man coming back from war. Or a particularly vivid Song of Solomon-adjacent REM cycle.

**CREMEANS** (hoarse, reverent)  
Because I was dreaming…  
You were topless.  
On the beach.  
We were romping.  
Biblically.

**JEN** (already grinning)  
Oh?

**CREMEANS**  
I had control.  
I was trying to… dream your bikini off. With thought.

**JEN** (laughs, scandalized)  
Jeffrey Lee Cremeans!

**CREMEANS** (still stunned)  
And just as the string started to untie…  
The intercom dinged.  
Like the Holy Spirit saying, “Nice try, but not yet, buddy.”

Jen bursts out laughing. Covers her face with her blanket.

**JEN**  
That’s what you were muttering about?  
Dream undressing me like some kind of subconscious magician?

**CREMEANS**  
It was almost real.  
It was sacred.  
It was mine.

**JEN** (still giggling)  
I’ll make you a deal.

**CREMEANS** (instantly alert)  
Yes?

**JEN**  
We get to the hotel.  
You don’t complain about jet lag.  
You don’t fall asleep in the car.  
You get me checked in, showered, and horizontal—and I’ll let you pick which bathing suit I lose first.

**CREMEANS** (sincerely, emotionally)  
You are… the most anointed woman alive.

**JEN** (grinning)  
You’re such a dork.  
But you’re my dork.  
Now put your shoes back on, Romeo. We’ve got paradise to go bless.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF A MAN WHO LOST A DREAM… BUT GAINED A MISSION.  
AND A WOMAN WHO KNOWS SHE'S THE PLOT, THE TWIST, AND THE SEQUEL.

  

## **EXT. TAHITI – AIRPORT EXIT ROAD – 9:43 P.M. – MOONLIT AND MIRACULOUSLY CLEAR

The wheels of the shuttle van (which, let’s be honest, is really a black luxury SUV with chilled towels in the cupholders) roll smoothly along the coast, the windows down, the Pacific whispering hello.

Jen leans her forehead against the glass, watching palm trees go by like shadows from a dream she’ll get to finish in real life.

Cremeans, beside her, is visibly smug.  
Quietly smug.  
The kind of smug only a man who has:

1. Written off international romance as a business expense,
    
2. Booked a suite priced like it comes with its own private deity, and
    
3. Gotten away with it…
    

…can carry without needing to brag.

**JEN** (softly)  
I expected traffic.

**CREMEANS** (shrugging)  
God parted the roads.  
For us.  
And also, it’s Tuesday.

She turns to look at him.

**JEN**  
How much did this place cost?

Cremeans exhales slowly. Watches the lights of their destination appear around the curve.

**CREMEANS**  
Let’s just say… if the IRS audits me, I’ll be describing this trip as an “executive strategy retreat.”

**JEN** (snorts)  
We’re retreating all right.  
Right into a five-star bed with God-tier thread count.

He doesn’t deny it.

**CREMEANS**  
And I had to pick the best.  
For branding.  
And marketing optics.  
And because… you deserve to remove your underwear in a room that costs more per night than my first car.

She goes silent. Turns back to the window. Smiles like someone whose whole spirit just got kissed.

**JEN** (quietly)  
You’re laying the charm on thick.

**CREMEANS** (leans in, voice low)  
And soon I’ll be laying something else on you.



Preferably after you step onto our private infinity deck in a robe made of fabric angels are jealous of.

**JEN** (still facing the window, deadpan)  
You think you’re getting a write-off for that line?

**CREMEANS**  
Only if you moan loud enough to count it as a marketing demo.

She bites her lip. Laughs.

The van turns into the long, winding driveway of a resort that looks less like a hotel and more like a Bond villain’s vacation lair, carved into the cliffs and glowing like it’s powered by generational wealth and coconut-scented magic.

**JEN** (quietly, in awe)  
You really booked this?

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
Top shelf, babe.  
Just like Fatburger.  
But with fewer pickles and more missionary.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF TIRES ON COBBLESTONE, WAVES KISSING SHORE, AND ONE MARRIED COUPLE ABOUT TO FILE JOINTLY UNDER “DELIRIOUSLY BLESSED.”

---

## **INT. OVERWATER BUNGALOW – TAHITI – 10:22 P.M.**  
(The door closes behind them with the hush of soft wood and softer intentions.)

The air smells like hibiscus and unsupervised sin.  
The moon spills through gauzy curtains.  
Waves lap gently under the bungalow like they’re applauding what’s about to happen. The bed looks like it was designed by a team of scandalized angels and orthopedic experts.

Jen is already barefoot, already stretching like she’s about to run drills.  
Cremeans sets his backpack down like a man about to be drafted into sacred battle.

**JEN** (turning to him, hands on hips)  
So.  
We’ve checked in.  
You’ve fulfilled your travel husband duties with excessive excellence.

**CREMEANS** (wry)  
Thank you. I try to be a five-star Sherpa of seduction.

She raises a brow. Steps closer.  
Pulls a folded piece of paper from her carry-on like it’s the Dead Sea Scrolls of Lust.

**JEN**  
I brought inventory.

**CREMEANS** (frowning gently)  
Like… for clothes?

She unfolds it.  
Sixteen items.  
Each one numbered.  
Some circled.  
Some annotated.  
There are stars. There are underlines. There are very confident verbs.

**JEN** (matter-of-fact)  
This is the honeymoon agenda.  
We’ve done the first two.

She taps the paper.

**JEN** (CONT’D)

1. Defloration.
    
2. Mutual first orgasm, penetrative.  
    (With a note: “Success! Training wheels. :)”)
    

**CREMEANS** (blinking, dryly)  
There are training wheels on our consummation?

**JEN**  
Yes. Because I didn’t deploy anything from column three. Yet.

She folds her arms. He stares at the list. Eyes scan ahead. Stops on things like:

- #7 – Suspended trust exercise
    
- #11 – Outdoor interlude, bug spray permitting
    
- #13 – “He calls me Ma’am”
    
- #16 – The Lord’s Day Finale
    

He looks up at her like she’s become someone new, or rather, like she’s finally revealing who she’s always been.  
His voice drops. Almost reverent.

**CREMEANS**  
You… hid this.

**JEN** (deadpan)  
I cloaked it.  
There’s a difference.

**CREMEANS** (quietly, awestruck)  
You might be the horniest person I’ve ever met.

**JEN** (smiling, proud)  
And yet I waited.

**CREMEANS**  
Three years.  
No hints. No slips. No… throat-clearing moans after Sunday school.

**JEN**  
I was patient.  Because you were worth it.

Beat.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
But now?  There are no rules but mine.  And my list.  And that bed.  And possibly that balcony chair depending on structural stability.

Cremeans just nods, slowly.  The kind of nod that says “My life just changed. Again. But this time I’m going to need electrolytes.”

**CREMEANS**  
Do I need a safe word?

**JEN** (already walking toward the bedroom)  
Yes. It’s “stop being such a coward.”

She disappears behind the curtain.  The list flutters slightly in the ocean breeze.  Cremeans picks it up.  Reads entry #9.

**CREMEANS** (V.O., reading quietly)  
“#9 – Honey on collarbone, removed orally, preferably after prayer.”

He exhales. Long. Slow. Grateful.  
And slightly terrified.

---

**## **EXT. OVERWATER BUNGALOW – INFINITY DECK – 10:39 P.M. – TAHITI**

The stars are out in full defiance of modesty.  The ocean is glass. The sky, velvet.  And the infinity deck glows faintly under tiki torchlight like a stage set for an extremely well-cast marital awakening.

Cremeans is barefoot, shirtless, and holding a beach towel like it’s going to help him survive the next six hours.

He’s standing in the doorway, list in one hand, soul in the other, calling out to the night.

**CREMEANS** (calling out, eyes wild with honeymoon zeal)  
Hey, Jen!  Get back here!  I gotta take your panties off on the beach!

There’s a moment of silence.  Then Jen’s voice floats back—not from the sand, but from somewhere just out of sight… closer.

**JEN** (offscreen, playful)  
The beach?  Tonight?

**CREMEANS**  
It’s on the list. #5. “Removed on beach, ceremonially, with reverence.”

**JEN** (appearing slowly onto the deck, wrapped in one of those silk robes the hotel provides that’s 0% helpful and 100% provocative)  
We’re forty feet above the beach.  The sand is downstairs.  Your legs are already jelly from row 2A.

She steps closer. The robe slips a little off her shoulder, probably accidentally on purpose.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
You want the beach?

**CREMEANS** (breathless)  
I want the beach.  I want the ceremony.  I want… whatever you wrote down under #14 that you labeled “pending weather conditions.”

She walks right up to him, reaches out, places a hand on his chest.

**JEN** (softly)  
Then the deck will have to suffice for tonight.

She slips out of the robe.  It falls like a curtain dropping at the start of an explicit Broadway revival.  She is barefoot, breathtaking, and—yes—still wearing those panties.  For now.

Cremeans goes absolutely still. Swallows. Hard.

**CREMEANS**  
The deck is good.  The deck is very good.

**JEN**  
Biblical good?

**CREMEANS**  
Genesis 1:31 good.

He steps toward her, list fluttering forgotten to the floor. His hands already reaching, reverent, ready.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF WATER LAPPING GENTLY BENEATH THE FLOORBOARDS,  
SOMEWHERE BETWEEN THE BEACH AND HEAVEN,  WHERE A HUSBAND IS ABOUT TO FULFILL HIS VOCATIONAL CALLING WITH BOTH HANDS.

---

**## **EXT. INFINITY DECK – POST-COITAL BLISS – 11:17 P.M. – TAHITI**  
(Warm air. Cool skin. Nothing but moonlight, exhaustion, and victory.)

Cremeans is flat on his back on the deck, completely spent, face turned to the stars, chest still heaving from what can only be described as a marital sacrament conducted at high altitude and full velocity.

His hair is a mess.  His soul is clean.  And the smile on his face?  Somewhere between spiritually reborn and narratively fulfilled.

Jen, lying beside him, is draped over a throw blanket, looking like a sun-drenched Roman goddess, smug and sleepy. She’s twirling his wedding ring on her pinky like it’s a decoder ring that just unlocked the secrets of the universe.

Then, softly at first—like a man who’s seen glory and wants to thank the heavens with the only cultural reference his mind can conjure—Cremeans starts to sing.

**CREMEANS** (blissfully)  
I’m turning Japanese / I think I’m turning Japanese / I really think so…

Jen opens one eye. Stares at him.

**CREMEANS** (still going, arms outstretched)  
Turning Japanese / I think I’m turning Japanese / I really think so—

She smacks his chest, not hard, just enough.

**JEN** (groggy, amused)  
Jeffrey Lee! What… in God’s name… are you doing?

**CREMEANS** (radiant, breathless)  
Celebrating!  
This is what it feels like when you hit a walk-off grand slam in Game 6 of the World Series.  
In slow motion.  
While naked.  
In paradise.

**JEN** (dryly)  
Is that what we just did?

**CREMEANS** (reverently)  
Babe… you are the World Series.  And I just won you.

He starts humming the tune again, completely unironically. Jen groans, flops an arm over her eyes.

**JEN**  
If you sing that at breakfast, I’m telling the concierge you have an inner ear infection and should be quarantined.

**CREMEANS** (laughing)  
Too late. I'm culturally possessed. I’m levitating.  I am anointed.  I am a man reborn in sweat and Japanese synthpop.

**JEN** (smirking)  
You’re a dork with a tan line in the shape of my thighs.

**CREMEANS** (still beaming)  
Turning Japanese…  
I really think so…

Jen sighs. Leans over and kisses his temple.

**JEN** (softly)  
Next time you sing that, you're wearing the kimono and fetching room service.

**CREMEANS**  
Deal.  As long as you’re not wearing anything at all.

---

## **INT. OVERWATER BUNGALOW – BEDROOM – 12:08 A.M. – TAHITI**

They’ve finally made it inside.

The bed is enormous, the sheets are tangled, the air conditioner hums like a lullaby for sinners. Jen lies on her stomach, body bare except for a silky hotel throw lazily draped across her hips. Her hair is a halo of satisfied chaos on the pillow.

Cremeans is sitting up, still buzzed on post-glory adrenaline and one of the most successful nights of his entire existence.  He’s holding his glass of ice water like it’s a trophy.

**CREMEANS** (marveling)  
I’m still reeling from the fact that you tan nude.

**JEN** (muffled into the pillow)  
Why would I cover my finest features?

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
You’re walking around this resort like it’s the Garden of Eden, and I’ve been over here paying taxes and wearing cargo shorts.

She chuckles. Shifts her legs.

**JEN**  
We’re on an island. The sun’s free. The tan lines are not.

**CREMEANS** (decisively)  
Okay. After a solid night’s sleep—real sleep, not interrupted-by-my-own-moan sleep—we get brunch, then we find a spot… and I’m joining you.

**JEN** (lifting her head, eyebrow raised)  
You? Naked?  Outdoors?

**CREMEANS** (resolute)  
Full commitment. Sun’s out, buns out.  But no indecency. We’ll find a tastefully remote cove or… sanctified bush.

**JEN** (laughing)  
Babe, your whole body is Ohio-pale. You’re gonna sizzle like a cheap steak.

**CREMEANS** (smirking)  
Not if you put lotion on me.  All over.

She rolls onto her side, propped up on one elbow, grinning like a woman about to do something that’ll either end in romance or an embarrassing trip to a Tahitian pharmacy.

**JEN**  
You want me to rub sunscreen on every inch of that accountant-grade body?

**CREMEANS**  
It’s a marital responsibility.  I read that in Ephesians.  Somewhere in the fine print.

**JEN**  
You’re gonna get weird tan lines on your toes.

**CREMEANS**  
Then you better even them out. Artistically.

She laughs. Tosses a pillow at him. He catches it—barely. Smirks.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Tomorrow, I bare my soul.  And my entire ass.

**JEN** (softly)  
I can’t wait.  But I’m bringing aloe.  And maybe a camera.

---

## **INT. LUXURY RESORT – BRUNCH BUFFET – 10:21 A.M. – TAHITI (NEXT MORNING)** 

(The sun is up. The air is warm. And the resort buffet is humming with that quiet, genteel tension found only in high-end vacation dining where no one knows what half the words mean.)

Cremeans and Jen, sun-kissed and smug with secrets, stroll into the restaurant like a pair of dignitaries from the nation of Marital Bliss.

The buffet is massive.  An architectural tribute to fusion confusion.  Towering pyramids of papaya, pineapple, and coconut jam.  Tongs next to items that look like tropical sea creatures wearing pastry hats.  Tiny bowls of fermented things. A fish station that smells suspiciously assertive for 10 a.m.

And somewhere in the middle? A corner labeled “Continental Comforts” like a safe zone for folks who whispered “Do y’all have regular bacon?”

**CREMEANS** (under his breath)  
This is like a food museum curated by someone who’s never met a Midwesterner.

**JEN** (eyebrows raised at a quiche topped with edible flowers)  
I’m not eating anything with petals before noon.

A server approaches, smiling with practiced grace.

**SERVER** (French accent)  
Bonjour. Would you like to sit inside or on the terrace?

**JEN**  
Terrace, please. We’re practicing for a scandalous afternoon.

The server blinks. Nods slowly. Leads them to a shaded spot with ocean views so intense they should come with a disclaimer.

## **INT. BUFFET LINE – MOMENTS LATER**

Cremeans eyes the offerings cautiously. He settles into the American quadrant with the quiet shame of a man who traveled thousands of miles for toast and scrambled eggs.

He loads his plate with:

- One cautious croissant
- Something that claims to be bacon
- A scoop of what looks like fancy hash browns but might actually be a taro situation
    
- And two pancakes that look like they were printed by a 3D sugar robot
    

Jen? She’s going rogue.  One half of her plate is filled with exotic attempts at adulthood: dragonfruit, smoked marlin tartare, and what might be passionfruit yogurt.  The other half is pure Ohio comfort: cheese cubes and a slice of banana bread she guarded like a hawk at the buffet line.

**JEN** (seated now, sipping hotel-grade coffee)  
You know, the French-Tahitian menu’s not really built for church potluck people.

**CREMEANS**  
We are absolutely the potluck people.

**JEN**  
But we’re doing our best.  Out here with our charcuterie courage and intercontinental heartburn.

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
They may not understand what “covered dish” means here, but they understand Benjamins.  And I gave them a whole lot of Benjamins.

**JEN** (musing)  
Yeah. Money talks.

**CREMEANS** (nodding, solemn)  
And in this hotel, it talks in pancakes and pineapple that’s already been sliced for you.

They toast their mimosas—ginger ale, obviously—and dig in. The food is tolerable. The view is priceless. And the real menu is still waiting for them back on the infinity deck.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF FANCY utensils scraping humble food,  AND A COUPLE WHO CAME FOR LOVE, BUT STAYED FOR THE BANANA BREAD.

---

## **INT. OVERWATER BUNGALOW – NOONISH – TAHITI – THE SUN IS RUDELY PERFECT**

Jen is on the terrace reapplying sunscreen with the focus of a woman who knows how quickly alabaster becomes lobster in this part of the world. She’s in a bikini top that doesn’t even pretend to hide intention, a gauzy wrap around her hips, and a posture that says "I am a weapon and the ocean is my stage."

Inside, Cremeans hangs up the phone, his wallet $120 lighter than necessary, his expression smug in that just-paid-too-much-on-purpose way.

**JEN** (calling out)  
Did you really just pay three times the going rate for a rental car?

**CREMEANS** (walking onto the deck, towel over one shoulder, very pleased with himself)  
Absolutely.  
And I’d do it again.

**JEN** (suspicious)  
Why?  Was it gold-plated? Did it come with its own saxophone player?

**CREMEANS**  
Nope.  I had the majordomo do it.

Jen raises an eyebrow. This is the third time today he’s used the word majordomo, and she’s starting to think he might not entirely know what it means.

**JEN**  
You mean… the concierge?

**CREMEANS**  
No. This guy’s more than concierge. He’s… a facilitator of destiny.

He steps up beside her, wraps an arm around her waist, and drops his voice like he’s about to narrate a high-budget miniseries on marital power dynamics.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
I overpaid on purpose. Strategically.

**JEN** (dry)  
You bribed him with vibes?

**CREMEANS**  
No. I created loyalty.  Now? Every time we need something—restaurant, boat, reservation, non-papaya room service—they’re going to bust their well-moisturized butts to make us happy.

**JEN** (squinting at him)  
That’s… wildly manipulative.  And kind of hot.

**CREMEANS** (smirking)  
Also, let’s not pretend.  I want to take you down the coast, find a secluded beach, and watch you unleash those dainty miracles under the kind of sun that makes angels weep.

**JEN** (mock-offended)  
“Dainty miracles”?  You make them sound like limited edition Christmas ornaments.

**CREMEANS** (solemn)  
They’re limited to me.  And baby, I want to worship in nature.

Jen sighs like she’s exasperated but also deeply into it. She picks up her sunglasses and slides them on with flair.

**JEN**  
Fine.  But I’m picking the radio station in the rental car.

**CREMEANS** (nodding)  
Deal.  But if they offer a CD player, I’m putting on Steve Winwood.

**JEN**  
Then I’m staying topless the whole drive to keep you from singing.

He freezes.  
Then slowly, reverently lowers his sunglasses.

**CREMEANS** (quietly, awestruck)  
God bless the overcharge.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF KEYS BEING DELIVERED,  SUNSCREEN BEING APPLIED,  
AND STRATEGIC TIPPING PAYING OFF IN SACRED EXPOSURE.

---

**## **EXT. TAHITIAN COASTLINE – RENTAL CAR – 1:07 P.M. – ROAD TRIP MODE INITIATED**

The rental car is a slightly beat-up Peugeot 405, vaguely beige, humming along a coastal road that looks like it was designed by a dream sequence and painted by someone who wanted to hurt your feelings with beauty. The windows are down. The air is warm. The sea glitters like it knows secrets.

Jen sits shotgun, sunglasses on, sarong tied loosely, her bikini top already a distant memory. A small towel is draped over her chest for modesty, or possibly for suspense.

Cremeans?  Behind the wheel, grinning like he just got handed the keys to heaven’s summer camp.

With the flare of a man who’s waited his entire adult life to have both love and decent stereo access, he pulls out a CD from his backpack—clearly labeled "ROAD GOD 1" in all caps—and inserts it into the dash.

The music kicks in, clear and rich and epically unironic:

🎶 Think about it, there must be higher love  
Down in the heart or hidden in the stars above… 🎶

Cremeans nods once. Firmly. Like this is the moment.

**CREMEANS** (loudly, over the music)  
YES.

**JEN** (laughing)  
You did not bring Steve Winwood to Tahiti.

**CREMEANS** (grinning like a fool in paradise)  
I brought Steve. Freaking. Winwood.  Because this isn’t just a honeymoon.  This is a journey.  
A spiritual ascension.

**JEN**  
You’re unbelievable.

🎶 Without it, life is wasted time… 🎶

**CREMEANS** (singing along badly)  
Look inside your heart, I’ll look inside mine—

Jen just stares at him. Smiling. Her towel slipping ever so slightly. The air thick with sunscreen and sentiment.

**JEN** (softly)  
You actually believe this song, don’t you?

**CREMEANS** (earnest)  
I didn’t.  Not until you.

She looks away, out the window, trying not to melt—but her smile gives her away.

🎶 Things look so bad everywhere…  
In this whole world, what is fair? 🎶

**CREMEANS** (softer now, still singing)  
We walk blind and we try to see…  
Falling behind in what could be…

They drive on, wind in their hair, the ocean beside them, the beat climbing, Steve preaching the gospel of romantic perseverance, and Cremeans watching his topless wife laugh in the front seat like it’s the last first day of the rest of his life.

And as the chorus hits?

🎶 Bring me a higher love  
Ohhhhhh—  
Bring me a higher love—ohhhhhh… 🎶

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF TWO PEOPLE DRIVING THROUGH A DREAM,  WITH LOVE IN THE FRONT SEAT, AND STEVE WINWOOD AS THEIR PROPHET.

---

**## **EXT. TAHITIAN COAST ROAD – RENTAL CAR – CONTINUOUS**  
(Windows down. Music blaring. The world fully surrendered to rhythm, sun, and the sanctified absurdity of love on vacation.)

Steve Winwood is still soaring through the speakers like a middle-aged archangel of emotion.  
Jen is still in the passenger seat, towel barely hanging on, sunglasses sliding down her nose from laughing too hard.

And Cremeans?  He’s not just driving—he’s piloting the emotional climax of an '80s romcom that’s never getting made but absolutely should.

Jen shakes her head, smiling as the chorus drops again:

🎶 Bring me a higher love… 🎶

**JEN** (teasing)  
Was that a set up, Jeffrey Cremeans?

She turns to him, eyes narrowed playfully.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
You queue up the song, drop the topless bit, lay down the spiritual monologue, and now we’re driving toward sin with a CD full of dad ballads?

**CREMEANS** (grinning like a feral man who won at life)  
Nope.

He reaches over—nonchalant, confident, baptized in both sunscreen and gall—and gives her left breast a warm, adoring squeeze.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D, deadpan)  
I just rolled with it, baby.

Jen groans.  Loud.  The sound of a woman caught between desire and deep, aching pun fatigue.

**JEN** (half-laughing, half-murderous)  
Jeff. That was so bad I think my ovaries revoked your access.

**CREMEANS** (smug)  
And yet, still…very much holding your attention.

She yanks the towel back up with one hand while trying to hide a grin. She fails. He sees it. Victory confirmed.

**JEN** (dry)  
If you make one more Winwood pun, I’m making you sleep on the balcony. With the geckos.

**CREMEANS** (mock-hurt)  
Those geckos respect me.  
They saw everything last night.

Jen bursts out laughing, almost dropping the towel again.

They cruise down the coastline, Steve singing them deeper into honeymoon glory, and Jen secretly planning how to punish him later. Lovingly. Enthusiastically. Probably with item #8 on the list.

---

**## **EXT. TAHITIAN BEACH – LATE AFTERNOON – GOLDEN HOUR**

They’ve stopped the car.

Somewhere along the coast, far from the tourists and closer to God’s personal screensaver, Cremeans pulled over just to sit with her. No towels. No agenda. Just the glow of 4:43 p.m. and the hush of surf rolling in with soft authority.

Jen sits in front of him on the sand, her legs stretched out, the hem of her wrap fluttering slightly in the breeze. He’s behind her, arms draped lazily around her waist, chin on her shoulder.

They’ve stopped talking. Not because there’s nothing to say.  
But because everything’s been said in sun and skin and proximity.

Then he speaks—quietly. Almost like it’s not meant for the air, just for her bones.

**CREMEANS** (softly)  
The guys have really been turned on by the next one.

Jen blinks.

**JEN** (quietly)  
The new track?

**CREMEANS**  
Yeah.  
The Evans brothers are enamored.  
I played it for them last week during that late-night thing at the studio…  
And I heard it, once, just once—and I thought…



I thought this was about you.

His voice drops lower, more fragile.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Seasons change and I have found you…  
Looks like you've been here a long time…  
Looks like you're here to stay…  
And I reason that that's O.K.

Jen’s eyes close.

He’s not quoting it like a love song.  
He’s quoting it like a fear.  
Like something he doesn’t want to name out loud.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Then it turns.  
When though, when will you be leaving…  
Way up in the trees…  
Afloat on the seas…  
I can't afford your voice…  
But I have no choice…



I hear that lyric and I think…  
God.  
Don’t let us ever get to that place.

He kisses her shoulder. Not out of passion—out of plea.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Let’s never let it get… there.  
Where I’m watching you float away.  
Where the only thing I can do is turn up the volume and pretend it’s enough.

She doesn’t speak right away.  
Just pulls his hands tighter around her, lacing her fingers into his.

**JEN** (softly)  
You won’t have to pretend.  
Because I’m not going anywhere.  
And if I do?  
You’ll be right there beside me, packing too many T-shirts and worrying about the return policy on sandals.

**CREMEANS** (half-laughs)  
That’s… strangely comforting.

**JEN**  
I’m not a lyric that walks away.  
I’m the bridge that comes back around when the song needs to mean more.

She turns her head, presses her lips to his temple.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
Let’s never get to that place.

**CREMEANS**  
Never.

The waves crash softly.

The wind shifts.

And behind them, the sun keeps lowering—but only because it has to, not because it’s leaving.

---
## **EXT. TAHITIAN BEACH – SUNSET – MOMENTS LATER  
(The sky is a stained glass of gold and violet. The ocean exhales. The breeze bows respectfully. And two people kneel in the sand—not because they’ve fallen, but because they’ve found something worth lowering themselves for.)

Jen turns toward him. Bare knees in the warm grit. Her hands are in his, and for once, he’s not leading—he’s asking.

**CREMEANS** (voice thick with devotion)  
Pray with me, Jen.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
For… forever.

She doesn’t answer right away.  
Just squeezes his hands.  
Then nods—once.  
A simple, profound yes that makes the wind pause.

They bow their heads together.

Not like a ritual.

Like a vow made of breath and faith and everything they’re afraid to lose.

**CREMEANS** (quietly)  
Lord…  
Thank You for the day You brought her into my life.  
Thank You for the patience You gave us to wait.  
Thank You for the fire, and the calm after it.

**JEN** (softly)  
Thank You for this love.  
That it’s weird.  
That it’s holy.  
That it’s ours.

**CREMEANS**  
Help us not just survive time… but savor it.

**JEN**  
Help us fight for “us” even when we forget why.  
Even when it’s easier not to.

**CREMEANS**  
Let me see her—clearly—when the world tries to fog it up.  
Let her see me…  
Not just when I’m strong.  
But when I’m yours.

**JEN**  
Let our joy be louder than our fear.  
And our faith… bigger than our pride.



**JEN** (whispering)  
Let this… be forever.

He nods, eyes still shut.

**CREMEANS** (hoarse)  
Amen.

**JEN**  
Amen.

They sit back on their heels. The tide pulls gently around their feet. A hush falls—not awkward. Not silent.

Just… held.

He kisses her knuckles.  
She brushes the hair off his forehead.

And for the first time in the entire trip, nothing needs to be said.

They just sit there.  
Two people.  
Prayed-up.  
Tanned.  
Married.

---

**## **EXT. SECLUDED TAHITIAN BEACH – EARLY NEXT MORNING – THE SUN’S FIRST WINK**

(The beach is empty, the breeze is gentle, and the sun is just starting to peek over the edge of the water like it’s nosy about someone’s business—and it should be.)

Cremeans stands there—shirtless, barefoot, wearing nothing but confidence and maybe a pair of swim trunks that are about to lose the battle. The man is on a mission. A mission of trust, of exposure, and of thorough SPF strategy.

Jen emerges from the bungalow with a beach bag that looks suspiciously like it was packed with intentions, not just towels.

She’s got the sunscreen. The big bottle. The one that squirts aggressively and smells like vacation and decisions.

**CREMEANS** (grinning, arms out like he’s welcoming judgment)  
Now, about applying sunscreen everywhere, Jen…

Are you ready to cover every square inch of me?

She stops walking. Tilts her head. Smirks like a Bond villain in a sundress.

**JEN**  
You mean every—

**CREMEANS** (nodding, solemn as a church deacon)  
Every.  
Last.  
Crevasse.

**JEN** (pretending to consider)  
That’s a lot of real estate, Jeff.

**CREMEANS** (shrugs)  
God gave me acreage. You married the deed.

She walks up to him slowly, deliberately, unscrews the sunscreen bottle like she’s about to bless something.

**JEN** (mock-serious)  
This is a sacred task.

**CREMEANS** (deadpan)  
I accept your ministry.

She pumps once. Rubs her hands together. Steps closer.

**JEN**  
Turn around. Spread ‘em.  
This is gonna be clinical and flirty.

He obeys. Turns like a soldier reporting for duty.

**CREMEANS** (over his shoulder)  
If you skip the backs of my knees, I’m filing for annulment.

She starts at the shoulders. Moves down.  
She’s thorough. Alarmingly thorough.  
And Cremeans is starting to lose composure about three vertebrae in.

**CREMEANS** (muffled)  
This is either foreplay or a baptism and I don’t know which.

**JEN** (cheerfully)  
Why can’t it be both?

She pats him once on the hip.  
Then spins him back around.  
Eye contact.  
Bottle raised.

**JEN** (CONT’D)  
Now… the front.

Cremeans swallows. Hard.

**CREMEANS**  
Every square inch?

**JEN** (grinning)  
Especially the inches that think they’re important.

---

**## **EXT. SECLUDED TAHITIAN BEACH – CONTINUOUS**

(The waves whisper. The sun is rising like it knows a secret. And this stretch of sand is currently hosting a private sacrament of SPF and shamelessness.)

Cremeans is now standing there, gloriously erect, his body glistening in a way that would concern polite society but would absolutely sell out a calendar in three languages.

Jen pauses, hands still slick with sunscreen, eyes dropping like they have a spiritual obligation to acknowledge the moment.

She raises an eyebrow.  
Says nothing at first.  
Just lets the silence carry the weight of his… enthusiasm.

Then, finally:

**JEN** (dryly)  
Nothing that gets us arrested, right?

**CREMEANS** (cheerful, completely unbothered by his extremely public joy)  
Nope! Totally legal.  
No laws against being enthusiastically alive.



But uh—make sure you get my toes too.

(he grins)

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Right after the bottom of my scrotum.

Jen stares at him.  
Hands on hips.  
Mouth slightly open in mock disbelief.

**JEN**  
You’re making this weird.

**CREMEANS**  
You brought the sunscreen. I brought the canvas.

**JEN** (muttering)  
You brought a tent pole.

**CREMEANS** (proudly)  
A structural one.  
Keeps the marital temple upright.

She sighs. But she’s smiling. And her hands are still warm with lotion. And let’s be honest—she was never not going to finish the job.

**JEN** (softly)  
Turn back around.  
Try not to moan at the toes.

**CREMEANS** (grinning wide)  
No promises.  
This is the most spiritually confusing moment of my life.

---


**## **EXT. SECLUDED TAHITIAN BEACH – NOONISH – SUN, SKIN, AND SLIGHTLY CONFUSING CHARACTER NAMES**

The sky is a canvas of relentless blue.  
The waves roll in with all the chill of a laid-back deity.  
Cremeans and Jen lie stretched out on their towels—unclothed, unashamed, and definitely not reading as much as they claim to be.

Between them, a slightly worn paperback rests, its cover dark and broody, its title in a language that doesn’t scream beach read but absolutely whispers "nerd-approved foreplay."

**CREMEANS** (gently, gesturing toward the book)  
That’s from Jeff Evans, by the way.  
Wedding gift.  
Snuck it into my luggage with a note that said, “For when the tan lines disappear and the brains come back online.”

Jen lifts it, turns it over in her hands. The title stares back: The Last Wish, by Andrzej Sapkowski—1994 edition, obscure as sin in the American Midwest.

**JEN** (squinting)  
Sapkowski?

**CREMEANS**  
Polish. Evans picked it up in Warsaw last winter.  
Apparently he’s been reading the untranslated stuff and claims it’s “brutal, romantic, and deeply Catholic,” which honestly sounds like something he would fall in love with.

**JEN** (grinning)  
I’m sorry, are you telling me our wedding present is a grim fantasy novel about a broody man who slays monsters and emotionally avoids intimacy?

**CREMEANS**  
Yes. So naturally, he thought of us.

She rolls onto her side, smiling, flipping through a few pages.

**JEN**  
This is what happens when you have two Jeffs in your life. One buys you lingerie. The other gives you Slavic existentialism with sword fights.

**CREMEANS** (mock serious)  
It’s the cross you bear.  
Beautiful, complicated woman… cursed with multiple Jeffs.

She tosses a little sand at him.

**JEN**  
Let’s lie here, pretend to read, and sneak peeks at each other over the pages.  
We’ll give Evans the satisfaction of believing we absorbed something literary between rounds of sunscreen and naked sun worship.

**CREMEANS**  
Deal.  
But if I catch you fantasizing about Geralt instead of me, I’m telling Gilley.

**JEN** (smirking)  
If I start picturing Geralt, I’m casting you.  
Long white wig. No shirt. One sword. Lots of grunting.

**CREMEANS** (blushing but pleased)  
Stop. I’m gonna need more sunscreen.

They lie back. The book rests open between them, unread.  
Their eyes drift to each other.  
And neither of them cares about chapter structure anymore.

FADE OUT: TO THE SOUND OF WAVES,  
SLIGHTLY STICKY PAPERBACKS,  
AND A COUPLE WHO KNOW THE BEST STORIES AREN’T ALWAYS ON THE PAGE.

---
## **EXT. SECLUDED TAHITIAN BEACH – LATE AFTERNOON – SUN LOWERING, HEARTS OPENING

They’ve moved under the shade now, not from shame, but from knowing when to rest. The sunscreen has done its job. The sand has molded to their bodies like it approves of their union. The paperback is forgotten beside them—dog-eared, slightly gritty, perfectly untouched for 40 minutes.

Jen is lying on her back, hair a halo of sand and salt.  
Cremeans is sitting beside her, one knee up, arms wrapped around it like a man trying to contain a future that’s just starting to bloom in his chest.

He’s quiet. For a while. Then:

**CREMEANS** (softly)  
This is why I work so hard, Jen.

She turns her head toward him. He’s not looking at her—he’s looking out at the water like it’s asking him questions.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
It’s not for the gear, or the guitars, or the rider that lets us skip load-in on Saturdays.



It’s for this.

He finally looks down at her.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
You in it.  
A home.  
Three kids running circles around us, wearing church shoes and ruining furniture.  
Me getting home late, tired… but knowing you’ve got the rest of it held together with grace and freezer meals.

Jen doesn’t interrupt. Doesn’t smile yet. Just listens, eyes soft.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
Can you do that?  
Can you run my household… our household… when things get loud and hard and dumb?



Because if you do that…  
I’ll be your shield.

He leans forward. Takes her hand in both of his.

**CREMEANS** (CONT’D)  
I’ll take every arrow the world throws.  
Every bill. Every breakdown. Every time one of our kids screams “I hate you!” and slams a door at 13.  
I’ll be there. Right in front of it.  
So you don’t have to flinch.

Jen breathes out slowly.  
And finally, she speaks—not dramatic, not dreamy—just real.

**JEN**  
You show me the life…  
and I’ll run the house.  
We’ll raise those kids.  
We’ll throw dinner parties where we forget the dessert in the freezer and your mom “casually” mentions our lawn.  
We’ll build it all from scratch.



You’ll be the shield.  
I’ll be the flame.

Cremeans closes his eyes. Just for a second. And when he opens them—

**CREMEANS** (quietly, but certain)  
Then we’re going to be unstoppable.


---

**## **EXT. SECLUDED TAHITIAN BEACH – EARLY EVENING – THE GOLDEN HOUR OF TEASING AND TENSION**

Jen stretches like a satisfied cat, the last rays of sun glancing off her shoulders, her skin glowing in that just-married, just-sunned, just-too-happy way. She turns lazily toward Cremeans, who’s doing a poor job pretending he’s not adjusting himself under the towel.

She smirks.  
That knowing, devastating smirk.

**JEN** (mock-casual)  
Your situation there seems to be… developing.  
Need assistance?

Cremeans sighs, resigned and aroused and deeply aware that he married a woman who weaponizes concern.

**CREMEANS** (grinning sheepishly)  
You’re not wrong.  
But… I’m not doing it here.  
Too exposed. Too risky.  
There are birds, Jen.

She raises an eyebrow.

**JEN**  
So the mighty Cremeans is afraid of a little… sand and scandal?

**CREMEANS**  
I’m not afraid.  I just have standards for where I ruin my reputation. You want sex on the beach?  We need a better beach.

**JEN** (tilting her head)  
A better beach?

**CREMEANS**  
A private one.  Somewhere no one but you, me, and maybe a confused sea turtle can bear witness.  We hit up the Concierge again.  Get a charter.  Find some tiny island with nothing on it but soft sand and our very, very bad decisions.

Jen bites her lip.

**JEN**  
So you’re saying… if I’m game?

**CREMEANS** (nods slowly)  
I’ll book the boat.  
Tomorrow.

They stare at each other for a long beat, the ocean humming, the evening closing in, and somewhere in the background, the spirit of marital ambition setting its GPS to “uncharted.”

**JEN** (softly)  
Deal.  But you better pack extra sunscreen, Captain Modesty.

**CREMEANS** (grinning)  
And aloe.  For both of us.

---

**TAHITI — HOTEL LOBBY, EVENING.**

Jeff walks in, still slightly sunburnt, still buzzing from the day's snorkeling trip and the thousand ways his wife smiled at him in water. Jen is upstairs showering — washing sand from the places only he is now allowed to touch.

He approaches the concierge desk. The Concierge is polished, French Polynesian, wearing a pressed white shirt and a knowing smile. He’s seen honeymoons. He’s seen fantasies. But something about Jeff — khakis, crewcut, wedding ring gleaming like a promise kept — makes him pause.

Jeff doesn’t stammer. He doesn’t fidget.

**JEFF:**
“I’d like to charter a boat.”  

**CONCIERGE:**
“But of course, monsieur. A fishing vessel? A sunset cruise?”  

**JEFF:**
“No. Something private. Just us. I want to find an island. Uninhabited. No staff. No other guests. I want to sleep on the beach. I’ll pay well. I want… freedom.”

The Concierge nods — professional, discreet — but slightly curious.

**CONCIERGE:**
“Of course, sir. Might I ask—should I prepare for food, shelter, any particular amenities?”  
Jeff smiles. Not awkward. Not cocky. Just clear.  

**JEFF:**
“We’re on our honeymoon. I plan to make love to my wife under the stars. Maybe in the sand. Maybe in the water. We’ll bring snacks.”

A beat of silence.  The Concierge blinks once. Then smiles back.  Professional. Gracious. And now just a little awed.

**CONCIERGE:**
“We shall find you something… worthy.”

---


**TAHITI – HOTEL BALCONY – LATE EVENING**

The wind moves slow and warm. The sea laps gently below.  
They’ve both showered. Jen wears one of his T-shirts, her damp hair pulled back with a soft tie. Jeff is barefoot, sipping something cold and nonalcoholic from a tall glass, looking like a man trying very hard not to grin too hard at life.

She curls beside him on a cushioned bench, knees tucked.

**JEN:**  
“Okay. The boat. The island. The… making love in the sand part.” (She says it like she’s still getting used to that kind of talk. But she’s smiling.)  
“How much is this going to cost?”

Jeff takes a slow sip.

**JEFF:**  
“Ballpark? About twenty-two grand.”

She stares at him.

**JEN:**  
“Twenty-two… thousand… dollars?”

**JEFF:**  
“Yes, ma’am.”

**JEN:** (half-laughing, half-panicking)  
“Jeffery Lee Cremeans. That is a car. That is a nice car.”

**JEFF:**  
“I already got a car. You’ve seen her. She’s a Saturn. She’s paid for.”

**JEN:**  
“You spent a car on one night?”

**JEFF:** (gently, with complete sincerity)  
“I spent a car on you.”

She’s silent. Not offended. Just… calculating.  
And then it hits her:

**JEN:**  
“Wait. Wait, wait—if you can casually drop twenty-two thousand dollars on a night, how much do you make? Like… actually?”

Jeff pauses. He doesn’t gloat. Doesn’t posture.  
He just tells her the truth.

**JEFF:**  
“About thirty thousand a month. Give or take. Some months are lighter. Some months surprise me.”

Silence.  
Jen leans back like she’s just been hit with a heatwave.  
She stares out at the ocean. Then stares back at him.

**JEN:**  
“That’s… three hundred sixty thousand dollars a year.”

**JEFF:**  
“Not all of it hits the bank. There’s taxes, tithes, savings, the band’s trust account, contracts, advances—”

**JEN:**  
“Jeff. Baby. Honey. I was worried I couldn’t buy a new blender.”

**JEFF:** (soft laugh)  
“Buy the blender.”

**JEN:**  
“I don’t even know what that kind of money feels like. I can’t run a household budget on vibes.”

**JEFF:**  
“Then let me show you. We’ll go over everything. You’ll know it all. It’s our money now.”

She leans into him, blinking, stunned. Then quietly:

**JEN:**  
“You’re not even stressed about it.”

**JEFF:**  
“I’ve been on the phone with lawyers and label execs since you were still reading bridal magazines. Money’s just numbers. You? You’re real.”

She looks at him. Fully. Blinking back a little emotion she hadn’t prepared for.

**JEN:**  
“That’s the most romantic thing anyone’s ever said to me.”

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
“Wait till you see the island.”

---

**TAHITI – 2:14 AM – SHORELINE**

She’s barefoot, one of his dress shirts thrown over her like a whisper.  
The wind is warm and whispering. The tide just shy of touching her toes.  
She’s hugging herself. Not cold. Just processing.

The moon turns the ocean to silver.  
Behind her, Jeff is probably just lying there, glowing quietly, not even aware that he’s left her with this kind of realization.

This is the Pacific Ocean. And her husband is wealthy beyond anything she ever allowed herself to imagine.

Not rich.  
Wealthy.

Chartering islands.  
Sleeping on sand like it’s a honeymoon package.  
Thirty grand a month just flowing in like the tide.

She thinks about his words. “It’s our money now.”

That sounded sweet, didn’t it?  
But it also means she just married into gravity.

---

And now the questions come.

- Who else does he support?
    
- How many lives orbit this man and his phone calls?
    
- How many crises has he solved with a signature?
    
- And were those “dopey” nerds at the wedding — the ones with mismatched jackets and warm, awkward smiles — part of that world?
    

Because now, standing here, they don’t seem so dopey anymore.

They seemed grateful.

- Like men who had been rescued by someone.
    
- Like guys who knew this wasn’t just Jeff’s wedding — it was the only moment they were ever going to get to see him soft.
    
- Like people who had been carried.
    

And Jeff? He never made it about himself. Never strutted. Never dropped the numbers.  
He brought a Saturn to a sword fight and still came out the king.

---

So what does it say about the people he keeps close?

It says: They trust him.  
It says: They love him.  
And it says: They know he’d bleed for them.

Jen stares at the water, blinking, feeling that slow warmth in her thighs — the leftover hum of a man who just loved her like she was the only woman God ever sculpted by hand.

And now she’s realizing:

She married the steward of an empire.

Not a loud one.  
Not a gilded one.  
But a quiet, righteous, relentless kingdom of loyalty, music, fire, and legacy.

And somehow, that man loves her.

---


**TAHITI – BEACHFRONT – 2:17 AM**

Jen is still looking out at the Pacific when she hears the soft shuffle of bare feet on sand.  
She doesn’t turn. She knows it’s him. She can feel it.

He walks up beside her.  
Not bothering with a towel.  
Not shy.  
Just there, skin kissed with moonlight, entirely unashamed.  
He stands beside her like Adam, post-sin, but before shame.

His voice is calm. A little sleepy.

**JEFF:**  
“Something wrong?”

She looks at him.

Takes him in.  
He’s flaccid. But even soft, he’s a lot.  
Still big enough to make her pause.  
Still a reminder of what they just did. What they can do. What they will do.

And that’s not the part that unsettles her.

**JEN:** (quietly)  
“I don’t know if I’m strong enough to handle your people.”

He raises an eyebrow.

**JEFF:**  
“My people?”

She nods. Doesn’t look away.

**JEN:**  
“The ones you lead. The ones who follow you. The ones who came to our wedding with eyeliner and velvet and… broken eyes. The ones you give money to without telling me. The ones who write songs about sin and sex and pain and… play them on national television.”  
  
“I don’t know if I can carry the weight of that world. If I can stand next to you in it.”

Jeff listens. Doesn’t interrupt.  
Just lets the tide roll in behind her words.

Then, slowly, he nods.

**JEFF:**  
“They’re broken people. But they’re mine. And they’re trying.”  
  
“I don’t manage their morals. I manage their lives. I keep them breathing long enough to get better.”  
  
“They’ve seen things you and I have never touched. And they still show up. Still write. Still thank God in their own shattered way.”

She swallows.

**JEN:**  
“But they look at you like you’re something between a pastor and a hitman.”

He chuckles.

**JEFF:**  
“That’s because I am.”

She blinks.

**JEFF:**  
“I keep them alive. I tell the truth. I never lie. And if someone tries to hurt them — I make that stop. No matter what it costs.”

Silence.

He steps closer. His skin brushes hers. Not sexual. Just real.  
And he says:

**JEFF:**  
“But you? You don’t have to carry any of them.”  
(softly)  
“You only have to carry me.”

Jen stares at him.

Naked. Honest. Still enormous in every sense — and yet, somehow, completely hers.

She exhales. Steps forward. Wraps her arms around him. Her cheek presses to his chest.

And she says, very quietly:

**JEN:**  
“Okay. But if I feel overwhelmed… you tell me the truth.”

**JEFF:**  
“Always.”

**JEN:**  
“And if they cross a line… you protect me first.”

**JEFF:** (without hesitation)  
“Before the breath leaves their lungs.”

They stay like that.  
The Pacific just behind them.  
The island in front of them.  
And no more secrets between them.

---

**TAHITI – BEACHFRONT – SAME NIGHT, MOMENTS LATER**

They’re still holding each other. Her cheek on his chest. The ocean humming behind them.

After a few beats of silence, Jeff shifts his weight slightly and speaks — voice low, calm, just a little amused.

**JEFF:**  
“You’re gonna like Jim.”

Jen tilts her head slightly.

**JEN:**  
“Jim?”

**JEFF:**  
“Drummer. Tall. Kind of looks like if a golden retriever got really good at math and then joined a band.”

She snorts softly.

**JEFF:**  
“He goes to church more than twice a year. Real church. Sunday morning, button-down shirt, hand-shaking, potluck casserole-type church.”

**JEN:**  
“That… actually surprises me.”

**JEFF:**  
“Yeah, you’ll have to overlook one thing.”

She pulls back just enough to look at him, suspicious.

**JEN:**  
“He’s not a serial killer, is he?”

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
“Methodist.”

**JEN:** (mock gasp)  
“No.”

**JEFF:**  
“I know. Tragic. They let anyone in those choirs. But Jim? Jim’s solid. Doesn’t smoke. Doesn’t chase. Tithes without bragging about it. Just… shows up. Week after week.”

**JEN:** (softly)  
“That sounds like you.”

**JEFF:**  
“No. I’m a Baptist. I bring casseroles and judgment. He brings rhythm and grace.”

She laughs. Genuinely now. The tension of a few minutes ago dissolving into the tide.

**JEFF:**  
“He keeps time. That’s his job. For the band. For himself. For me. He keeps time so the rest of us can get loud, or lost, or stupid — and still find our way back.”

**JEN:** (quietly)  
“You trust him.”

**JEFF:**  
“With everything but my wife.”

**JEN:** (grinning)  
“Smart man.”

They stand together in the moonlight, finally breathing easy again.

---

**TAHITI – BEACHFRONT – STILL NIGHT**

They’ve started walking slowly back toward their little hut. Barefoot. Skin warm from moonlight and each other. Conversation humming now, alive, flowing easily.

Jen’s fingers trace the inside of Jeff’s palm as they walk.

**JEN:**  
“Tell me about another one. Someone else I’ll need to meet.”

Jeff exhales, thoughtful.  
Smiles a little sideways.

**JEFF:**  
“Bill.”

**JEN:**  
“What’s his deal?”

Jeff lets out a small laugh — not mocking, just… perplexed.

**JEFF:**  
“Bill is… intriguing.”

**JEN:**  
“That’s code for ‘I don’t understand him, but I’m a little fascinated.’”

**JEFF:**  
“It’s not wrong.”

They step around a tide pool, and Jeff continues.

**JEFF:**  
“He’s trippy. Not drugs-trippy — not like Gilley. Just… head in the clouds. Sees music like architecture. Hears color. Plays a synth like it’s a scalpel.”

**JEN:**  
“Artist.”

**JEFF:**  
“Yes — but at his core? He’s an engineer. Builds sound. Layer by layer. All logic, all precision, all control. It’s like watching a stoner play chess.”

She laughs. Then pauses.

**JEN:**  
“Straight?”

Jeff doesn’t answer immediately.  
He’s not uncomfortable — just honest.

**JEFF:**  
“I don’t think so. Not strictly. He never says. Never chases. Doesn’t flirt. Doesn’t broadcast anything. Just floats. You get the feeling he’s watching a different movie than the rest of us.”

**JEN:**  
“Does it matter to the band?”

**JEFF:**  
“Not even a little.”  
  
“He’s not our anomaly because of who he might sleep with. He’s our anomaly because he never loses his center. Not even once.”

Jen processes that. Looks at Jeff.

**JEN:**  
“You admire him.”

**JEFF:**  
“I monitor him. With admiration.”

They reach the porch. The sea still whispers behind them.

**JEFF:**  
“Compared to the rest of the band, he’s the one that doesn’t fall apart. Doesn’t scream. Doesn’t crave the edge.”

**JEN:**  
“What does he crave?”

**JEFF:**  
“Resonance.”

She doesn’t fully understand that yet — but the way Jeff says it tells her it’s important.

And somewhere deep inside, she decides:  
She wants to hear Bill play.


---

**TAHITI – HUT VERANDA – POST-BEACH, PRE-BED**

Jeff pours them both water. The good kind, from a tall glass bottle that costs too much. Jen curls into a rattan chair, her legs pulled under her. She’s still trying to picture Bill with headphones on and a blank expression, building cathedrals of sound.

**JEN:**  
“Okay. So I’ve got Jim. I’ve got Bill. Who’s next?”

Jeff pauses.  
Takes a sip.  
Then gives her a look that’s both amused and deeply serious.

**JEFF:**  
“Gilley.”

Jen raises an eyebrow.

**JEN:**  
“The infamous?”

**JEFF:**  
“That’s the one.”

He sits down across from her. Sets the glass down. Leans forward, elbows on knees.

**JEFF:**  
“You need to know him. But more than that — you need to know how to handle him.”

Jen tilts her head, alert.

**JEFF:**  
“I grew up two doors down from Gilley. He was loud in fifth grade. He was loud in high school. He’s still loud now. But now he’s got a band and money and the kind of face that gets him whatever he wants — and he knows it.”

**JEN:**  
“So… he’s trouble.”

**JEFF:**  
“He’s charm with a pulse. A walking hormone with a leather jacket. He’s a magnet. And I’ve watched women who should know better forget their own names when he walks in the room.”

**JEN:** (quietly)  
“Would he try something with me?”

Jeff locks eyes with her. Not angry. Not jealous. Just blunt.

**JEFF:**  
“He will. Not because he’s evil. Because it’s habit. He’ll test the waters. Flirt. Flash the smile. Try a line or two.”

**JEN:**  
“And if I say no?”

**JEFF:**  
“Then he’s gone. Instantly. You throw up a stop sign, he respects it. But if you leave the door cracked — even a little — he will kick it open just to see what’s on the other side.”

**JEN:**  
“So… a predator.”

**JEFF:**  
“No. A player. And he only plays if you’re on the board.”

He leans back.

**JEFF:**  
“If your energy says ‘not available’ — emotionally, sexually, spiritually — he drops it. You don’t become prey. You become invisible.”

**JEN:**  
“Sounds cold.”

**JEFF:**  
“No. It’s instinct. It’s survival. Gilley has so much testosterone, he probably sweats cologne. He walks into a room and people turn. He commands. Without effort. Without tactics.”

**JEN:**  
“So why isn’t he more… dangerous?”

Jeff shrugs.

**JEFF:**  
“Because if he ever learned self-control? If he ever zipped his pants up and stayed focused for six months straight? He wouldn’t just run a band. He’d run a state. Maybe the country.”

**JEN:**  
“That good?”

**JEFF:**  
“That magnetic. But that’s not how he works. Gilley isn’t built for stillness. He needs chaos. Attention. Heat. Women are just… mirrors to him. Reflections of how powerful he feels.”

Jen takes that in.  
Then, softly:

**JEN:**  
“So what do I do?”

**JEFF:**  
“Smile. Nod. Laugh at the first joke. Then shut it down. Not with anger. With indifference. He reads energy like a hawk. Show him you don’t play, and he’ll respect you for it. Probably never flirt with you again.”

**JEN:**  
“And if I compliment his shirt?”

**JEFF:**  
“He’ll ask if you want to see it on your bedroom floor.”

**JEN:** (deadpan)  
“Charming.”

**JEFF:**  
“Tragically.”

He finishes his water.  
They sit in silence for a moment.  
Then Jen grins.

**JEN:**  
“So… you grew up two doors down from that circus act?”

**JEFF:**  
“Yup.”

**JEN:**  
“And you came out like this?”

**JEFF:**  
“Someone had to do the homework.”


---

**TAHITI – VERANDA – NIGHT**

Jen shifts against him. The conversation is deepening — not just about individuals, but about what they stand for.

**JEN:**  
“And of course… there was Jeff Evans.”

**JEFF:**   (soft chuckle)  
“Yeah. Chains and all. That’s Evans. Other half of the Brain Trust. He and Kathy write the lyrics.”

**JEN:**  
“I’ve heard some of them. They’re… intense.”

Cremeans:  
“Deliberate.”

**JEN:**  
“Some of them made me uncomfortable.”

**JEFF:**   
“Good. They’re supposed to.”

He looks at her now — not with edge, but with conviction.

**JEFF:**  
“Kathy and Evans aren’t out to entertain. They’re out to expose. They write to drag things into the light. Especially religious hypocrisy. That’s the target. Not faith. Not truth. Hypocrisy.”

Jen is quiet, absorbing.

**JEFF:**    
“You and I both know God doesn’t hate sinners. He died for sinners. But He has words for liars who pretend they’re clean while they rot on the inside. Kathy and Evans go after that rot. Line by line.”

**JEN:** (carefully)  
“So… the coarse language? The apocalyptic imagery?”

**JEFF:**    
“It’s not noise. It’s judgment. And it's earned.”

**JEN:**  
“And you’re okay managing that?”

**JEFF:**   (without hesitation)  
“I believe in what they’re doing. I don’t write a single note. But I know the difference between sin and deception. They’re not writing filth — they’re writing truth in a dialect the broken can understand.”

She lets that sit for a moment.  
Then nods. Just once.

**JEN:**  
“You were never afraid of the dark, were you?”

**JEFF:**   
“Not if I know who’s holding the match.”


---

**TAHITI – VERANDA – NIGHT**

They’re lying together now. She’s half-dozing, cheek on his chest. The ocean’s still speaking, soft and steady.

But Jeff’s mind? Still working.

And after a long silence, he says:

**JEFF:** 
“The trouble with Jeff…”

Jen stirs slightly.  
Looks up.

**JEFF:** 
“…is Kathy.”

**JEN:** (instantly awake)  
“Oh.”

**JEFF:** 
“Not like that. Not in the soap opera sense. It’s not scandal. It’s… worse.”

He stares up at the ceiling of stars, like he's trying to chart their madness in constellations.

**JEFF:** 
“They love each other. Deeply. Obsessively. They get each other in a way no one else ever will. It’s not romantic. Not consistently. It’s not sexual. Not permanently. But it’s real.”

**JEN:**  
“That sounds…”

**JEFF:** 
“It’s nuclear. You’ve got Evans — a natural. Lyrics fall out of him like prophecy. He breathes rhythm. He bleeds melody.  
And then you’ve got Kathy — a hammer in the dark. She works. Grinds. Builds every word like a cathedral. She’s brilliant — but it drains her.”

**JEN:**  
“And they write together?”

**JEFF:**  
“Better than anyone. They make magic. Real, dangerous, industry-shaking art.  
But then? They burn each other down.”

He exhales.

**JEFF:** 
“They love each other.  
Then hate each other.  
Then need each other.  
Then wound each other.  
And start all over again.”

**JEN:**  
“That’s awful.”

**JEFF:** 
“It’s inevitable.”

He looks down at her. Gentle, but firm.

**JEFF:**
“My job isn’t to save them. My job is to contain them. To protect them from themselves.  
To keep the fire burning without letting it torch the house.”

**JEN:**  
“How?”

**JEFF:** 
“Carefully. Daily. With God’s help and a thousand back-channel conversations.  
I edit out the worst lines. I delay studio dates. I separate hotel floors.  
I pray when no one’s looking.”

She doesn’t know what to say.

So she just says:

**JEN:**  
“That’s… heavy.”

**JEFF:**  
“That’s the job. They can’t figure it out. They’ll never figure it out.  
But if I do my part, they won’t destroy each other.  
At least not this year.”

He kisses her temple.  She squeezes his hand.  And that’s how she finally understands: Her husband doesn’t just manage a band.

the manager brain kicks in.

He points to the waterproof bags and ration boxes, still sitting near the tree line.

Cremeans: (practical, still grinning)  
“But first we gotta make sure our gear’s safe.  
Those cardboard ration boxes’ll turn into oatmeal in about two minutes.”

Jen laughs —  
clapping a hand over her mouth, rain already soaking her hair.

**JEN:** (teasing, breathless)  
“See?  
This is why I married you.  
Passionate.  
Protective.  
Practical.”

Jeff shrugs — mock-humble.

Cremeans:  
“One out of three’s not bad.”

Jen moves fast — helping him drag the waterproof bags up under the thickest part of the palms, stacking the empty ration boxes under a low branch where the rain won’t pound them flat.

The rain thickens — turning the air into a curtain of silver.

Jen ties her soaked hair back — grinning wickedly.

**JEN:**  
“Maybe…  
maybe this replaces shower sex on my honeymoon to-do list.”

Jeff straightens up — laughing hard now.

Cremeans: (teasing)  
“What, too much to ask for plumbing?”

**JEN:** (stepping closer, voice low, rain dripping from her lashes)  
“Who needs plumbing when you have thunder and lightning and a naked husband in the wild?”

Jeff grabs her waist —  
pulls her in —  
both of them already soaked, laughing, hearts hammering.

The storm gathers itself above them —  
ready to break —  
ready to baptize them again.

And they’re ready too.
