TAHITI – ISLET – LOVE LIKE A STORM

The first drops hit like laughter —  
soft, teasing, playful.

Jeff and Jen crash into each other —  
naked, slick, grinning —  
their bodies already humming from the leftover charge of the afternoon.

He lifts her against him —  
her legs wrapping around his waist —  
his mouth crashing against hers in a kiss wild enough to make the thunder jealous.

They stumble back onto the sleeping bag —  
already soaked, already sliding, already laughing —  
as the rain thickens into a drumming roar.

But they don’t stop.

They can't.

Because the storm is inside them now.

Cremeans (internally):  
*If the world is going to fall apart,  
we’re going to love each other to the last crack of thunder.

Jen presses her forehead to his —  
eyes blazing, skin burning —  
and rides him with a rhythm as fierce as the pounding rain.

Their bodies slap together —  
wet skin on wet skin —  
the noise of it drowned in the ocean's roar and the sky’s deep, shaking growl.

And then —  
the heavens rip open.

The rain becomes a wall.  
A hammer.  
A baptism of fire made water.

Thunder cracks so loud that the ground beneath them shivers.

The palms thrash overhead.  
The whole world goes dark for a heartbeat,  
then flashes back to life in white fire.

And Jeff and Jen —  
laughing, gasping, clinging, driving each other higher —  
decide without words:

Match it.

Their hips slam together harder.  
Their hands clutch and roam more desperately.  
Their mouths find each other in gasping, open kisses —  
biting, panting, devouring.

This isn’t careful.  
This isn’t polite.

This is love that dares the sky to burn.

Jen arches back —  
the rain carving rivers down her breasts, her belly, her thighs —  
and cries out without fear, without shame, without anything left to hold back.

Jeff drives into her —  
harder, deeper —  
his whole body singing with the storm's rage,  
his whole soul anchored only to her.

Cremeans (internally):  
*If this is the end of the world —  
let it end with her breath in my mouth,  
with her body clutching mine,  
with our love louder than the thunder.

They crash together —  
again and again —  
rain blinding them, drowning them, glorifying them.

Their climax isn't a single moment.

It’s a flood.

A rising.

A surrender.

The same way the ocean surrenders to the storm.  
The same way the earth surrenders to the rain.

They shatter —  
together —  
laughing, crying, gasping —  
as the sky howls and weeps and crowns them with holy, furious blessing.

TAHITI – ISLET – AFTER THE FLOOD

As suddenly as it slammed into them,

The rain tapers off —  
the hammering roar softens into a gentle patter, then a mist, then nothing.

The sky splits open again —  
bright, blinding blue above —  
as if the whole tantrum of the heavens had never happened at all.

The ocean sloshes lazily at the shore.  
The palms drip.  
The sand sucks and shifts underfoot — soaked to its bones.

Jeff and Jen lie side-by-side on the half-flooded sleeping bag —  
completely drenched, completely naked, completely happy.

**JEN:** (grinning, breathless)  
“That…

Cremeans: (nodding)

we just lived through a minor apocalypse.”

**JEN:** (half laughing)  
“I'd say…  
an inch and a half. Maybe two.”

Jeff stretches — muscles sore, heart light.

Cremeans: (grinning)  
“Wouldn't surprise me.  
This is one of the rainiest places on Earth.

laughing so hard she can't even sit up again.

happy in a way that only wildness can make you happy.

Overhead, a single rainbow —  
sharp, fierce, perfect —  
arches out over the endless, forgiving sea.

TAHITI – ISLET – THE WET SPOT MYSTERY

The wet spot?”

It’s messy.

TAHITI – ISLET – SUDDEN, AWKWARD REALIZATIONS

They finish wringing out the sleeping bag —

Jen flops onto her back —  
arms stretched wide, hair a wild halo on the drying bag.

Jeff settles beside her —  
propping his head on one hand, watching her with lazy, affectionate eyes.

The storm has passed.  
The sea murmurs.  
The world slows.

And in the golden, goofy quiet —

She blinks up at the sky —  
makes a little grimace —  
and then laughs.

Jeff raises an eyebrow —  
already amused.

Cremeans: (grinning)  
“Uh-oh.  
That’s the face of an extremely weird thought.  
Spill it.”

laughing and groaning at the same time.

**JEN:** (muffled)  
“You’re gonna regret asking.”

Jeff nudges her side — playful.

Cremeans:  
“Try me.”

Jen peeks out from behind her fingers — bright red but giggling.

**JEN:** (half-horrified, half-laughing)  
“I just realized…

that my mom…  
changed her own teeth every third day after me and my brothers were born.”

Jeff blinks.  
Processing.

Cremeans: (careful)

Jen nods frantically — laughing harder.

**JEN:**  
“Yes! Dentures!  
But when you're little,

Mom’s teeth come and go.  
No big deal.”

Jeff snorts —

**JEN:** (mock-tragic)  
“And only now, at twenty-one years old, after making love in a monsoon,  
do I realize how incredibly weird that is!”

Jeff doubles over laughing —  
nearly face-planting into the sand.

Jen buries her face in his shoulder, both of them shaking with laughter.

**JEN:** (giggling)  
“Not exactly the mental picture you want floating into your brain right after sex.”

Cremeans: (gasping, grinning)  
“Definitely not the honeymoon fantasy brochure, babe.”

They cling to each other —  
laughing, groaning, loving every awkward, human, hilarious second of it.

Because this too is marriage:  
the weird thoughts, the strange memories, the stuff you can't plan for…  
and the one person who laughs with you anyway.

TAHITI – ISLET – THE AWKWARD REALIZATION

The sun is sinking low, soft and golden, as Jen and Jeff relax on the now-dry sleeping bag —  
still naked, still tangled, but now in a state of quiet amusement.

Jen lies back, hands behind her head, gazing up at the sky.  
And then, out of nowhere, her brain collides with something that’s been lurking there —  
something so weird, so funny, and so awkward, she can't help but blurt it out.

**JEN:** (laughing, half-groaning)  
“Oh my God.  
I just realized something.  
This is so weird.”

Jeff turns his head to her, already amused by her sudden shift in energy.

Cremeans: (grinning)  
“Uh-oh.  
That sounds dangerous.  
Spill it.”

Jen rolls her eyes, covering her face with one hand as she shifts into a sitting position, her voice still full of laughter.

**JEN:** (half-sighing, half-laughing)

Jeff looks at her, confused for a second, his eyebrows furrowing slightly.

Cremeans:  
“Wait… what?”

Jen’s face is bright red now, but the laughter still spills out.

**JEN:** (awkward but amused)  
“Like a lot.  
Frequently.  
Regularly.

At 21 years old.

Cremeans: (laughing hard)  
“Oh my God!  
You just figured that out?

**JEN:** (mock-shocked, hands in the air)

All those times I was pretending to be asleep,  
and they were, like, making more kids…”

Cremeans: (laughing even harder)

Jen’s laugh is just as wild, now fully giving in to the ridiculousness of it all.  
Her cheeks burn, but she can’t stop smiling —  
the weirdest, most hilarious realization coming at the least expected moment.

**JEN:** (giggling)  
“I mean, who even wants to know about their parents’ sex life, right?  
I didn't ask for this mental image, Jeff.  
But there it is.”

Jeff takes a deep breath —  
finally able to catch his breath through the laughter,  
still shaking his head in disbelief.

Cremeans:  
“Well, now we know the truth about why I was always so good at keeping secrets.  
My parents gave me that gift.”

Jen sighs —  
laughing and shaking her head at herself.

**JEN:** (smiling sheepishly)  
“I really don’t know how I didn't figure that out earlier.  
I guess it’s just… one of those things you don’t think about.”

The world is still warm around them, the storm now a distant memory, and the two of them just lay there — laughing at the absurdity of the moment,  
and together in all the awkwardness of discovering the truth of family.

TAHITI – ISLET – DIGGING FOR THE GOOD STUFF

Seed by seed.

Of building something real.  
Of choosing love, even when it’s hard.  
Of becoming more than either could be alone.

And the stars wheel overhead,

And they hold each other under the endless night —

TAHITI – ISLET – NO COMPROMISE

The stars are steady above them —

**JEN:** (quiet but hard as iron)

No painkillers.  
No epidural.  
No compromise.”

Jeff goes still —

**JEN:**

I want to feel it.  
I want to do it the old way.  
The real way.”

She shifts — sits up slightly, her hair a wild halo in the starlight.

**JEN:**  
“It’s going to be you, and me,  
and my teeth gnashing, grunting, straining, pushing.  
And God willing, it’s going to end with a baby crying in my arms.  
Not a surgical team.  
Not a drip line.  
Not a curtain.”

She breathes deep —  
not out of drama, but certainty.

**JEN:**  
“I’m going to hurt.  
And I’m going to do it anyway.”

Jeff stares at her —  
heart thudding, eyes wide —  
seeing his wife not just as the woman who shares his bed,  
but the warrior who will bring life into the world.

He doesn't interrupt.  
He doesn’t try to soften it.  
He just nods.

Cremeans: (quietly)  
“Then I’ll be there.  
Every second.  
Every breath.  
Every push.  
I’ll hold your hand.  
I’ll hold your hair.  
I’ll hold the line.”

Jen swallows —  
because it hits her just how real that sounds coming from him.

**JEN:** (softly)  
“Even if I scream at you?”

Cremeans:  
“Especially then.”

She exhales —  
shaking a little, from love, from truth, from the knowing.

**JEN:**  
“I don’t want to be numbed.  
I want to be present.  
I want to meet our baby awake and alive and completely whole.”

Jeff reaches up —  
cups her face with both hands.

Cremeans: (fierce and reverent)  
“Then you’ll do it.  
And I will be there.  
You are the bravest person I’ve ever met.”

And for a moment,  
they sit in silence —  
not romantic, not soft — but holy.

Because this is marriage too:  
not just love on the beach,  
but pain.  
Blood.  
Breath.  
And bearing life together.

TAHITI – ISLET – THE Costliest Promise

The stars seem to dim —  
or maybe it’s just the way the world narrows down  
to just them,  
just this breath,  
just this impossible thing.

Jen opens her mouth to speak —  
then closes it again —  
choked silent.

Jeff feels it —  
feels her whole body stiffen against him,  
feels the earthquake building behind her ribs.

He doesn't rush her.  
He just strokes her back slowly,  
waiting.

Jen swallows hard —  
a sound too loud in the hush of the island.

She tries again.  
Fails.  
Presses her forehead against his shoulder —  
as if she needs to borrow his strength just to say it.

And then —  
finally —  
the words come, cracked and raw:

**JEN:** (barely a whisper)  
“If it ever…  
if it ever comes down to…  
me or the baby…”

She pulls back —  
forces herself to meet his eyes —  
even though hers are swimming, even though her throat burns.

**JEN:** (voice shaking)  
“Pick the baby.  
Pick our child.  
Save them.  
Even if it means losing me.”

Jeff’s heart shatters —  
absolutely, utterly shatters.

He reaches for her —  
cups her face in both hands, holding her like she’s already halfway to heaven.

Cremeans: (hoarse)  
“Jen…”

But she shakes her head —  
stubborn, fierce, clear.

**JEN:** (stronger now)  
“I’m serious.  
This is my choice.  
This is my vow.  
This is my gift.  
If you ever have to choose — choose life.  
Choose our baby.”

Jeff closes his eyes —  
because it’s too much to look at her,  
too much to hold this impossible, perfect, burning love.

He presses his forehead to hers —  
breath shaking —  
trying to memorize her in this moment.

Cremeans: (whispering)  
“You are the bravest woman God ever made.”

Jen smiles —  
small, broken, beautiful.

**JEN:** (softly)  
“I just love you.  And I love them.  Even before they exist.  And that's what love does.  It lays down its life when it has to.”

Jeff pulls her close —  so close — as if he could fuse her heartbeat to his own.

And together, under the vast, endless sky, they build an altar out of their love.  One that costs everything.  One that will never be forgotten.

**TAHITI – ISLET – THE Dream Beneath the Stars**

They lie side-by-side —  
naked, still damp from rain and ocean and love,  
the sleeping bag half-dried beneath them, forgotten now.

Above them —  
the sky stretches wider than any cathedral,  
thick with stars.

The Milky Way spills across the blackness like a river of light.  
So vast, so fierce, so impossibly beautiful it almost hurts to look at it.

There are no cities.  
No campfires.  
No lamps.

Only the hush of the ocean lapping the shore —  
slow, steady, eternal —  
and the faint, living music of the wind through the palms.

Jen’s hand finds Jeff’s.  
Their fingers tangle —  
a slow, instinctive weave,  
like roots growing under the surface.

Neither speaks.  
There’s nothing left to say.  
Every word has already been spoken.  
Every promise already carved into the night air.

They just breathe —  
together —  
feeling their hearts sync into the same slow, heavy rhythm.

Cremeans (internally):  
This is it.  
This is forever.  
Right here.  
Right now.  
Naked.  
Unafraid.  
Underneath the living heavens.  
My wife.  
My life.  
My whole story, just beginning.

Jen turns her face slightly —  
nuzzles against his shoulder —  
lets out a soft sigh that carries all the weight of love, and hope, and fierce quiet joy.

Above them, the Milky Way hums on.  
And somewhere far beyond it,  
God smiles —  
seeing what two people have dared to build in the middle of nowhere,  
with nothing but faith, and bodies, and love.

They drift —  
slowly, sweetly —  
into sleep.

Into the dream they just made real.

Extensive Narrative Summary of the Honeymoon – Jeff and Jen Cremeans

---

Setting and Setup

- Time: 1994.
    
- Location: Tahiti (initially at the resort, later to a private islet).
    
- Newlyweds: Jeff and Jen Cremeans.
    
- Tone: Newly married, sexually inexperienced but fiercely devoted Christian couple navigating new intimacy with joy, awkwardness, wonder, and respect.
    

The honeymoon is not a fantasy of instant sexual prowess.  
It’s two good-hearted young adults fumbling, growing, learning how to honor each other in nakedness and joy.

Their days are split between:

- Exploring each other sexually (with growing skill and trust).
    
- Talking about their futures — children, money, homebuilding, spiritual priorities.
    
- Learning each other's rhythms — emotionally, spiritually, sexually.
    
- Exploring the physical world around them — Tahiti, the ocean, a deserted islet.
    

---

Major Events Timeline

---

1. Resort Days – Private Room Exploration

- First nights after the wedding are spent in a resort hotel.
    
- Their sexual experiences are clumsy but honest.
    
- Multiple rounds of intercourse — awkward but joyful — as they both discover and encourage each other.
    

Key conversations include:

- Jeff explaining his financial status (~$30,000/month income).
    
- Jen grappling with the magnitude of his career.
    
- Long talks about the band’s members, morality, marriage values, and their dreams of family life.
    
- Jen revealing her fierce intention to breastfeed naturally and to give birth without drugs if possible.
    
- The "baby name" conversation starts — and jokes about needing more understanding of pregnancy and bodies.
    

---

2. Early Sex Scenes (Hotel Room – Multiple Rounds)

First Sexual Encounters

- Context: Fumbling, tender, intensely emotional.
    
- Style: Slow intercourse; Jeff cautious about hurting Jen.
    
- Unique Details:
    

- First mutual orgasms are clumsy but joyful.
    
- Kissing is constant, slow, exploratory.
    
- Jen initiates further sessions with patience and playful hints (nudging her breasts toward him, etc.).
    

---

Second and Third Intercourses

- Context: Building confidence but still awkward.
    
- Highlights:
    

- Jen tries giving oral sex for the first time — struggling with the taste and texture of semen.
    
- Jeff reassures her — celebrating her effort and love, not treating any difficulty as failure.
    
- Mutual kindness and slow physical adjustment dominate these sessions.
    

---

3. Boat and Islet Trip – The Desert Island Adventure

- Jeff charters a private boat to take them to an uninhabited islet.
    
- Both strip nude immediately upon arrival — embracing the Edenic, Biblical feel of the place.
    
- They experience a full day and night completely alone on the islet, camping, making love, surviving together.
    

---

4. Major Sex Scenes on the Islet

Beach Lovemaking (Sunlight Scene)

- Context:
    

- They prepare a sleeping bag on the white sand to prevent sand injury.
    
- First time making love fully outdoors, under the sun, exposed to nature.
    

- Style:
    

- Very slow, sweat-soaked, incredibly tender.
    
- Emotional stillness after penetration — lying together, stuck together by sweat and heat.
    

- Unique Notes:
    

- Jen feels totally at peace being naked under God's sky.
    
- Jeff treasures her without rush.
    
- Holy, timeless feeling.
    

---

Rainstorm Lovemaking (Thunderstorm Scene)

- Context:
    

- A massive tropical storm hits mid-afternoon.
    
- They are caught naked in torrential rain, deafened by thunder.
    

- Style:
    

- Fierce, urgent, wild.
    
- They escalate their lovemaking to "match the storm" — passionate, energetic.
    

- Unique Notes:
    

- Cathartic emotional release through physical intensity.
    
- Deep emotional bonding afterward.
    

---

Post-Storm Snuggling (No Immediate Sex, Deep Bonding)

- After the storm passes, they sit in a small freshwater rivulet.
    
- Splashing each other, laughing, rinsing off sweat, salt, and rainwater.
    
- Emotional intimacy deepens significantly here.
    
- No immediate intercourse — just connection.
    

---

5. Post-Storm Reflections and Family Dreams

- Jen and Jeff discuss future children openly.
    
- Jen admits fears about small frame, childbirth struggles.
    
- Jeff remains endlessly patient, supportive, and promises to be there at every second.
    
- Jen bravely insists: If it comes down to me or the baby, save the baby.
    

- Jeff is shattered by the love in that statement, but he accepts it.
    

---

Sexual Growth Summary

Over the course of the honeymoon:

- From Fumbling to Confidence:
    

- Early intercourse scenes show awkwardness, minor pain, mutual patience.
    
- By the island scenes, they are moving in sync — bodies and hearts attuned.
    

- From Shyness to Boldness:
    

- Jen initiates more physicality as her confidence grows.
    
- Jeff grows more comfortable exploring her body lovingly.
    

- From Inexperience to Mutual Joy:
    

- They celebrate victories — first orgasms, first successful oral attempts, first passionate lovemaking sessions.
    
- They embrace mistakes and laugh through awkwardness together.
    

---

Catalog of Sex Scenes (Chronological)

|Scene|Location|Style|Key Emotional Notes|
|---|---|---|---|
|1. First intercourse|Hotel room|Slow, clumsy, emotional|Virgin exploration, careful, overwhelmed joy.|
|2. Second intercourse (shorter)|Hotel room|Soft, mutual desire|Start of physical ease, slow kisses, mutual need.|
|3. First oral attempt (Jen to Jeff)|Hotel room|Tender, messy|Jen struggles; Jeff treasures her effort.|
|4. Beach lovemaking|Desert islet|Slow, hot, sacred|Holy stillness, emotional nakedness.|
|5. Thunderstorm lovemaking|Islet (rainstorm)|Wild, urgent|Passion matching nature's fury, physical emotional catharsis.|

---

Closing Emotional State Before Transition

By the end of their Tahiti stay:

- They are bonded deeply:  
    Spiritually, physically, emotionally — no secrets between them anymore.
    
- They are ready to face real life:  
    Parenthood, homes, long years ahead —  
    with faith, laughter, fierce loyalty, and love stronger than their fears.
    

---

(End of Extensive Summary.)

---

Ready for What's Next

This gives you:

- A full narrative map of the honeymoon.
    
- A sex catalog without sleaze, focused on character development.
    
- A solid clean closure point for Phase 1 of the story.
    

---

The Tokyo Transition:

1. Setting:

- City: Tokyo, Japan.
    
- Time: About a week into their marriage.
    
- Mood:
    

- Newness fading into stability.
    
- Wide-eyed wonder (Tokyo is overwhelming for anyone in the 1990s).
    
- A pivot from intimate world to public world.

---

2. Situation:

Jeff Cremeans has to actually work.  
He's there to finalize negotiations for Commuted’s first Japanese licensing deal (or concert tour, or dual deal — you can pick later).  
It’s serious, complex, cutthroat.

For the first time:

- Jen is not just the beloved wife.
    
- She’s a fly on the wall — watching Jeff in his other natural habitat.
    

---

3. How Jeff Acts:

- In Business:
    

- No fumbling.
    
- No bashfulness.
    
- Lethally calm.
    
- Surgical precision.
    
- Tactical patience.
    
- Absolute steel when necessary.
    

- With Her:
    

- Gentle side-glances.
    
- Silent reassurances.
    
- Protectiveness sharpened into strategy — he knows she’s watching, and he doesn’t want her to worry.
    

To Jen, he is totally recognizable — but magnified.

She will think:

“This is the same man who kisses my forehead and cries at hymns.  
But when it’s war out here —  
he fights without raising his voice.”

And she will fall even deeper in love,  
because now she sees the whole man.

---

4. Emotional Stakes:

- Jen sees:
    

- His competence.
    
- His ability to protect not just her, but a whole crew of reckless artists.
    
- His tactical mind at full strength.
    

- Jeff shows:
    

- That his love for her never blinks — even when he’s wielding sharp tools professionally.
    
- That his strength is not about pushing people around — it’s about holding ground when others would surrender.
    

---

5. Bonus Ideas for Emotional Texture:

- Language barrier scenes — watching Jeff navigate without arrogance, respecting the local culture, doing it right.
    
- Late-night exhausted cuddling in a Tokyo hotel,  
    where Jen runs her hands across his shoulders and realizes:  
    he's carrying the weight of ten other lives, and he never complains.
    
- Private whispered conversations where Jeff vents just a little to Jen —  
    because she’s the only safe place he has.
    
- Maybe Jeff pulls off an incredible deal — and Jen is proud in the way a woman is proud not of a trophy husband, but of a warrior.
    

---

Summary of Your New Phase

|Part|Mood|Purpose|
|---|---|---|
|Tokyo Arrival|Awe, Wonder|Shift from purely private to a public world together.|
|Watching Jeff Work|Reverence, New Eyes|Jen sees the full warrior side of her husband.|
|Aftermath|Deepened Intimacy|Emotional and physical love deepens because trust deepens.|

---

Final Thought Before We Launch It:

This Tokyo shift would make the next intimacy scenes even better —  
because now Jen isn’t just loving the man who caresses her at night.  
She’s loving the man who carries empires on his back by day — and still comes home humble.

That’s real romance.  
That’s earned passion.  
That’s a love story with legs that can walk into 60 years of marriage.

Narita International Airport, 8:00 AM — Tokyo Arrival

The wheels kiss the tarmac with a gentle jolt —  
first rubber, then steel, then bone.  
Flight 837 from Los Angeles rolls down the endless gray of Narita’s runways,  
caught in a strange, low light.

Japan at 8:00 AM feels different.

Not just because of the time zone,  
or the exhaustion clinging to the edges of Jeff Cremeans' brain.  
Not just because of the language on every sign — kanji, hiragana, unreadable rivers of black ink flowing across white surfaces.

But because Tokyo hums.  
Even at sunrise.

---

Jeff glances sideways at Jen.

She's pressing her nose against the small, oval window like a kid.  
Still barefoot from the flight, jeans rolled at the ankle, an old Cincinnati Reds sweatshirt stretched across her body.  
No makeup.  
Hair in a messy bun.

She looks like home.  
She looks like every future he ever wanted.

---

The overhead chimes sound.  
Doors to manual.  
Prepare for arrival.

The plane jerks a little as they taxi toward the terminal.

Jen laughs quietly — the pure kind of laugh you only make when you're alive in a new world —  
and says:

"We’re here. We really made it."

Jeff smiles tiredly, stretching out a cramp in his lower back.

"Yeah, baby. We’re here. Welcome to Tokyo."

---

Inside Narita

The airport smells sterile —  
plastic and metal and recycled air —  
but there's a sweetness, too:  
a faint trail of brewed tea somewhere beyond the customs desks.

The place buzzes without roaring.  
Polite motion everywhere.  
Attendants bowing slightly.  
Signs pointing in two, three languages.

"Arrivals — 出発"

Jen clutches her little backpack to her chest like a kid on a field trip.

Jeff tugs their one heavy suitcase off the carousel.

They don't talk much —  
just move together through the maze of immigration counters and luggage inspection with sleepy, stunned teamwork.

It is 8:00 AM.  
They are 6,400 miles from Ohio.  
And Tokyo doesn’t care who they are.

Which is perfect.  
Because for a little while —  
they’re not anyone but two kids in love, with a shared name and a full life packed into one blue Samsonite suitcase.

---

Small Details Along the Way

- Jen stares too long at a vending machine full of hot coffee cans and blinking lights.
    
- Jeff keeps his arm slightly in front of her without thinking — protective, casual, instinctive.
    
- A group of businessmen rush past, briefcases flapping, their suits perfect even after a flight.
    
- Somewhere, an older woman in uniform hands them a bright orange flyer: Welcome to Japan. Respect local customs. Bow before handshake.
    

Jeff folds it neatly without reading it.  
They'll be respectful.  
They'll be themselves.

---

Final Steps Out of Narita

The glass sliding doors whoosh open.

And for the first time —  
the true breath of Tokyo hits them:  
humid, electric, smelling faintly of exhaust and seawater and cherry blossoms even though it's early summer.

Jen stops for just a second, absorbing it.

Jeff stands behind her, one hand on the suitcase, one hand on the small of her back.

Neither says anything.

The city is waiting.  
The life is waiting.  
And so is the first real test of who they are outside the cocoon.

---

Let’s Land This Scene: Tokyo, Narita Airport — On the Ground

---

The jet bridge smells like air conditioning and possibility.  
And something else —  
a kind of floral antiseptic.  
The scent of an airport that runs on politeness and bleach.

Jen adjusts her carry-on over one shoulder and takes her first full step into Japan.

She stops.

"Oh my gosh," she whispers, not out of reverence —  
but from actual shock.

"It’s so… clean. Like, really clean.  
And nobody’s yelling.  
And the signs make sense.  
And where’s the chaos?*"

Jeff’s too tired to answer.  
He just gives a half-smile and adjusts his jacket.

---

They move through customs like they’re part of a dance they never rehearsed:

- Passport.
    
- Stamp.
    
- Bow.
    
- Nod.
    
- Thank you.
    
- Keep walking.
    

Everything is quiet.  
Everything is so fast,  
and so calm,  
that it almost makes them feel like they're doing something wrong just by existing at normal American volume.

---

Then it hits Jen again —  
the scale.

Not the size of the airport.  
The size of the people.

"Oh my gosh, babe…" she whispers, leaning in.  
"I'm tall."  
"Like, actual tall."

She isn’t.  
She’s 5'4", on a good day.  
But here?  
The crowd swirls around her in a gentle tide of black hair and bowed heads,  
and for once in her life, she is not the smallest person in the room.

She turns and looks at Jeff —  
6'1", Midwestern, square-shouldered, tired as death —  
and suddenly he looks like a tower walking through a model village.

"Jeff," she hisses, "you’re a skyscraper."

He grunts.

"I'm a skyscraper with plantar fasciitis and no caffeine. Let’s find the exit."

 ---

They followed the signs toward ground transportation, passing under polished white signs, down escalators lined with brushed steel.

Ahead, the vending machines appeared.

Not just a few.  
A wall of them.

Coffee cans.  
Cigarettes.  
Plastic-wrapped rice balls.  
Cold beer.  
And tucked between them —  
small machines with cartoon covers, blinking red lights, and blurred-out adult material.

Jen stopped.

She stared.

She turned to Jeff, slack-jawed.

This is an airport, she said.

Jeff adjusted his shoulder strap, barely glancing.

Welcome to Japan, he said.  
This is one of our best markets.

Jen pointed with her whole hand.

That one is selling beer.  
That one is selling cigarettes.  
That one is selling… I don’t even know what that is.

Jeff grunted.

Porn. Probably softcore. It’s legal if it’s pixelated. Different cultural standards.

She blinked at him.

You’re kidding.

I’m not even warmed up yet, he said.  
You should see the Shibuya vending machines.

She muttered under her breath.

I can't even buy Tylenol from a vending machine at home.

Jeff laughed quietly.

Here? You can buy a bottle of whiskey, a magazine, and a hot meal at the same corner.  
And nobody blinks.

They moved again, weaving around travelers in pressed suits.  
Jen kept sneaking glances back at the machines as if they might start walking.

She tugged on his sleeve.

Babe… are we sure this isn’t a fever dream?

Jeff smiled without opening his eyes all the way.

Jet lag, vending machines, and public decency codes.  
Nope.  
You're officially in Tokyo.

---

They shuffled toward the exit, pulling their battered suitcase behind them.

Jen pointed discreetly at the man across the terminal.

**JEN:**  
Hey, babe. Maybe you should ask that soldier where he got his Mountain Dew.

Jeff turned his head, tracking where she was pointing.

The man stood proud, backpack slung over one shoulder, Mountain Dew in hand, wearing a crisp green Class A uniform like armor against the world.

Jeff slowed.

**JEFF:** (gently)  
That’s not a soldier.  That’s a Marine.  They’d take offense if you got that wrong.   
Marines are Marines from the day they enlist to the day they die.  It’s not just a job. It’s a blood oath.

Jen blinked, absorbing that.

Jeff adjusted the suitcase handle, gaze lingering for a moment longer on the Marine’s back.

**JEFF:** (lower, almost to himself)  
Remind me sometime to tell you about my friend Tim Wright.  Persian Gulf, '91.  He didn’t even have to enlist.  He volunteered.  Went halfway across the world for people he didn’t even know.

Jen reached out and touched his hand, squeezing. No more words needed between them. They kept moving, toward the humid Tokyo air,  toward whatever waited next,  
carrying a small, private salute with them.

---

Jeff hesitated, then peeled off from Jen and the suitcase, moving toward the young Marine. The Marine caught the approach instantly —  shifted his seabag, squared his shoulders, heels clicking together without even thinking.

Jeff stopped a respectful distance away, hands loose at his sides.

**JEFF:**  
Excuse me, Marine.  Where'd you get the Mountain Dew?

The Marine blinked once, then answered with mechanical precision.

**Marine**: 
(sharp, respectful)  
Sir, I obtained it at the FamilyMart kiosk, Sir.  Terminal 2, near Gate 47, Sir.  They have a limited American selection, Sir.  Recommend moving fast, Sir, they sell out quick, Sir.

Jeff nodded once, covering a grin.

**JEFF:**  
Appreciate it, Marine. Carry on.

**Marine**: (snapping a crisp nod)  
Aye aye, Sir.

Jeff turned back toward Jen, who was stifling a laugh behind her hand.

---

They rejoined the current of humanity, suitcase rattling behind them.

**JEN:** (whispering, teasing)  
I think you got Sired half a dozen times in thirty seconds.  You gonna be okay?

**JEFF:** (grinning tiredly)  
It’s good for me.  Keeps my ego down.  Reminds me some people still believe in standing straight and speaking clear.

They kept walking.  Somewhere beyond the escalators, a FamilyMart waited — and maybe, just maybe, salvation in a green plastic bottle.

---

**JEFF:** (mock serious)  
We're going to get the Holy Grail now.  
And you're going to get a diet one.  
And all will be right with the world.

Jen snorted, bumping his hip with hers.

**JEN:**  
You're delirious.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
No, I'm a prophet.  There’s a FamilyMart kiosk near Gate 47.  The Marine said so.  And if we don't find it soon, I’m going to start seeing visions.

They trudged through the airport, surrounded by businessmen in perfect black suits, tiny women with careful hair, orderly lines moving like rivers.

Jen shook her head, smiling to herself.

**JEN:**  
Imagine explaining this to our parents.  “Yeah, our first adventure in Japan?  It was a pilgrimage for neon sugar water.”

**JEFF:**  
It’s not sugar water.  It’s courage in a bottle.  It's hope.  It's America.

**JEN:** (laughing)  
You are so weird sometimes.  I love you.

**JEFF:**  
Right back at you, babe.  Now march.

They pressed onward, eyes scanning for the green glow of salvation.

---

They walked side by side, the FamilyMart glowing faintly ahead like a promised land. Jeff squeezed her hand lightly.

**JEFF:**  
So when we get back to the States…  what exactly are you going to tell your parents we did in Tahiti?

Jen laughed under her breath, half-delirious, half-giddy.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Uh… that we saw a lot of beaches?  That we admired the natural beauty?  That we worked on our tans?

**JEFF:** (teasing)  
Worked on our tans?  That's what we're calling it?

**JEN:** (mock innocence)  
I mean… we did spend a lot of time outside.  Mostly naked.  Mostly sweaty.

Jeff chuckled, his chest rumbling low.

**JEFF:**  
You realize your mom’s going to look me dead in the eye and know exactly what we did.

**JEN:** (laughing)  
Probably.  But she’s Baptist.  She’s just going to pretend she doesn’t know.

**JEFF:**  
Blessed are the deniers.

They reached the FamilyMart, doors sliding open with a soft hiss. The bright cold of the refrigerated cases washed over them like a tiny miracle.

**JEFF:** (mock reverent)  
Holy ground.

Jen leaned against him, still laughing, still clutching his hand.

---

Jeff leaned down, grabbing a bottle of Mountain Dew from the cooler, twisting it in his hand like a relic retrieved from a myth.

Jen snatched a Diet one, tapping the cap against his bottle lightly.

**JEN:** (grinning wickedly)  
Besides…  if you have me knocked up by the time we visit my parents,  all will be forgiven.

Jeff froze mid-sip.

**JEFF:** (choking a little)  
Oh.  Oh, that's the plan now?

Jen shrugged, sipping her Diet Mountain Dew like it was the most natural thing in the world.

**JEN:** (mock innocent)  
I'm just saying.  If I’m glowing and hormonal and craving pickles by Thanksgiving,  
my mom’s going to forget we ever disappeared to a tropical island half-naked.

Jeff shook his head, grinning helplessly.

**JEFF:**  
You are trouble.

**JEN:** (beaming)  
You married me anyway.

They clinked bottles again, plastic against plastic, tired against tired, love against love,  and drank.

---

They followed the signs, dragging their small mountain of baggage toward the transportation center.  Getting from Narita to downtown Tokyo was almost laughably easy.  Polite signs.  Clear instructions.  Smiling attendants pointing the way to the trains and shuttle services.  They boarded the Narita Express without fanfare, collapsed into the reserved seats, the hum of the tracks soothing and foreign at the same time.

Jen pressed her face to the wide train window, eyes wide, stunned into silence.  Outside, the suburbs blurred past — clean, tight, orderly — and then, as the train sped onward, the density began to grow.  The buildings huddled together.  Then stacked higher.  
Then pressed tighter.  Mile after mile after mile of endless city.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
This is…this is insane.  It just keeps going.

Jeff leaned back, arms crossed, watching her more than the window.

**JEFF:**  
Biggest city you’ve ever been to before this was Washington, right?

**JEN:** (nodding)  
Yeah.  And that was crazy enough.  This is…I don't even have words.

Jeff smiled faintly, exhaustion pulling his features down but pride lifting his voice.

**JEFF:**  
I’ve been to London.  Moscow.  Berlin.  New York.  L.A.  Tokyo…Tokyo takes the cake.

Jen sat back slowly, letting the endless skyline swallow her.

**JEN:**  
I can't even tell where one town stops and another starts.  It’s just… people.  And lights.  And buildings.  Forever.

**JEFF:**  
Forty million people.  Give or take.  All stacked up and moving at the same time.

**JEN:** (half to herself)  
It’s like another planet.

The train hummed onward, carrying them deeper into the heart of the machine.  Deeper into the world that didn't slow down, didn't explain itself, didn't wait for newcomers.  Jen reached for Jeff’s hand without thinking.  He gave it to her instantly.  They watched Tokyo unfold together, two small humans hurtling toward the beating center of the biggest thing they had ever seen.

The Narita Express slowed as they approached Tokyo Station, the massive hub swallowing them whole without ceremony.  They stepped off the train, tugging their suitcase into a current of human beings so dense, so fast-moving, it felt like a living river.  Jen tightened her grip on Jeff’s hand, her eyes darting everywhere at once.

Neon lights.  Billboards stacked ten stories high.  Music blaring from store windows.  Thousands of people — in suits, in uniforms, in schoolgirl outfits — flowing around them like water around rocks.

**JEN:** (staring, overwhelmed)  
This isn’t a city.  It’s another planet.  We’re on Mars.

Jeff smiled tiredly, guiding her through the crowd with practiced patience.

**JEFF:**  
Welcome to downtown Tokyo.

Jen twisted around, trying to take it all in, craning her neck to look up at the skyscrapers that seemed to tilt over them.

**JEN:** (half laughing, half terrified)  
There’s no sky.  There’s just… buildings.  And lights.  And noise.

**JEFF:**  
You get used to it.  Sort of.

They dodged between businessmen moving like a military drill team, slid past a line of taxis, and edged toward the station exit.  Jen shook her head slowly, dazed.

**JEN:**  
How do people even live like this?  How do you find your own breath in all of this?

Jeff chuckled under his breath.

**JEFF:**  
Same way you find it back home.  One step at a time.  One street at a time.  You pick your line and you keep walking.

They broke free of the station, stepping into open air — if you could call it open — surrounded by a canyon of glass and steel stretching into the sky.

Jen stared up again.

**JEN:**  
If we get lost, we’re just gonna die here, aren’t we?

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Nah.  Tokyo’s the safest city on Earth.  You’ll die of embarrassment before you die of anything else.

She squeezed his hand tighter, still spinning slowly on her heel, overwhelmed but grinning anyway.

**JEN:**  
Mars.  
I’m telling you.  
This is Mars.

Jeff tugged the suitcase forward.

**JEFF:**  
Then let’s find the American Embassy on Mars.  
Or at least our hotel.

They moved into the crowd again, two tiny dots swallowed by the heartbeat of the biggest city on Earth.

The taxi dropped them off in front of the hotel, a towering slab of glass and steel that disappeared into the clouds above.

Jen craned her neck, squinting upward, her mouth slightly open.

**JEN:**  
Does it ever end?  
I mean…  
seriously, does it stop somewhere up there?

Jeff rolled their suitcase onto the curb, chuckling low in his throat.

**JEFF:**  
Welcome to vertical living, babe.

Jen kept staring, staggered.

**JEN:**  
How can we even afford this?

Jeff shrugged like it was nothing, even though he looked as tired as she felt.

**JEFF:**  
Favorable currency exchange.  
Plus…  
a lot of this is getting written off as a business expense.

He bumped her gently with his elbow.

**JEFF:**  
You wanna come with me?  
Maybe have a business dinner?  
Talk to some of the guys?  
They seem pretty nice.

Jen tore her eyes away from the impossible height of the building to squint at him.

**JEN:**  
Business dinner?

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Yeah.  
Especially the couple I met in Los Angeles.  
Good people.  
Think you'd like ‘em.

Jen leaned into him, head against his shoulder for just a second.

**JEN:**  
As long as I don’t have to pretend to know anything about music contracts or whatever you’re doing…  
I’m in.

Jeff kissed the top of her head without even thinking about it.

**JEFF:**  
You being there’s good enough.  
Trust me.

The doorman bowed, and they rolled their battered suitcase inside — two small figures swallowed by marble, chandeliers, and the soft hum of luxury.

The world could keep spinning crazy outside.  
But inside, it was just them.  
Still married.  
Still in this together.

The front desk clerk bowed, handed over two slim key cards in a pristine envelope, and murmured something about "the Honeymoon Suite" with a careful smile.

Jeff took the envelope, nodded politely, and turned back to Jen.

**JEFF:**  
Seventy-fourth floor, babe.  
Top of the world.

Jen looked past him toward the elevators — a bank of chrome doors that gleamed like launchpads.

**JEN:** (nervous laughter)  
That’s… really high.  
Really, really high.

Jeff pressed the call button.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
It’s a rocket ride, too.  
Just hang on.

The elevator doors whooshed open.  
They stepped inside a capsule of glass and mirrors, the kind of design that made you very aware of exactly how fast you were about to go.

The doors slid shut.  
There was a faint ding.

And then they launched.

The elevator surged upward like it had been shot from a cannon.  
The ground disappeared beneath them so fast Jen felt her knees wobble.

**JEN:** (yelping, half-joking, half-serious)  
I’m gonna pee myself.  
I'm serious.  
This is bad.

Jeff laughed, steadying her by the waist.

**JEFF:**  
Bladder control, babe.  
Focus.

**JEN:** (gasping)  
You say that like it’s easy when your organs are getting rearranged.

The lights marking each floor ticked up faster than she could blink —  
20, 30, 40, 50 —  
until finally the numbers slowed and the elevator glided to a smooth, precise stop.

74

The doors slid open with a whisper. Jeff guided her out, still grinning.

**JEFF:**  
See?  
Piece of cake.

**JEN:** (mock glaring)  
Cake doesn’t make you feel like you’re about to black out.

They stood in a silent hallway lined with thick carpet and elegant lighting.  
At the end, a double door waited with a small polished plaque:  
The Honeymoon Suite.

Jeff held out the key card like a magician presenting a final trick.

**JEFF:**  
After you, Mrs. Cremeans.

Jen rolled her eyes, heart pounding from the ride and from the simple weight of being here —  
so far from home,  
so high above the ground,  
so deep inside a life she barely dared to believe was real.

She swiped the card.

The door unlocked with a soft click.  
And the whole world — Tokyo, their marriage, their future — stretched out on the other side.

Jen stepped through the door and stopped cold, suitcase forgotten, eyes wide.

This wasn’t Tahiti.  
And it sure wasn’t the Sheraton back in Cincinnati.

The room stretched out in front of them —  
sleek, minimal, almost surgically clean.  
Soft lighting tucked into the ceiling.  
Low furniture, precise and modular, almost futuristic.  
A platform bed set low to the floor, framed by translucent screens instead of a headboard.  
The window — a wall of glass —  
gave a dizzying, heart-stopping view of Tokyo sprawling beneath them in every direction.

It wasn’t cozy.  
It wasn’t tropical.  
It was… efficient.  
Disciplined.  
Utterly, breathtakingly foreign.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
This…  
this doesn't look like the Sheraton.

Jeff set the suitcase down carefully, glancing around, taking it in.

**JEFF:**  
Yeah.  
Different vibe.

Jen walked forward slowly, fingertips brushing across a lacquered wood desk that looked too pretty to actually touch.

**JEN:**  
In Tahiti, everything was wood and flowers and ocean breeze.  
This feels like…  
like we’re living inside a really expensive calculator.

Jeff chuckled, tugging at his shirt collar.

**JEFF:**  
Welcome to the Japanese version of a honeymoon suite.  
Minimalism.  
Respect for space.  
No clutter.

Jen turned slowly in a circle, taking it all in.

**JEN:**  
I mean… it's beautiful.  
It's just…  
cold.

Jeff watched her, hands in his pockets, understanding more than he could say.

**JEFF:**  
It's not cold.  
It’s different.  
Different rhythm.  
Different rules.

Jen pressed her hand to the glass, looking out at the endless city lights pulsing far below.

**JEN:** (softly)  
Mars.

Jeff came up behind her, wrapping his arms around her waist, resting his chin on her shoulder.

**JEFF:**  
Not Mars.  
Tokyo.  
You’ll see.

They stood there together for a long minute, letting the city hum beneath them,  
letting the strangeness settle,  
letting themselves belong to this new place — if only for a little while.

Jeff slipped off his jacket, tossing it over the low-backed chair by the window.

**JEFF:**  
I know you like sushi, Jen.  
And I know you're wiped out.  
But let's do something authentic for breakfast.  
Let’s get a real Japanese breakfast down in the restaurant,  
then we’ll come back up here and just crash.  
I promise — I’ll keep my hands off you.  
Scout’s honor.

Jen dropped onto the edge of the low bed, still looking half-dazed.

**JEN:** (grinning lazily)  
Are you sure you’re gonna keep your hands off me?  
Because…  
I wouldn’t mind.

Jeff snorted, rubbing his face with both hands like he was trying to stay awake by sheer willpower.

**JEFF:**  
I’m sure.  
I’m dead to the world, babe.  
You could put a five-course meal in front of me,  
and I’d still fall asleep in the miso soup.

Jen flopped backward onto the bed, arms sprawled out.

**JEN:**  
Fine.  
Authentic breakfast.  
Then death nap.  
Lead the way, General.

Jeff grabbed the room key and their passports from the table, checked his wallet out of sheer habit, and held out his hand.

**JEFF:**  
Come on, Mrs. Cremeans.  
Let’s go pretend we’re cultured.  
At least until the rice knocks us out.

Jen groaned, but she grabbed his hand anyway, letting him pull her up.

Together, they stumbled back toward the elevator —  
two Americans running on love, sugar, and fumes,  
chasing one last piece of the world before sleep finally claimed them.


The hostess bowed politely and guided them to a small table near the window.  
The restaurant was quiet, filled with soft clinking sounds and the muted conversations of early risers.  
Outside, the city glittered in the morning haze.

Jen picked up the menu and scanned it, eyebrows knitting together.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
This menu…  
this breakfast…  
these choices…  
this doesn't look like we're in the United States anymore.

Jeff smiled across the table, rolling his neck like it was made of concrete.

**JEFF:**  
That's part of the upside.  
And sometimes the downside of traveling outside the States.  
There’s gonna be some stuff you really like.  
And some stuff… you’ll just survive.

Jen leaned in, pointing discreetly at a few items.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
What's this? Grilled fish for breakfast?  
Miso soup?  
Pickles?

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Pretty standard.  
They do lighter, cleaner breakfasts here.  
Protein, fermented stuff, rice, miso, green tea.  
No pancakes drowning in syrup.  
No bacon grease party.

Jen made a face like she wasn’t sure if she was impressed or terrified.

**JEFF:**  
You might like the tamago — the sweet egg omelet.  
Or the grilled salmon.  
They do rice here better than anywhere on Earth.  
And the miso's actually pretty good.  
Warm, salty, wakes you up a little.

Jen wrinkled her nose, trying not to look too skeptical.

**JEN:**  
So you're saying no Captain Crunch today.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
No Captain Crunch.  
But if you’re brave, you might find your new favorite thing.

She sighed dramatically, setting the menu down.

**JEN:**  
Okay.  
I’ll be brave.  
Order for me.  
Just… no raw squid, okay?  
I’m not emotionally prepared for that.

**JEFF:** (mock solemn)  
No raw squid.  
I promise.

He flagged down the server with a small bow,  
ready to lead his wife into one more small adventure —  
one bowl of miso soup at a time.

Jeff gave the order in slow, careful English, paired with polite nods.  
The server bowed slightly, scribbling quickly, and moved away without fuss.

Jeff leaned across the table, lowering his voice.

**JEFF:**  
I got us the tamago — sweet egg — and one of the grilled salmon.  
We’ll split it.

Jen looked relieved she didn’t have to make any choices just yet.  
She toyed with her chopsticks, still looking around like she was dreaming.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
I’m probably really, really hungry.  
And I’m betting you’re really, really hungry.  
So I got extra.

Jen nodded, a little dazed.

**JEFF:**  
Besides…  
these are Japanese-sized portions.  
Not American-sized portions.

**JEN:** (dry)  
Meaning I’m gonna need three breakfasts to make one back home.

**JEFF:**  
Basically.

They both sagged into their chairs at the same time, their bodies finally admitting just how far they'd been pushed.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
I don’t even care if it’s weird.  
I just want warm food and a real bed.

**JEFF:** (smiling tiredly)  
Coming right up, babe.  
One brave breakfast…  
and then we crash like the good little tourists we are.

The smell of grilled fish and warm rice drifted from the kitchen,  
soft and unfamiliar,  
but somehow comforting in its own way.

The plates arrived in a silent, practiced ballet —  
set down gently in front of them with a polite bow from the server.

One plate held neat slices of tamago, glossy and golden, stacked like tiny bricks.  
The other carried a portion of grilled salmon, pink and delicate, beside a perfect scoop of white rice and a few small pickled vegetables arranged with absurd precision.

Jen stared at it all, eyes wide.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
This looks utterly weird and unfamiliar…  
but it smells really good.  
  
It even smells… vaguely American.  
Like… Sunday morning at somebody else's house.

Jeff picked up his chopsticks, adjusting them in his fingers with the careful patience of a man who had done this a few times before.

**JEFF:**  
Told you.  
Warm food is warm food.  
Doesn’t matter what continent you're on.

Jen poked the tamago cautiously.

**JEN:**  
It’s sweet?

**JEFF:**  
Like breakfast cake.  
Trust me.  
You’ll like it.

She took a small bite, eyes widening in surprise.

**JEN:**  
Oh wow.  
That’s… actually really good.

Jeff grinned, taking a piece of the salmon for himself.

**JEFF:**  
See?  
Different rhythm.  
Same idea.  
Feed your body.  
Feed your soul.

Jen chewed thoughtfully, the unfamiliar tastes unfolding in slow, simple layers.  
Rice.  
Egg.  
Salmon.  
Salt.  
Warmth.

Outside the window, Tokyo thundered past at full speed.  
But inside, at their little table, time slowed down just enough for them to belong.

---

Jen picked at her rice, still trying to make sense of the meal, then leaned across the table a little closer, whispering like they were sharing some great international secret.

**JEN:**  
So the Japanese like using seafood a lot more than pig, right?  
Not so much on the bacon and sausage here?

Jeff wiped a little bit of rice off his lip with a napkin, nodding.

**JEFF:**  
Right.  
Pork’s around, but not at every meal.  
Way more seafood.  
Way cleaner flavors.

Jen stabbed a piece of salmon thoughtfully, chewing on a bigger question.

**JEN:**  
Okay, real talk.  
Am I gonna fall out of bed over their version of sushi?  
Like… is it going to wreck me?  
Am I going to be ruined for the rest of my life?

Jeff laughed under his breath, low and warm.

**JEFF:**  
Depends.

**JEN:** (raising an eyebrow)  
On what?

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
On if you’re ready for the real stuff.  
Because sushi here?  
It’s not California rolls with fake crab and avocado.  
It’s clean.  
Sharp.  
Simple.  
Like eating the ocean the way God made it.

Jen wrinkled her nose a little.

**JEN:**  
That sounds… scary.

**JEFF:**  
It’s not.  
It’s honest.  
You’ll either love it, or you’ll respect it and go find a plate of teriyaki.  
No shame either way.

Jen chewed slowly, thinking it through.

**JEN:**  
You’re trying to Jedi mind-trick me into being brave, aren't you?

**JEFF:**  
Guilty.

She laughed, shaking her head, and grabbed another piece of tamago, popping it in her mouth with exaggerated bravery.

**JEN:** (mouth full)  
Fine.  
Bring it on.  
Bring on the weird fish.  
Bring on Mars food.  
I can do this.

Jeff smiled across the table at her,  
tired and proud and in love.

---

Surreal.
