Jen was quiet, digesting that, the pulse of the city throbbing around them.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
They might not be what you expect.  None of this life is what you expect.

Jen looked up at him, her face serious but calm — grounded, the way he loved most about her.

**JEN:** (quiet)  
As long as you’re the same man at work…  the same man here, with me…  I’ll be okay.  
I didn’t marry a movie star.  I married you.

Jeff felt something loosen in his chest —  a knot he hadn’t realized he was carrying —  and he kissed the top of her head without even thinking.

**JEFF:** (low, sure)  
And that’s all I ever want to be.

They moved forward again,  into the noise and the lights,  knowing the world ahead might be loud, messy, unpredictable —  but it would always be theirs.

Jeff gave a short, dry laugh, squeezing her shoulder again as they walked.

**JEFF:** (half-smiling)  
You married an accountant, Jen.  
  
You married an accountant.

Jen looked up at him, her smile playing at the edges of her lips.

Jeff shook his head a little, as if reminding her — or maybe reminding himself — exactly who he was.

**JEFF:** (quiet, steady)  
You don't ever have to worry about me.  I'm not a singer.  I'm not a dancer.  I’m not on a record.  I'm not starring in some flashy music video.  I just cut record deals.  I find the opportunities.  I figure out how to turn crazy dreams into honest paychecks.  
Decent profit.  Solid future.

He pulled her a little closer through the crowd, his voice growing a shade more intense.

**JEFF:**  
And when I'm out there, in the middle of their madness…  I'm the one keeping them in check.  Keeping them out of trouble.  Keeping them…  safe from themselves.

Jen absorbed all of it quietly, her hand tightening around his side.

She didn’t just hear the words —  she understood the weight behind them.  The burden he carried that none of his wild, brilliant bandmates ever seemed to notice.

**JEN:** (soft, sure)  
I know.  I see you.

Jeff’s chest loosened again, that same wave of gratitude flooding him.  The kind that came from being seen —  really, truly seen —  without the armor, without the reputation, without the noise.

**JEFF:** (smiling)  
Good.  Because you’re the only person I ever really wanted to see it.

Jen smiled up at him, that wide, endless, boundless smile,  and the city, no matter how bright or loud or endless it felt —  it couldn't outshine the simple, perfect truth of them walking side by side.

Jeff glanced around, taking stock, realizing just how far they'd wandered.  
The neon towers of their hotel were nowhere in sight anymore — swallowed up behind rows of mid-rise buildings, noodle shops, game arcades, and countless blinking signs he couldn’t even begin to translate.

**JEFF:** (chuckling)  
Would you look at that?  
We’ve been walking… what?  
Twenty-five minutes?  
Just shooting the breeze.

Jen grinned up at him, her cheeks a little flushed from the steady pace, but her spirit nowhere near tired.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
Some honeymoon.  
Wandering around lost in Tokyo.

Jeff squeezed her hand, a playful glint in his eye.

**JEFF:**  
Not lost.  
Strategically exploring.

She laughed, bumping his hip with hers.

But even as he joked, something caught Jeff’s eye —  
just up ahead, tucked between two larger, sleeker storefronts.

A narrow doorway.  
A faded noren curtain hanging down over it — deep blue, with simple white kanji characters he couldn't read.  
A faint, delicious smell drifting into the street: rice vinegar, grilled fish, a hint of fresh seaweed.

Inside, he caught a glimpse —  
tiny, wooden counter, maybe a dozen seats total.  
No tourists.  
Only a few locals hunched over plates, eating in silence or murmuring low conversation.

It looked honest.  
It looked real.

**JEFF:** (slowing down)  
Hey.  
This…  
this might be it.

Jen followed his gaze, her nose wrinkling in concentration, catching the smells, the mood, the low steady buzz of something authentic.

**JEN:** (soft, excited)  
It doesn’t look fancy…

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Perfect.  
Hole-in-the-wall.  
Exactly what we wanted.

He steered her gently toward it, stepping out of the flood of sidewalk traffic.

**JEFF:**  
If a city of forty million people has hidden places…  
this feels like one of them.

Jen squeezed his hand back, her eyes bright.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Let’s do it.

Jeff smiled wide, pushed aside the noren with one hand, and led her inside —  
into a tiny world carved out from the endless electric storm,  
where love, adventure, and maybe the best sushi of their lives  
waited just beyond the threshold.

The noren curtain fluttered shut behind them, sealing them inside a space barely larger than a living room.

It was pure Japan.  
Tatami mats lining the edges.  
Dark wood paneling.  
A single long counter worn smooth by decades of use.  
Behind it, two chefs moved with precise, almost sacred efficiency, knives flashing in silence.

The air smelled sharp with vinegar and sea brine, and soft with rice steam.  
Old paper lanterns hung from the ceiling, casting a warm, golden glow.  
The low murmur of conversation was purely Japanese — not a single word of English anywhere.

Jeff felt a small tightening in his gut — not fear, exactly, but awareness.  
This wasn’t for tourists.  
This was the real thing.

He glanced at Jen, who was already smiling wide, taking it all in like she was breathing it.

They were seated at the counter by an older man with silver at his temples and hands so deft they looked carved from oak.  
Menus, hand-written and entirely in kanji, were set gently in front of them.

Jeff rubbed the back of his neck awkwardly, trying to frame how he was going to mime their way through an order without causing an international incident.

But before he could even open his mouth —

A woman appeared from the back.

Late fifties maybe, dressed simply in a dark blue kimono, carrying a tray with two small cups of tea.

She smiled warmly at them, setting the cups down with a small bow — and then said, in the crispest, most flawless California accent Jeff had ever heard:

**Owner’s Wife:** (cheerful)  
Welcome! We’re so happy you found our little shop. You two from the States?

Jeff and Jen froze for a beat, stunned.  
Then Jen’s hand flew to her mouth, stifling a delighted laugh.

Jeff blinked once, twice, then finally managed to speak.

**JEFF:** (grinning wide)  
Uh… yeah.  Yeah, we are.  From Ohio.

The woman smiled even brighter, her face crinkling with kindness.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Oh, wonderful! I grew up in San Diego before moving back here.

(beat, playful)  
You’re in good hands.  Relax.  We’ll take care of you.

Jeff slumped slightly in relief, letting out a breath he didn’t realize he'd been holding. 
He looked over at Jen, who was already grinning at him like she’d won some kind of cosmic bet.

**JEFF:** (muttering under his breath)  
Only you could pull us into a Tokyo sushi place run by someone who sounds like they just left the beach.

Jen laughed, her eyes twinkling.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
See?  Follow the crowd.  Follow the signs.  *Trust* your wife.

Jeff raised his tea cup toward her in a small, grateful toast.

**JEFF:**  
To strategic exploring.

**JEN:** (clinking cups)  
And dumb luck.

The owner’s wife chuckled softly, bowing again.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
You two are gonna fit in just fine here.

And in the warm little pocket of Tokyo they had stumbled into,  
surrounded by strangers and old wood and the scent of real rice,  
they settled in for a meal neither of them would ever forget.

The owner’s wife leaned casually against the counter, a knowing twinkle lighting up her dark eyes as she set down a small lacquered menu — this one, blessedly, annotated with a few English translations scribbled in the margins.

She sized them up with the quick, easy grace of someone who had spent a lifetime reading people.

Her gaze flicked from Jeff —  
tall, alert, clothes a little too practical —  
to Jen —  
wide-eyed, glowing, still soaking in every detail like a sponge.

**Owner’s Wife:** (playful, teasing)  
Let me guess…  One of you’s the seasoned traveler,  

(tilting her chin toward Jeff)  
and one of you’s the brand-new bride,  

(staring straight at Jen, smiling warmly)  
seeing the world for the first time?

Jen’s mouth dropped open slightly in surprise, then she laughed, glancing up at Jeff with wide, amused eyes.

Jeff chuckled too, rubbing the back of his neck sheepishly.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Okay, that’s either psychic powers or you’ve seen a lot of newlyweds.

The woman laughed, her face crinkling in delight.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Oh, honey,  I’ve seen a thousand couples come through here.  You can tell right away.  The seasoned ones, they sit down like they’re docking a ship.  The new ones,  

(soft smile)  
they can’t stop smiling at each other.

Jen flushed a little, but she was still smiling — she couldn’t stop smiling.

**Owner’s Wife:** (teasing)  
What do you think?  Can I read minds?  Or just faces?

Jeff glanced over at Jen, who gave him a tiny shrug and an even tinier grin that said, she’s got us dead to rights.

**JEFF:** (smirking)  
Maybe both.

The woman laughed again, this time deeper, more richly.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Good.  Then let me help you order, hmm?  

(leaning closer like she was letting them in on a secret)  
Trust me —  I’ll bring you a few things you’ll love.  No menus needed.  Just say yes.

Jen nodded eagerly, still giggling, and Jeff — sensing the magic of the moment — simply said:

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Yes.  We’re in your hands.

The owner’s wife clapped her hands once, pleased,  and disappeared behind the counter,  leaving them sitting at the tiny sushi bar,  still laughing,  still amazed,  
still falling a little deeper into this strange, bright new life they were building —  
one bite at a time.

Jeff leaned forward a little, resting his forearms casually on the smooth wood of the counter, giving the woman a warm, easy smile.

**JEFF:** (friendly, open)  
I'd like to place our trust in you.  Money's no object tonight.  Just… dinner for two.  
A real experience.  Something special.

He hesitated for half a second, then added with a wry grin:

**JEFF:**  
And… keep in mind,  we’re Americans.  From the Midwest.  Portion control for us works… 
a little different than it does here.

Jen laughed softly beside him, covering her mouth as if trying not to sound too gleeful.

The owner's wife threw her head back and let out a rich, delighted laugh — the kind that said she’d already made up her mind about them and it was nothing but good.

**Owner’s Wife:** (grinning wide)  
Oh, honey,  I had you two sized up the minute you walked through that door.

She wagged a playful finger at Jeff and Jen, almost scolding, almost motherly.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
You’re my favorite kind —  big hearts, big appetites, big eyes.

She leaned down a little, voice dropping to a conspiratorial whisper:

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Trust me.  I’m gonna knock you two flat.  You’ll walk out of here full, happy, and maybe a little dizzy.  In the best way.

Jeff laughed, relaxing even further into the moment, the city, the marriage, the life he was building with the girl at his side.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Sounds perfect.

The woman gave them a little wink, turned on her heel, and started calling out sharp, musical orders in Japanese to the chefs behind the counter.

And just like that,  the night unfolded —  promise by promise,  plate by plate,  one perfect, unexpected miracle at a time.

The owner’s wife bustled back toward them with a small tray, sliding two beautifully arranged plates onto the counter — thinly sliced sashimi arranged like delicate rose petals atop gleaming shiso leaves.  It was art, not food.

She leaned over the counter with a bright smile.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
You want beers with that?  Best way to start.

Jeff smiled warmly, but shook his head gently.

**JEFF:**  
No thank you, ma’am.  We’re Baptists.

Her eyebrows lifted slightly — not in offense, just mild, genuine curiosity — like she was filing that away.

**Owner’s Wife:** (grinning)  
Baptists, huh?  I’m… familiar.  Never understood you folks… but I like you anyway.

Jen giggled softly behind her hand, and Jeff just smiled, used to the reactions by now.

**JEFF:**  
So…what kind of non-alcoholic drinks do you have?  Tea, maybe?

The woman nodded, immediately getting it.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Plenty.  

(beat, chuckling)  
More than you could ever drink.  But to keep it simple —  I’ll just bring you something good.  Hot and clean.  Don’t worry about the fancy stuff.  You wouldn’t understand the nuances yet.

Jeff raised his hands in surrender, laughing.

**JEFF:**  
I trust you.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Blindly.

The woman winked and whisked herself away again, leaving them sitting before their first dish —  the scent of fresh fish and wasabi in the air,  the warm hum of laughter and knives behind the counter,  and the steady, growing feeling that this was going to be one of those meals  they would remember for the rest of their lives.

Jen leaned in closer to Jeff, her voice low but bubbling with excitement, her eyes wide as she took it all in — the glistening sashimi before them, the precision of the chefs' movements behind the counter, the cozy hum of the tiny room.

**JEN:** (whispering, thrilled)  
We hit the jackpot, I think.  I just can't even…  It’s incredible.

She inhaled deeply, almost reverently.

**JEN:**  
All the scents, the smells… It’s like nothing I’ve ever experienced.  Clean.  Fresh.  
Rich.  It’s not heavy like some places back home — it’s just alive.

Jeff smiled, propping his chin on one hand, more focused on watching her than the food for a moment.

She gestured slightly with her chopsticks — still unused, still a little intimidating — toward the two chefs behind the counter.

**JEN:** (awed)  
And just… watching these guys work?  They’re incredible.

One of the chefs, a wiry man with hands like instruments, was slicing through a block of tuna with such effortless grace it looked like silk parting.  The other crafted tiny towers of rice and fish without even glancing down.

**JEN:** (soft)  
It’s like… like watching someone paint a masterpiece.  But with food.

Jeff grinned wider, warmth swelling in his chest.  Seeing her this alive, this curious, this completely lit up by the world —  it made everything worth it.

**JEFF:** (teasing, gentle)  
Best honeymoon stop yet?

Jen turned and beamed at him, her cheeks flushed from excitement, not from the heat.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Best anything yet.

Their tea arrived just then — delicate porcelain cups filled with a fragrant, steaming brew — and they raised them in a small, impromptu toast.

**JEFF:** (soft, smiling)  
To jackpots.

**JEN:** (glowing)  
To Tokyo.

And they sipped,  and they laughed,  and the night unfolded like a treasure chest — one glistening surprise at a time.

You said:

Jen clutched her tea cup in both hands, practically bouncing in her seat with wide-eyed energy, her cheeks glowing with excitement.

She leaned in closer across the tiny counter, voice lowering to a conspiratorial whisper — even though no one around them could understand a word of English.

**JEN:** (giddy, breathless)  
This might be… almost as good as the private beach.

Jeff blinked, caught completely off guard, tea halfway to his mouth.

**JEFF:** (startled, teasing)  
Almost as good?  You mean… the beach where we, you know… had sex?  Under the stars?  In the rain?  All that?

Jen bit her lip, trying and failing to contain her grin.

**JEN:** (laughing)  
Yes.  That beach.

Jeff set his tea down carefully, studying her like she was a strange, beautiful creature he'd somehow tricked into marrying him.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Alright, now you’ve gotta explain.  I thought that was the highlight of the trip.

Jen nodded quickly, eager to explain, her words rushing out.

**JEN:**  
It was!  It is!  But this —  

(gesturing wildly around the tiny sushi shop)  
this is like…  the magic you don't expect.   That was magic we planned — the island, the ocean, the stars… but this?  We wandered into it by accident.  No reservations.  No map. 
No guidebook.

She sat back a little, eyes shining.

**JEN:**  
It’s just happening.  And it’s perfect.  And it feels like… like God smiling at us.  Like a little wink from heaven saying, "Yeah, keep trusting each other. Keep trusting Me. You’re doing just fine."

Jeff swallowed hard, feeling the lump rise in his throat, unexpected and sharp.

**JEFF:** (quiet, full)  
You’re amazing.

Jen shrugged, playful again, but the warmth between them was heavy, rich, undeniable.

**JEN:** (smiling)  
You married me.  You’re stuck with all this enthusiasm.

Jeff chuckled low and deep, reaching out to squeeze her hand gently where it rested on the counter.

**JEFF:**  
I wouldn't trade it for the whole world.

Around them, the chefs moved like poetry, the city buzzed beyond the door,  
and inside their tiny corner of Tokyo,  something stronger than luck,  something deeper than planning,  something divine  was quietly weaving their lives even closer together.

Jeff finally turned his attention fully to the plate in front of him.  The sashimi was breathtaking — artfully arranged, the colors so vivid they seemed almost impossible: deep ruby tuna, pale translucent squid, gleaming pink salmon, a delicate curl of yellowtail.

He picked up his chopsticks — fumbling only slightly — and carefully selected a slice of tuna, placing it gently in his mouth. He chewed once. And then stopped.

**JEFF:** (thinking, stunned)  
Holy… this isn’t just good.  This is different.

He blinked slowly, letting the flavors bloom across his tongue.  It was clean, buttery, rich without being heavy,  like the ocean had given him a gift, wrapped it in silk,  
and handed it over without a receipt.

He swallowed, savoring the last trace of it, and then looked over at Jen —  who was still gingerly poking at her own plate, wide-eyed —  and then back at the owner’s wife, who was watching them both with a sly, knowing smile.

**JEFF:** (low, reverent)  
This is… this is top tier.  Top shelf.

He shook his head a little, still stunned.

**JEFF:** (soft, amazed)  
I’ve been here before.  Been to Japan a few times.  Had some really good meals.  Really good.  But this?

He gestured lightly with his chopsticks, almost as if it would be disrespectful to wave them around too much in a place this sacred.

**JEFF:**  
This is something else.

Jen finally dared a bite herself, her face lighting up almost immediately.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
It tastes like…  like it’s not even food.  It’s like…  sunlight.  And rain.  And the sea.  
All mixed together.

Jeff smiled, a deep, contented smile that reached all the way down to the soles of his feet.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Told you trusting strangers would be worth it.

Across the counter, the owner's wife winked,  like she knew exactly the moment her little shop had wormed its way permanently into their hearts. And with every perfect, melt-on-the-tongue bite,  Jeff realized he wasn’t just having the best sushi of his life —  
he was building a memory that would never, ever fade.

The owner's wife reappeared, carrying a polished wooden tray with a kind of easy ceremony —  not rushed, not theatrical, just right —  and set it gently down in front of them.

On it were three small plates, each arranged with almost impossible precision:  
a shimmering piece of nigiri, barely kissed by soy;  a delicate mound of vinegared octopus, sliced paper-thin;  and a tiny, perfect handroll of crisp nori, brimming with fresh crab and cucumber.

She smiled warmly, bowing her head slightly.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
First course.  Please, take your time.  There’s more coming.

Jen leaned forward, wide-eyed, almost reverent.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
It’s like Christmas morning.  If Christmas morning was made of fish.

Jeff chuckled under his breath, picking up his chopsticks carefully, respectful like he was handling something sacred.

The flavors hit them in waves —  the nigiri melting on the tongue like it had never been solid;  the octopus soft but with a gentle chew, bright with just a hint of citrus;  the crab roll so fresh it seemed impossible it had ever been in the ocean, like it had been conjured up for them from thin air.

Jeff sat back after a few bites, savoring, feeling the beginning of something bigger.

**JEFF:** (thinking)  
First course.  And it’s already better than ninety-nine percent of what I’ve ever eaten anywhere.

Jen chewed thoughtfully, swallowed, and leaned closer to him, whispering as if sharing some world-shaking secret.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
We might need to move here.  Just for this.

Jeff laughed, low and easy,  feeling for the first time in days like the world had slowed down,  like it had given them a small, perfect pocket of peace and wonder.

And as the last bite of the first course disappeared,  Jeff caught the owner's wife smiling at them again —  a twinkle in her eye that said,  You ain't seen nothing yet.

The next course came across the counter with a kind of quiet, reverent energy.  This time it was the owner himself — the older man with silver at his temples and hands steady as stone — who placed the tray before them.

Jeff and Jen straightened instinctively, sensing that something a little more serious was happening now. The owner’s wife joined him at the counter, standing just a half-step behind and to the side.  She smiled warmly at them and gave a tiny, respectful bow.

**Owner’s Wife:** (gentle, almost formal)  
My husband would like to say a few words.  
  
He doesn’t speak a lick of English,  so… I’ll translate for him.

Jeff nodded respectfully, and Jen did the same, suddenly feeling like honored guests rather than just customers.

The owner spoke a few short, rich sentences in Japanese — his voice low, careful, deliberate.  The room seemed to quiet a little more, almost unconsciously.

The wife turned back to them, translating smoothly, her voice soft and full of pride.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
He says… you two are very welcome here.  
  
He can tell you are good people.  

(another beat, smiling)  
He says the way you sit close, the way you talk softly to each other… It reminds him of when he and I were young.

Jeff felt his chest tighten — not in discomfort, but in that sudden, unexpected way that happens when something real and pure hits you straight between the ribs.

The owner spoke again, a little longer this time.

**Owner’s Wife:** (translating)  
He says the food you are about to eat —  this second course —  is something special.  
It is made with fish from Hokkaido.  Caught just yesterday.  Very fresh.  Very expensive.  
  
But tonight, for you,  he is giving it as a gift.

Jen gasped softly, bringing her hand to her chest.  Jeff could only stare, humbled in a way words couldn't reach.

The owner's wife bowed slightly once more, her voice lowering.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
He says… he hopes you will carry the memory of this meal with you.  Like we have carried the memory of each other,  through all our years.

Jeff cleared his throat, swallowing against the tightness there.

**JEFF:** (soft, sincere)  
Please tell him… we are honored.  Truly honored.

The owner's wife smiled, tears just barely pricking the corners of her eyes, and relayed the words in smooth, flowing Japanese. The old man smiled, slow and full,  bowed deeply,  and returned behind the counter,  hands already moving again with the grace of a lifetime's devotion.

Jeff reached out, found Jen’s hand, and held it tightly under the counter.  She squeezed back just as fiercely. And together, they turned toward the second course —  
a gift,  a memory,  a small piece of someone else’s lifelong love,  laid humbly before them.

Jeff leaned in close to Jen again, his voice low, warm, and thoughtful — the buzz of the small restaurant fading into the background as he spoke quietly for her ears alone.

**JEFF:** (explaining, steady)  
This right here… what just happened?  It’s the real heart of Japan.

Jen turned her full attention to him, sensing this was one of those moments where he was letting her see a part of his mind she hadn’t really glimpsed before.

**JEFF:**  
The Japanese… they’re an honor-based culture. Very sentimental. It’s not about quick wins, not about hammering out deals overnight.  It’s relationships that matter.  Trust.  Respect.  Taking your time to build something real.

He nodded toward the chefs, the owner and his wife moving quietly behind the counter with a kind of practiced grace that only made sense if you’d lived it day after day.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
Here?  The exploration…  the circling…  the meals…  the gifts…  the conversations about life, about family…  that’s where the real work happens.

Jen listened intently, cradling her tea cup like it was something precious.

**JEFF:**  
By the time you get to the main event —  the contract signing, the handshake, the dotted line —  it’s basically a formality.  Just putting on paper what both sides already know in their hearts.

He smiled a little, almost ruefully.

**JEFF:**  
Japan isn’t really…  direct.  Not the way we are back home.  Not the way Americans like to be.

He shrugged lightly, not criticizing, just explaining.

**JEFF:**  
Here, you feel things out.  You listen more than you speak.  You show you can be trusted long before you ever talk about business.

Jen nodded slowly, taking it all in, her eyes serious and wide.

**JEN:** (softly)  
It’s beautiful.  Harder…  but beautiful.

Jeff smiled, brushing a strand of hair back behind her ear.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
It’s a different kind of strength.  And if you respect it,  if you work with it instead of against it…  you can build something better.  Something lasting.

Jen reached across the table, laying her hand lightly on top of his.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Just like us.

Jeff looked at her for a long moment,  then nodded,  once, firmly,  feeling the simple truth of it settle between them like a cornerstone laid into bedrock.

In the middle of a city of forty million souls,  in a tiny shop tucked under endless neon,  
two newlyweds found themselves learning how to build something permanent —  
brick by brick, breath by breath,  meal by meal.

Jeff gave a soft, almost private chuckle, glancing around the cozy little shop as if weighing the magnitude of it all against the humble surroundings.

**JEFF:** (low, thoughtful)  
And this…  this is why we’re here tonight.  Why we’re here in Japan this week.

Jen’s eyebrows lifted slightly, the pieces starting to click into place for her.

**JEFF:** (explaining, calm)  
I’ve been working on a project…  quietly.  
  
A limited edition LP — just for the Japanese market.  Commuted music.  From the Meadowlands concert we recorded in New York.

Jen blinked, impressed.

**JEN:** (soft)  
The Meadowlands?  That was a huge show.

Jeff nodded, a slow, measured nod, his hand idly tracing a small pattern against the tabletop.

**JEFF:**  
Huge.  The energy there… it was off the charts.  It’s the perfect foundation for something rare, something collectors over here will kill to have.

He glanced around again, taking in the careful craftsmanship, the attention to detail in every tiny part of the shop.

**JEFF:**  
Japan respects craftsmanship.  They respect limited things.  Things made with care.  
Things not mass-produced.

Jen smiled, already seeing how it fit together.

**JEN:** (softly)  
So it’s not just music.  It’s… an experience.

Jeff grinned at her, proud and a little amazed at how fast she understood.

**JEFF:**  
Exactly.  I’ve been working with the American team at Sony in Los Angeles, getting all the logistics hammered out… but now…  now it’s time to pave the way for the final deal.  

(beat, meaningfully)  
Face to face.  The right way.

Jen’s hand brushed his, a light, proud touch.

**JEN:** (smiling)  
You’re really good at this.

Jeff smiled back at her, the compliment warming him more than he could say.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
I’m good at picking the right partners.  

(beat, squeezing her hand)  
In business…  and in life.

Jen blushed lightly, but she held his gaze — steady, sure, just like she had at the altar.

Across the counter, the owner’s wife placed the next set of small dishes before them,  
as if the universe itself was answering back:  trust well placed,  love well founded,  
dreams well underway.


**JEFF:** (easy, playful)  
That big meeting, the real heavy stuff?  That’s not till later in the week.  So I’m thinking…  tomorrow?  We go to the Tokyo Dome.  Catch a baseball game.

Jen’s face lit up instantly, excitement bubbling through her exhaustion.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Seriously?

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Seriously.  Figured it'd be a good way to catch our breath.  You've only been to Riverfront to watch the Reds, right?  Maybe up to Municipal Field once or twice?

Jen gave a little shrug, smiling a bit sheepishly.

**JEN:**  
Actually… no.  
  
Because my parents grew up in Portsmouth — way down south —  it was actually easier for them to take us to Three Rivers in Pittsburgh.  Closer than driving all the way north to Cleveland.

Jeff blinked, grinning even wider now.

**JEFF:** (teasing)  
You’re kidding.  You’re a secret Pirates fan?

Jen laughed, covering her mouth.

**JEN:**  
No!  

(beat, teasing)  
At least not openly.

Jeff chuckled, picking up his tea cup again and giving her a mock-serious nod.

**JEFF:**  
We’ll have to work on that.  Can’t have my wife secretly rooting for the enemy.

Jen leaned forward, eyes sparkling.

**JEN:** (laughing)  
You mean we’re both gonna learn to root for Japanese teams tomorrow?

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Exactly.  Neutral ground.  New teams.  New rules.  New memories.

Jen beamed, the idea of a new, spontaneous adventure lighting her up just as much as the perfect sushi had.

**JEN:**  
Only two professional games ever.  Tomorrow’ll be number three.  

(beat, softer)  
And the first one with you.

Jeff squeezed her hand lightly under the counter, feeling it all fall into place —  the food, the city, the woman beside him —  like a life he hadn’t even realized he’d been waiting his whole life to find.


Jeff and Jen barely had time to finish their tea before the owner himself reappeared at the counter, carrying a lacquered wooden tray as if it held the Crown Jewels.

Behind him, the owner's wife followed, smiling knowingly —  the kind of smile that said, we've saved the best for last. The third course was set down before them with a reverent precision.  And for a moment, Jeff and Jen just stared.

It wasn’t flashy.  It wasn’t piled high or over-decorated.  It was simple:  perfect nigiri — thick slices of gleaming fish, each piece molded onto beds of vinegared rice by hand.  
But the colors were beyond vivid — deep reds, buttery yellows, shimmering silvers.

And the scent — clean, sweet, alive — rose like a tide. The owner’s wife leaned in slightly, voice warm.

**Owner’s Wife:**  
Third course.  Best of the house.  Only for special guests.

Jen’s hand fluttered to her chest again, wide-eyed.

Jeff, who had eaten some of the best meals in Tokyo during past trips, felt something shift deep inside him —  an instinctive sense that this wasn’t just food.  This was a gift.

He picked up a piece — a slice of deep red toro, fatty tuna — and placed it carefully into his mouth. And then he stopped. The world stopped.

For a full second, he forgot where he was, forgot he was holding chopsticks, forgot everything except the melt of fish against his tongue — buttery, rich, impossibly soft, almost sweet. It was perfect.  Beyond perfect.

He opened his eyes, found Jen watching him, her own piece poised halfway to her mouth, her expression a mixture of awe and excitement. She bit into hers — a piece of salmon so fresh it seemed to dissolve on her tongue — and her eyes went wide.

**JEN:** (whispering, stunned)  
Oh my gosh.  This is…  this is the best thing I’ve ever eaten. Ever.

Jeff couldn’t even manage a joke.  He just nodded, slowly, solemnly, like a man who had witnessed a miracle.

**JEFF:** (quiet, full)  
Best thing.  Ever.

They ate in silence for a few moments, savoring every bite — not rushing, not laughing, just being there,  letting the experience etch itself deep into their memory.

Across the counter, the owner and his wife watched them, smiling softly,  as if this was exactly the reaction they had hoped for —  as if feeding people well was an act of love in itself. And in that tiny glowing pocket of Tokyo, Jeff and Jen learned something they would carry with them for the rest of their lives: Some moments didn’t need words.  
Some moments spoke for themselves.  Some moments were simply…  
perfect.

Jen set her chopsticks down carefully, wiping her mouth with a napkin, her expression thoughtful now — the giddy excitement of the meal mellowing into a quieter curiosity.

She leaned a little closer to Jeff across the narrow counter, her voice low but serious.

**JEN:** (soft, curious)  
Now, Tokyo’s supposed to be…  one of the safest cities in the world, right?

Jeff nodded immediately, reaching for his tea, casual but confident.

**JEFF:** (reassuring)  
Yeah.  Absolutely.

Jen tilted her head slightly, studying him the way she always did when she was working through something in her mind.

**JEN:**  
So…  is there gonna be any sort of difficulty, you know,  with you and me walking around downtown late?  Like… way past midnight?

Jeff smiled a little, setting his tea down carefully, choosing his words.

**JEFF:** (calm, honest)  
Not really.  Not here.  Not like home.

He glanced around the small shop — quiet, orderly, everyone minding their business — and then gestured vaguely toward the door, to the sprawling, glowing city just beyond.

**JEFF:**  
You’re not gonna find a lot of street crime here.  No random mugging, no smash-and-grab stuff like you might worry about back in the States.

Jen looked relieved, but Jeff could see she was still processing.

**JEFF:** (gentle)  
You’ll see people —  businessmen, schoolkids, even women — walking home alone late at night.  Nobody bothering them.  Nobody hassling anybody.

He smiled a little more, softer now.

**JEFF:**  
Tokyo runs on trust.  On rules.  On respect.  It’s not perfect, nothing ever is. But you and me walking around past midnight?  It’s about as safe as you could ever hope for in a city this size.

Jen let out a breath she didn’t realize she was holding, smiling now too, reassured.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
Good.  Because I think I could walk all night and still not see everything.

Jeff chuckled, reaching over to gently brush his fingers against her wrist.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Then let’s walk until we get lost.  And then walk some more.

The owner’s wife caught their eyes just then and gave them a knowing little nod —  
like she understood everything without a single word being said.

Outside, the city still pulsed and shimmered,  and inside, Jeff and Jen finished their meal, ready to step back into a world that, for once, felt like it was welcoming them with open arms.

Jen’s eyes sparkled like neon caught in water,  
her voice dropping to a playful, wicked whisper across the little space between them.

**JEN:** (grinning, conspiratorial)  
Then good.  Husband…  
I propose that we just get lost in the city —  
walk till we can’t walk anymore —  
and then go back to the room…  
and have sex till dawn!

Jeff froze for two beats, chopsticks hovering forgotten over the last scraps of their miracle meal.  
He stared at her — that mischievous flash in her eyes, the sheer reckless joy radiating off her.

Two beats.

**JEFF:** (steady, low)  
Agreed.

But there was something more simmering just under the surface now —  
a quiet, raw truth blooming up between them.

Jeff set his chopsticks down with care, leaned in just slightly, letting his words hit only her ears.

**JEFF:** (softer, meaning it)  
And…  
I think…  
  
I trust you enough now  
that tonight…  
I might go down on you.

Jen’s mouth parted slightly, the breath hitching in her throat,  
her face lighting up like someone had handed her the stars themselves.

For a second, she was too stunned to speak —  
then she squeezed his hand under the counter, practically vibrating with excitement.

**JEN:** (whispering fiercely)  
I can’t wait.  
(beat, laughing softly)  
But you’re not getting out of a night of wandering first.

Jeff laughed low in his chest, the sound rolling out easy and full.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Wouldn’t dream of it.

Jen squeezed his hand again, this time dragging her thumb in a slow little circle across his palm.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Four…  
maybe five hours of getting lost in Tokyo.  
And then you.  
And me.  
  
And no sleep till sunrise.

Jeff gave a soft, amazed laugh —  
because somehow, impossibly,  
he loved her even more at that moment  
than he thought a human heart was capable of.

They finished their tea slowly,  paid their bill with deep bows and honest thanks,  and stepped out into the glittering, endless Tokyo night —  hand in hand, heart to heart,  
ready to lose themselves completely…  in the city,  in the stars,  and most of all,  
in each other.

They stepped out into the electric river of Tokyo’s night,  the air thick with neon glow and the faint hum of life that never fully slept. Jen held tightly to Jeff’s hand, her sandals clicking softly against the sidewalk as they wandered aimlessly — no destination, no timeline, just the endless city breathing around them. She tipped her head back to look at a towering wall of lights, glowing billboards stacked ten stories high, digital ads looping silently over a sea of moving faces.

**JEN:** (quiet, awed)  
You know…  this had to be what inspired Blade Runner.  All of this.  The way the city moves…  the way the light never really dies.

Jeff grinned, glancing sideways at her, his heart giving a little kick at how sharp she was — how she could see the shape of something bigger under the noise.

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
You’re not wrong.  Ridley Scott —  he spent time here before he filmed it.  Said Tokyo at night was like stepping into the future.

They passed a side street that glowed pure blue, the smell of sizzling pork and sweet soy sauce drifting toward them like an invisible rope, pulling them deeper into the city.

**JEFF:** (soft, thoughtful)  
And you can see it.  All the layers.  The noise.  The colors.  The crowds that just move without needing to talk.

Jen smiled up at him, her eyes wide, alive.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Makes you wonder…  are we the past? And this is the future?

Jeff laughed quietly, squeezing her hand.

**JEFF:** (teasing)  
Babe, right now we’re just two kids from Ohio  getting lost on purpose in a city of forty million people.  

(beat, smiling)  
We’re both.

Jen laughed too, swinging their hands slightly between them as they walked.

Above them, the neon poured down like endless rain.  Around them, Tokyo buzzed, alive and eternal. And in the middle of it —  Jeff and Jen Cremeans,  two tiny points of light,  
falling deeper into love with every step.

They crossed another wide intersection, the crosswalk lines glowing faintly under the overhead lights, and ducked into a quieter side street lined with tidy little trees —  
actual trees, with carefully trimmed branches and small square patches of grass at their roots.

Jen tugged Jeff’s arm gently, slowing their pace as she looked around, her expression thoughtful.

**JEN:** (soft, surprised)  
You know…  
there’s a lot more nature here than I expected.

Jeff glanced around too — the greenery tucked along sidewalks, small rooftop gardens overhead, little shrines hidden between storefronts.

**JEN:** (continuing, curious)  
I thought it would be…  
like…  
a hundred percent paved over.  
All concrete and steel and neon.  
(beat, marveling)  
But there’s trees…  
little gardens…  
even patches of grass.

Jeff smiled, seeing it now through her fresh eyes.

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Tokyo’s smart about it.  
  
They know people need places to breathe.  
Even in a city this packed.  
  
Small pockets of green.  
Little breaks in the noise.

Jen turned in a slow circle on the sidewalk, taking it all in —  
the quiet hum of late-night traffic,  
the warm smell of earth mixed with city rain,  
the way a tiny tree could somehow look right at home between a skyscraper and a ramen shop.

**JEN:** (softly)  
It’s beautiful.  
(beat, smiling)  
Like the city’s trying to remind itself —  
"We're still alive. We’re still human."

Jeff chuckled, slipping his arm fully around her waist as they walked.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Maybe that’s why it feels so different here.  
  
Even when it’s crazy, even when it’s loud…  
it’s still alive.

Jen leaned her head briefly against his shoulder, content.

And they kept walking —  
through light and shadow,  
through city and garden,  
through the heart of Tokyo  
and deeper into the story they were writing together,  
one step at a time.

They strolled past another glowing storefront when Jen suddenly tugged on Jeff’s arm, her eyes catching a glint of something shiny behind the glass.

It was a small, cluttered little shop —  
half souvenirs, half practical gear —  
and right there in the window, under a flickering fluorescent light,  
a rack of outrageous sunglasses.

Jen’s face lit up like a kid spotting a candy store.

**JEN:** (excited, half-laughing)  
Can we get matching sunglasses?  
Like… real matching.  
Mirror-shades.

Jeff turned to look, squinting into the window, then back at Jen’s hopeful grin.

He chuckled, shaking his head fondly.

**JEFF:** (teasing)  
As long as we’re not picking up samurai swords  
or anything else that's gonna get me flagged by customs,  
we’re good.

He reached down, gave her hand a squeeze.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Let’s do it.

Jen practically bounced on her toes, dragging him toward the door.

Inside, the shop smelled like new plastic and dust,  
and a tiny, elderly shopkeeper bowed to them politely without a word.

They gravitated straight to the sunglasses rack —  
rows of wild, mirrored shades gleaming under fluorescent lights.  
Some were silver, some were gold, some so obnoxiously blue they looked like superhero costumes.

Jen immediately pulled a ridiculous pair off the rack —  
big, silver mirror lenses, aviator style —  
and stuck them on her face with a huge grin.

**JEN:** (posing)  
How do I look, husband?

Jeff laughed — genuinely laughed, the kind that shook his shoulders —  
and plucked a matching pair off the rack for himself.

He slid them on and gave her a slow, exaggerated nod.

**JEFF:** (mock serious)  
We look like the world's least competent secret agents.

Jen giggled, grabbing his arm.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Perfect.

They paid in yen, bowed to the old shopkeeper —  
who looked faintly amused but said nothing —  
and stepped back out into the Tokyo night.

Two kids from Ohio.  
In matching, ridiculous mirror shades.  
In the middle of the most dazzling city on earth.

And they couldn’t have looked  
—or felt—  
more invincible.

They stepped back out into the buzz and glow of the Tokyo night, the neon reflecting off every slick surface, the pavement still alive with motion even as the clock edged past midnight.

Jen slipped her arm through Jeff’s, grinning like she was getting away with a crime.

She glanced around through the ridiculous mirrored lenses and laughed.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
Okay…  
it’s bright enough that I can kinda see with these on.  
But we are definitely…  
sunglasses at night people right now.

Jeff tilted his head, peering through his own shades —  
and promptly bumped slightly into a signpost he hadn’t noticed.

He stopped, reaching up and tugging the glasses off with a sheepish grin.

**JEFF:** (dry, amused)  
Yeah.  
I can’t see a thing.  
  
You’re in charge of navigation.

Jen tipped her sunglasses down the bridge of her nose to look at him over the top of the lenses, smirking.

**JEN:** (mock serious)  
Oh, that's reassuring.  
Put the blind guy behind the girl who can only see “kinda.”

Jeff laughed, pocketing his shades, his free hand sliding back around her waist.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
We’ll just wander until the city gives up a secret.

Jen slid her sunglasses back up, proud and ridiculous and absolutely thrilled to be ridiculous together.

And hand in hand,  
two slightly lost, slightly reckless,  
completely happy newlyweds  
kept drifting through the endless, glowing night —  
laughing, teasing, loving the whole chaotic wonder of it.

Jeff adjusted his arm around Jen’s shoulders as they wandered slowly down another neon-lit street, the mirrored sunglasses now tucked safely away but the conversation still fresh.

He glanced down at her, his voice easy but edged with a little real-world weariness.

**JEFF:** (explaining, thoughtful)  
You know why my guys and Kathy wear sunglasses inside?  
At night?  
All the time?

Jen shook her head, smiling curiously.

**JEN:**  
I figured it was just…  
you know…  
a rock star thing.

Jeff gave a soft chuckle but shook his head.

**JEFF:** (steady)  
It’s flash photography.  
Constant flash photography.  
  
You have a press conference?  
You’re standing up there for thirty minutes —  
and you get dozens, sometimes hundreds of flashes  
going off right in your face.  
Point-blank.  
Over and over.

Jen winced instinctively, blinking like she could feel the imaginary flashes already.

**JEFF:** (low, serious)  
It punishes your eyes.  
Hard.  
  
The human eye wasn’t made for that.  
You take that many hits, night after night,  
and it ages you.  
Burns you out.

He smiled a little then, almost wryly.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
Sunglasses aren’t about looking cool.  
They're armor.  
Survival gear.

Jen looked up at him, thoughtful now, seeing another layer to his world she hadn't really understood before.

**JEN:** (quiet)  
It’s not all fun and parties, huh?

Jeff gave a small, tired smile —  
not bitter, just honest.

**JEFF:**  
Parts of it are.  
But it’s a lot more work, a lot more wearing down,  
than anybody ever wants to believe.

Jen tightened her arm around his waist in silent answer.

And together they kept walking,  
the flash and dazzle of the city playing harmlessly over them,  
as Jeff kept teaching her not just about Tokyo,  
but about the unseen costs of chasing something bright  
for long enough that it starts to burn.


Jeff slowed their pace a little, steering them down a quieter alley lit only by soft lanterns swinging gently overhead.  
It gave them a little bubble of peace to talk — something about the topic at hand demanded a quieter street.

He glanced at Jen, seeing the thoughtful crease in her brow, and decided to step carefully but honestly.

**JEFF:** (calm, reflective)  
You know the phrase, right?  
Sex, drugs, and rock and roll?

Jen gave a little half-smile, a soft, familiar roll of her eyes.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
I’ve heard it.  
Not exactly part of youth group, though.

Jeff chuckled.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
No, not part of youth group.  
(beat, thoughtful)  
The thing is…  
the sex and the drugs —  
they come after the fame.  
After the floodlights hit you.  
When people start throwing themselves at you.  
When the world starts offering you everything, and you’re just…  
not ready for it.

Jen nodded, understanding that part, her expression soft but serious.

**JEN:** (gently)  
Okay.  
That makes sense.  
But…  
where does the drugs part come in?  
How could that authentically fit into how a band works?  
  
I don’t get that part.

Jeff sighed, slow and measured, like he’d had this conversation in his own head a hundred times.

**JEFF:** (explaining)  
Unlike our world —  
our Baptist world —  
where we see alcohol, and anything like it, as pretty much a straight path to destruction…  
  
in their world?  
A drink, maybe two,  
it loosens your lips.  
Loosens your tongue.  
Takes down walls.  
Opens creative doors.

Jen’s brow furrowed, but she listened carefully, really trying to understand.

**JEFF:**  
They believe —  
and I mean all six members of Commuted —  
they would violently but respectfully disagree with you and me on this…  
  
They believe a little alcohol…  
a little loss of inhibition…  
helps catch the raw nerve.  
The honest emotion.  
The stuff that's too scary to say stone-cold sober.

Jen chewed her lip, still looking skeptical, but thinking it through.

**JEN:** (slowly)  
So it’s not about…  
getting wasted?  
Falling down drunk?

Jeff shook his head firmly.

**JEFF:**  
No.  
Not if it’s done right.  
  
It’s about tapping into the stuff that’s buried.  
The fear, the anger, the heartbreak.  
All the things that make real music sting a little when you hear it.

He smiled a little then, almost wistfully.

**JEFF:**  
Properly managed —  
it can make art.  
True art.  
Unfiltered, raw, bloody art.

Jen was quiet for a long moment, digesting it.

Then she slipped her hand back into his without a word.

**JEN:** (soft)  
I’m glad you’re there to keep them honest.

Jeff squeezed her hand back, grateful, grounded by her steady trust.

**JEFF:** (low)  
Me too.

And they kept walking,  
through the city that pulsed with its own raw, wild music,  
two kids from a quieter world,  
trying to understand the rhythm of another —  
and finding, somehow,  
that love could walk both roads at once.

They walked a little further down the narrow street, their footsteps quiet on the slick pavement,  
the bright roar of the main avenue fading behind them like a memory.

Jeff squeezed Jen’s hand again, thoughtful, weighing what he wanted to say next —  
then decided to just lay it out plain.

**JEFF:** (low, serious)  
But.  
  
Unproperly managed?  
(another beat, heavier)  
It’s corrosive.

Jen turned her head, watching him carefully now.

**JEFF:** (quiet, steady)  
It’ll rot you from the inside out.  
  
Drugs.  
Alcohol.  
Fame.  
Sex.  
The whole cocktail.

He exhaled slowly, his voice almost grim for a moment.

**JEFF:**  
I’m lucky.  
Really lucky.  
Only one of the six even remotely tests that boundary.

Jen’s brow furrowed slightly, concern slipping into her expression.

**JEN:**  
Jeremy?

Jeff nodded.

**JEFF:** (sighing)  
Yeah.  
Jeremy Evans.  
  
He’s…  
he’s got all the raw talent in the world.  
But he’s in a lousy relationship.  
Toxic.  
The kind that chews you up and makes you look for the wrong exits.

Jen bit her lip, thinking it through carefully.

**JEN:** (soft)  
But isn’t he getting married later?

Jeff gave a short, dry chuckle — the sound not cruel, but full of an older kind of sadness.

**JEFF:** (grim)  
Yeah.  
  
And she’s gonna break his balls.

Jen recoiled just slightly, her eyes wide —  
not from the meaning, but from the language.

She pulled back half a step, her expression a funny mix of surprise and gentle scolding.

**JEN:** (soft gasp)  
Jeff!

Jeff smiled sheepishly, rubbing the back of his neck.

**JEFF:** (apologetic, teasing)  
Sorry.  
Bad choice of words.  
(beat, softer)  
But it’s true.

Jen recovered quickly, still teasing him with a mock-hurt look as she bumped his hip with hers.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
I guess even my straight-arrow husband’s got a little rock and roll in him.

Jeff laughed, low and real.

**JEFF:** (warm)  
Only for you, Mrs. Cremeans.

And together they drifted further into the heartbeat of Tokyo,  
learning a little more about the messy, dangerous world he managed —  
and building something stronger between them with every careful, loving step.

Jeff walked a few more steps in silence, then glanced over at Jen, catching the playful glimmer still hidden behind her mild scolding.

He decided to push just a little deeper, speaking slower, more thoughtful now.

**JEFF:** (reflective)  
You know…  
this is kinda what I was trying to figure out the other day.  
  
When I was fumbling around…  
trying to find the right word to talk about your… well…  
your center.

Jen blushed a little, but she smiled too —  
that tender, sweet smile that had quickly become his favorite thing in the world.

Jeff squeezed her hand gently, anchoring them both in the moment.

**JEFF:** (soft, honest)  
So far…  
our whole relationship’s been pretty curated.  
  
When we were dating,  
we got to show each other our best selves.  
You know?  
All cleaned up.  
Polished.  
Careful.

Jen nodded, her expression turning thoughtful too, tracking right along with him.

**JEFF:**  
And now it’s 24/7.  
365 days a year.  
No pause button.  
No carefully planning the next perfect date.  
  
It’s just…  
life.  
Messy.  
Real.  
Raw.

He rubbed the back of his neck again — a small nervous habit Jen was already learning to read.

**JEFF:** (sheepish)  
I honestly didn’t even think of "balls" as being profane.  
  
It’s just a word.  
Kinda rough around the edges.  
But not…  
not ugly.  
Not hateful.

Jen let out a soft, understanding laugh, bumping his hip gently again.

**JEN:** (teasing, warm)  
It’s not the word, Jeff.  
It’s just…  
you caught me off guard.  
(beat, smiling)  
You’re usually so…  
perfectly you.

He smiled back, a little shy, a little relieved.

**JEFF:** (low, affectionate)  
Well…  
welcome to the real me, Mrs. Cremeans.  
A little clumsy.  
A little rough.  
  
But madly in love with you.

Jen’s heart squeezed at that —  
at the way he could be so strong and yet so tender in the same breath.

**JEN:** (soft)  
I love the real you.  
Even when you say something a little shocking.

Jeff leaned over and kissed the top of her head, slow and sure.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Good.  Because there’s a lot more of the real me where that came from.

Hand in hand, hearts wide open, they kept walking —  deeper into Tokyo, deeper into their marriage,  and deeper into the beautiful, imperfect, sacred thing they were building one messy, real day at a time.

---

Jen slowed a little, tugging on Jeff’s hand to make sure he was really hearing her —  not just with his ears, but with his heart.

She wasn’t angry.  She wasn’t upset.  She was… explaining, the way she always did when something really mattered.

**JEN:** (steady, thoughtful)  
I just…I can’t abide the F-word.  And I can’t abide using the Lord’s name in vain.  Those two…those are lines I don't cross.  Won't cross.

Jeff nodded slowly, listening closely, taking her seriously.  Jen tightened her fingers around his.

**JEN:** (calm, sure)  
Other than that…language?  It’s just…a tool.  I choose my words.  On purpose.

She looked up at him, eyes clear, face lit by the ambient neon bleeding down from the high towers above.

**JEN:** (soft)  
It’s the cadence.  
The vocabulary.  
It’s my culture, Jeff.  
It’s the way I was raised.

She smiled a little — not apologizing for it, not excusing it —  
just sharing it with him.

**JEN:** (earnest)  
I do it out of respect.  
To maintain dignity.  
  
To keep the room’s temperature where it should be —  
where people can listen…  
without everything getting hot and wild and out of control.

Jeff felt the weight of her words settle into him, real and permanent.

Jen squeezed his hand again, not scolding, not demanding —  
but offering something very rare and very pure.

**JEN:** (gently)  
Maybe you should really think about it, Jeff.  
About what’s true…  
and what’s just…  
vulgar.

Jeff breathed in slowly, letting that sink deep.  
Not just words.  
Not just rules.  
Respect.  
Dignity.  
Intention.

He turned toward her fully, his thumb brushing the back of her hand.

**JEFF:** (quiet, sincere)  
You’re right.  
  
And I love you even more for it.

Jen smiled, simple and bright,  
and together they kept walking,  
two very different souls who somehow spoke the same language  
where it mattered most.

---

Jen swung their hands lightly between them, her step light despite the seriousness of their conversation.  
She clearly wasn’t done — she was thinking it through, articulating it carefully, in that particular Jen way where every word mattered.

She glanced up at Jeff again, her voice softer, a little playful now but still precise.

**JEN:** (thoughtful, choosing her words)  
For instance…  
I think the word prick is just… silly.  
(beat, smiling)  
It doesn’t feel real.  
It’s not… serious enough.  
It’s like calling a thunderstorm a drizzle.

Jeff chuckled low under his breath, but kept silent, letting her work her way through it.

**JEN:** (gentle, musing)  
Penis feels too clinical.  
Too… textbook.  
Like something you’d hear in a doctor’s office.  
(beat, wrinkling her nose a little)  
Not very warm.  
Not very personal.

Jeff nodded, following right along, intrigued at the way she thought through even this part of life.

Jen’s voice dropped slightly — not embarrassed, just more intimate.

**JEN:** (soft, sure)  
But cock?  
(beat, smiling shyly)  
Cock is delightful.  
It’s the right word.  
(another beat, slower)  
Because it’s…  
you.

She squeezed his hand, a slow, almost reverent squeeze, her eyes locking on his.

**JEN:** (carefully, meaning every syllable)  
It’s you…  
when you change.
