He didn’t need to be asked twice.

---

Jeff sat back down on the bed, still digesting her suggestion. Jen tucked her legs under her, watching him carefully,  reading his moods the way only she could now.

**JEN:** (softly, thoughtfully)  
Maybe…Maybe you call your guy on the West Coast.  The American side.  Let them know what happened.  Let them talk to Sony Japan for you.  Save face all around.

Jeff tapped his fingers against his thigh, considering it.  It had the clean, indirect elegance that Japanese culture valued.  It avoided a direct confrontation.  It let everyone pretend things weren’t as bad as they were — while still putting the right amount of pressure exactly where it belonged.

He smiled, slow and genuine.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
You know…  You might just make a good little Tokyo resident after all.

Jen laughed —  a bright, delighted sound that filled the hotel room.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
Well…  With all the public baths,  the pickled vegetables for breakfast,  and now learning how to avoid confrontation…  Why not?

Jeff reached out and pulled her into his lap,  holding her close, breathing her in.

**JEFF:** (murmuring into her hair)  
Smart.  Beautiful.  Dangerous.

Jen wriggled proudly.

**JEN:** (mock-serious)  
Mrs. Jeffrey Lee Cremeans.  Diplomat to the Empire of Japan.

Jeff laughed —  a full, rich sound —  and kissed her temple.

**JEFF:** (still grinning)  
You make me better, you know that?

Jen shrugged, all innocence.

**JEN:** (smiling)  
That's the idea, lover.

---

Jeff fiddled with the phone for a good minute,  squinting at the complicated printed instructions for international dialing.

**JEFF:** (muttering)  
Exit code…  Country code…  Area code…  Phone number…

Jen snuggled deeper into the covers,  watching him with a mix of amusement and affection. Finally,  after a few beeps, a few crackles, and a long wait,  the call connected.

**Voice:** (sharp, familiar)  
Jeff?  This is Mike.

Jeff leaned forward instinctively —  years of business sense making him straighten up even when sitting on a bed in Tokyo.

**JEFF:** (even, professional)  
Hey, Mike.  Hope I'm not waking you.

**MIKE** (growling)  
Forget about that.  What the hell happened over there?

Jeff kept his voice calm.

**JEFF:** (steady)  
They disrespected my wife.  Openly.  At the first meeting.  Asked what she was doing there, like she was luggage.

There was a brief, dangerous pause.

**MIKE** (quiet fury)  
Those dumb sons of bitches.

Jeff said nothing, letting the weight of it settle.

**MIKE** (still furious)  
We briefed them, Jeff.  I personally briefed them.  Told them you were on your honeymoon.  Told them you were bringing your wife.  Told them to treat her like gold.

Another pause.

**MIKE** (lower, dead serious)  
You did right walking out.  You did exactly right.

Jeff felt a knot in his chest loosen a little.

**JEFF:** (relieved)  
Appreciate you saying it.

**MIKE** (grim)  
We’ll handle it from this side.  I'll call Japan corporate.  I'll call New York.  We'll put the screws to them.

**JEFF:** (measured)  
I don’t want blood.  But I want them to understand.  And I want them to fix it.

**MIKE** (immediate)  
They will.  Or there’s no deal.

Jeff rubbed a hand over his face, exhausted but grateful.

**JEFF:** (softly)  
Thanks, Mike.

**MIKE** (firm)  
Enjoy your honeymoon, Jeff.  We’ll keep the wolves off you.

Jeff hung up the phone slowly,  his hand lingering on the receiver. Jen watched him carefully, reading him again.

**JEN:** (gently)  
Good call?

Jeff smiled —  small, tired, but real.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
Yeah.  Good call.

He slid back under the covers,  pulling her into his arms,  feeling the world right itself around her.

---

Jen slipped out of bed,  the hotel robe brushing around her legs as she padded across the room. Jeff watched her lazily,  his muscles finally starting to unknot after the call. She knelt down in front of the mini-fridge,  fiddled with the latch, and opened it with a soft pop.

There, nestled among a few random bottles of water and sodas, was a single, precious can. She pulled it out reverently,  like it was a relic. Turned around slowly, grinning like a kid at Christmas.

**JEN:** (playful, warm)  
I think you’ve earned this one, sir.

She passed it underhanded to him,  and Jeff accepted it with both hands like it was a touchdown pass in overtime.

He stared at it for a second —  the bright radioactive green of the can,  the familiar Mountain Dew logo. And then he laughed —  a low, genuine laugh that rumbled up from deep inside.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
I think this might be the best present I’ve ever gotten.

Jen perched back on the edge of the bed, beaming at him.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
Better than the wife you got on this trip?

Jeff cracked the can open with a satisfying snap-hiss  and took a long, grateful drink before answering.

**JEFF:** (mock-thoughtful)  
Close second.  Real close second.

Jen leaned over and kissed his cheek.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Right answer, Mr. Cremeans.

Jeff clinked the can against her forehead gently in thanks. The little fizz of the soda, the warm comfort of her beside him,  the knowledge that he hadn't compromised a damn thing that mattered…This was a man at peace.  At least, for now.

---

Jeff leaned back against the headboard,  savoring the last few swallows of his Mountain Dew, feeling it cut through the lingering exhaustion like a sharp little jolt.

Jen tucked herself next to him,  one leg draped lazily over his.

**JEFF:** (reflective, almost casual)  
You know why Commuted’s such a big hit over here?

Jen tilted her head curiously.

**JEN:** (soft)  
Because you’re good?

Jeff chuckled.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Well, yeah.  But it’s deeper than that.  It’s the lyrics, Jen. The way Kathy writes, the way Jeff Evans writes…They’re so damn forward about sex, about longing, about all the messy, complicated stuff.  It spooks a lot of people in the States.  MTV won’t touch some of it.  Top 40 radio? Forget it.

Jen frowned a little.

**JEN:** (quietly)  
But it’s honest.

Jeff nodded.

**JEFF:** (serious now)  
Exactly.  It’s honest.  Europe gets it more —  the BBC, New Music Express, all those guys.  They’re not as…Puritan about it.

He took a breath, searching for the right words.

**JEFF:** (more animated)  
But here?  Here in Japan?  The way we talk about sex, about bodies, about longing —  It’s like we’re already speaking their language.  No translation needed.

Jen blinked, thinking it through.

**JEN:** (soft, impressed)  
So you’re…ahead of the curve.  Way ahead.

Jeff smiled crookedly.

**JEFF:** (shrugging)  
Maybe twenty years ahead in the U.S.  Maybe two or three in London.  But right here, right now?  Tokyo’s ready.

Jen studied him —  really studied him —  and for the first time she felt it fully:  the scope, the ambition,  the way her husband had tied himself to something massive and unpredictable. Not just a band.  Not just a job. A movement.

**JEN:** (softly)  
I married a despicable revolutionary!

Jeff laughed again, warm and unguarded.

**JEFF:** (playful)  
You married an accountant, remember?

Jen kissed the underside of his jaw.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
A revolutionary in blue flannel and jeans.

He pulled her closer.

**JEFF:** (murmuring)  
You’re not wrong.

They lay there for a while,  letting the quiet Tokyo night press in around them —  the city buzzing just beyond their window,  the future humming under their skin.

---

Jen shifted slightly, propping her chin on Jeff’s bare chest,  watching him think, feeling the slow, steady rise and fall of his breathing.

**JEN:** (softly, but firmly)  
How much money did you throw away, Jeff… when they insulted me?

Jeff stiffened, just a little.  His fingers paused where they were idly stroking her hip. He didn’t answer right away.

**JEFF:** (quiet, serious)  
Don’t ask a question…if you don't want to know the answer.

Jen blinked —  not hurt, but seeing the weight he carried.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
I want to know.

Jeff sighed, tilting his head back against the headboard, staring up at the ceiling for a long beat before speaking.

**JEFF:** (gruff)  
High six figures.  Maybe a low seven, depending on how the licensing deal played out over a couple years.

Jen exhaled slowly. She hadn’t really understood until now — this wasn’t a scuffle over pride.  This was real.  Real consequences.  Real money.  Real future. And he had walked away from all of it. For her.

Jen laid her hand over his heart.

**JEN:** (softly, fiercely)  
I’m worth it.

Jeff looked at her then —  eyes dark, intense, steady.

**JEFF:** (absolute)  
You were worth it before we ever got on the plane.

Jeff shifted slightly, his hand still resting over hers on his chest,  his voice low, deliberate.

**JEFF:** (measured)  
It’s not just about the P&L.  Not really.

Jen frowned lightly, listening.

**JEFF:** (patient, explaining)  
Yeah, this limited edition deal would’ve been a nice hit —  turn a quick profit,  build a little cash pile.  But that’s not the real play.

He ran his free hand slowly through his hair, collecting his thoughts.

**JEFF:** (steady)  
It’s about mindshare.  It’s about getting Commuted’s name —  our sound —  into new ears.

Jen nodded slowly.

**JEFF:** (continuing)  
It’s about opening the market.  Getting some Japanese teenager to hear Bill’s synth lines and think it’s cool.  Getting somebody to see Kathy on stage and not just think “sexy frontwoman” —  but to actually hear her voice, her lyrics, the weight behind them.

He took a breath, his hand tightening lightly over hers.

**JEFF:** (quietly intense)  
We’re not just selling albums.  We’re selling a future.

Jen’s eyes widened slightly —  because it wasn’t arrogance in his voice.  It was pure, quiet belief.

**JEN:** (soft)  
You're building something bigger than just one record deal.

Jeff smiled, a little crooked, a little weary.

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Yeah.  Bigger than one album.  Bigger than me.  Maybe even bigger than them.

Jen pressed her lips to his bare shoulder.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
I’m proud of you.

Jeff closed his eyes for a second, letting that settle deep into his bones.

**JEFF:** (soft, hoarse)  
I just want to do right.  By them.  By you.

Jen smiled against his skin.

**JEN:** (teasing, but tender)  
Well… You’re off to a hell of a start, Mr. Cremeans.

Jeff chuckled, the sound a little raw, a little shaky.

They lay there for a long time afterward —  bodies entwined,  minds humming not just with love,  but with shared purpose. Building a life,  a future,  one risk at a time.

Jeff shifted again, staring up at the ceiling,  his arm still loosely around Jen’s bare shoulders.

**JEFF:** (quietly, almost confessing)  
Here’s the truth, Jen.

She stilled, listening carefully.

**JEFF:** (steady, but heavy)  
*69 Reasons* — that was the debut.  We sold more than ten million copies.

Jen blinked.  She knew they were successful —  but hearing it spelled out like that still hit different.

**JEFF:** (gruff)  
Then came the sophomore slump.

Jen frowned, puzzled.

**JEN:** (soft)  
But you still went platinum, right?

Jeff gave a small, mirthless smile.

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Yeah.  *Shall I Beg?* still went double platinum.  By any normal band's standards?  It was a dream come true.

He took a slow breath.

**JEFF:** (grittier)  
But compared to the first album?  Sales were down eighty percent.

Jen’s mouth opened slightly — shocked.

**JEFF:** (honest, almost weary)  
Eighty percent, Jen.  We got a lot of critical love —  Rolling Stone, Christgau, all the big names.  Everybody who’s ever dreamed of launching a band loved us.

He laughed once, short and sharp.

**JEFF:** (bitter smile)  
Except the cash registers.

Jen slipped her hand into his.

**JEN:** (quiet but fierce)  
You still made music.  Real music.

Jeff turned his head to look at her, really look at her —  this stubborn, beautiful woman who refused to measure him by numbers alone.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
Yeah.  We did.

He swallowed hard, his throat thick.

**JEFF:** (even softer)  
And maybe that’s what’s scaring me now.  We’re good.  We’re so darn good.  But what if good isn’t enough?

Jen squeezed his hand hard.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Then we keep being good.  We keep building.  And you remember that numbers don’t tell the whole story.

She kissed the side of his neck.

**JEN:** (warm, playful)  
Besides.  You’re stuck with me now.  Built-in fan club, lifetime subscription.

Jeff laughed for real this time —  low and rough and grateful.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Best fan club I could’ve asked for.

They stayed there, wrapped around each other,  not trying to solve it all tonight —  
but knowing they were on the same side of every fight to come.

---

Jeff stared up at the ceiling,  his voice dropping into a low, steady rhythm —  the kind of cadence he used when he was laying down something important.

**JEFF:** (quiet but firm)  
You just hit it, Jen.  One of the big reasons we wanted to partner with Sony Japan Music in the first place.

Jen shifted, curling a little closer, listening intently.

**JEFF:** (explaining, building)  
Commuted wants more than just album sales.  We’re trying to build a movement.  OK?   
A community.

He laced his fingers behind his head.

**JEFF:** (more animated now)  
We’ve got our newsletter, the fan organization, the whole grassroots network.   In English-speaking markets — the U.S., Canada, England — we can run that ourselves.   
Even Germany, most of Western Europe — they can read English passively.

Jen nodded slowly.

**JEFF:** (heavier)  
But Japan?  South Korea?  If we’re serious — if we really want mindshare here —  it has to be native.  Their language.  Their culture.  Their beat.

Jen’s eyes widened a little — beginning to feel the scale of it.

**JEFF:** (grim smile)  
I can’t do that sitting in Dayton, Ohio.  We need partners.  Sony’s the best at it.  Sony’s the biggest.  They know how to make it happen.

He turned his head, locking eyes with her.

**JEFF:** (quiet, hard)  
And Sony disrespected my wife.

Jen sucked in a breath —  because there it was, plain and unvarnished.

**JEFF:** (finishing, razor-sharp)  
So I told them…*Good morning*.

He said it like a weapon — polite, final, utterly lethal.

Jen smiled, slow and fierce.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
You’re not just building a movement.  You’re building one worth fighting for.

Jeff smiled back, the kind of smile that showed his teeth just a little.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
Damn right I am.

Jen propped herself up on one elbow, her hair tumbling down over her bare shoulder, staring at her husband like he’d just started speaking in tongues.

**JEN:** (disbelieving)  
Why on earth did the fans call themselves *The Convicted*?

Jeff chuckled softly, the sound low and familiar.

**JEFF:** (fond, a little amazed)  
Well…  What happens if you get to a place in life where you gotta ask the Man in charge to commute your sentence?

Jen blinked, processing.

**JEN:** (spluttering, stunned)  
You’ve got to be kidding me.  It’s… it’s that simple?

Jeff shrugged a little, smiling faintly.

**JEFF:** (matter-of-fact)  
It is, Jen.  It’s just one of those things.  We didn’t think it up.  We didn’t market it.  We didn’t push it.

He tapped his chest lightly with two fingers.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
It just… happened.  It was emergent behavior.

Jen shook her head slowly, amazed.

**JEFF:** (explaining, gentle)  
They named themselves *The Convicted*  because they haven't had their sentence commuted yet.

Jen’s mouth opened — and then closed again. Because that wasn’t just branding.  That was personal.  That was spiritual.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
It’s… beautiful.

Jeff nodded once, slow and sure.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
It is.

They lay there for a long moment, breathing together,  soaking in the meaning.

---

Jeff shifted slightly, propping himself up on one elbow, his voice dropping into that low, confessional tone he used when telling Jen something nobody else ever really heard.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Jen…  
  
Have you ever heard of the song “*The Left Hand*”?

Jen blinked, curious.

**JEN:** (shaking her head)  
Nope.  Is it… about left-handed people or something?

Jeff laughed once, a low bark.

**JEFF:** (grinning wider)  
Not even close.  The craziest fans — the superfans —  they’re almost exclusively women.  And when we put out the single for “*The Left Hand*,”  the cover art was simple.

He held up his own hand as if showing it off.

**JEFF:** (describing)  
Just Kathy’s left hand.  Her nails — this gorgeous, luscious red polish.  Classy. Tasteful.  But it sparked something.

Jen leaned closer, fascinated.

**JEFF:** (amused)  
And then…they started showing up to concerts — only their left hand painted red.  Not the right hand.  Only the left.

Jen’s mouth fell open a little.

**JEFF:** (chuckling)  
It turned into a secret handshake.  A silent signal.  It spread across the fan base like wildfire.

He shook his head in wonder.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
You can’t buy that kind of fanaticism, Jen.  You can’t market it.  Kathy caught the moment.  The temperature of young women in the States?  She had her finger — or her left hand — right on it.

Jen laughed, delighted and amazed.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
So what’s it actually about then?  World peace?  Midwestern loyalty?

Jeff snorted.

**JEFF:** (mock grim)  
Nope.

He leaned in a little closer, whispering like it was some dark scandal.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
It’s actually about betrayal.  And losing faith.  The left hand, traditionally, is the sinister hand — the hand that betrays.

Jen’s eyes widened in shock.

**JEN:** (stammering)  
So… they’re walking around showing off a betrayal symbol??

Jeff gave a slow, helpless shrug.

**JEFF:** (smirking)  
They think it’s empowerment.  Solidarity.  Sisterhood.

He shook his head again, marveling.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
They completely misread it —  and somehow made it beautiful.

Jen threw her head back and laughed.

**JEN:** (wiping her eyes)  
Only you guys could write a breakup song  and end up starting a feminist fashion movement.

Jeff smiled wide, real and proud.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
That’s Commuted for you, baby.  Accidental revolutionaries.

---

Jen’s eyes sparkled with excitement, her voice rising as the idea took shape.

**JEN:** (bright)  
You know what you ought to do?  Make an official Left Hand fan club kit!  Little card, little badge…  and a bottle of red nail polish!

Jeff smiled — but it was a thin, almost pained smile.  He took a slow breath, his voice lowering.

**JEFF:** (carefully)  
Jen… you… might want to read the lyrics before you jump in with both feet.

Jen blinked, her smile faltering a little.

**JEN:** (confused)  
What do you mean?  It’s a breakup song, right? Sad, but empowering?

Jeff rubbed a hand through his hair, staring up at the ceiling.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
It’s… not just about heartbreak.

He turned his head and locked eyes with her, dead serious.

**JEFF:** (heavy)  
The woman in the song —  she’s completely, utterly betrayed.  Cheated on. Left behind.

Jen’s face tightened, listening.

**JEFF:** (grimmer still)  
And she’s viewing it all through…through the lens of masturbation.

Jen’s mouth opened, but no sound came out.

**JEFF:** (soft, almost whispering)  
She’s literally…  masturbating with her left hand.  Because it’s the only thing she has left that can’t betray her.

Jen stared at him, stunned.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
How… how do you even know that?

Jeff’s expression darkened, almost guilty.

**JEFF:** (raw)  
Because the woman who wrote it —  Kathy —  told us.  That’s how she masturbated.  And she wrote that song…right after a horrific breakup.

He hesitated — just for a second — before laying it all out.

**JEFF:** (grim)  
And I’m scared to death… scared to death that she wrote it after breaking up with Jeff Evans.

Jen clutched the sheets instinctively, goosebumps rippling down her arms.

**JEFF:** (explaining, painfully honest)  
In the writing room —it’s not just Kathy and Jeff Evans.  Gilley’s there.  Jeremy Evans is there.  Bill pitches in.  Jim? Not so much.  But all of them… every one of them… they follow the one golden rule.

He turned his palm up, empty.

**JEFF:** (soft)  
Write what you know.

Jen swallowed hard.

**JEFF:** (finishing, hushed)  
And it’s scary… sometimes… what they know.

They sat there in silence for a long beat,  both feeling the deeper, darker undercurrents that surrounded Commuted —  not just noise, not just fame —  but something painfully, achingly real.

---

Jen sat forward, her eyes burning with something deeper now.  Something fiercely intelligent.

**JEN:** (pressing him)  
Is your band all about an unflinching depiction of female sexuality?  Of male sexuality?

Jeff met her gaze evenly.

**JEFF:** (nodding)  
Absolutely.  That’s the shtick.  That’s always been the shtick.

Jen didn’t blink.

**JEN:** (commanding)  
Then do it.

Jeff blinked.

**JEN:** (insistent)  
Then do it.  Own it.  Lean into it.  Be the bull in the china shop.

She poked his chest for emphasis.

**JEN:** (playful, but serious)  
You want to change the world?  Start charging, honey.

Jeff let out a short, surprised laugh — and she wasn’t done yet.

**JEN:** (grinning)  
Now…  you’re gonna have to buy me a copy.  *Shall I Beg?*  Go down to Tower Records, or wherever.  Buy the CD.

She folded her arms triumphantly.

**JEN:** (mock stern)  
And guess what, Mr. Cremeans?  I don't even own a CD player.

Jeff laughed harder now, rubbing his hands over his face.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
So you're buying that, too.  You're buying me the music and the machine to play it on.

She softened slightly, but her voice was pure steel underneath.

**JEN:** (earnest)  
If you're gonna be a bull — then be a bull.

She gave a sly little smile.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
They'll think we're the opposite of Gaijin.  They’ll think we're dangerous…and beautiful.

Jeff just sat there, shaking his head in awe —  because he realized, with bone-deep certainty,  she really did understand.

Jeff sat there for a long moment, still reeling a little from the sheer fire in her voice.  Then he asked, honestly — and maybe a little in awe:

**JEFF:** (gently)  
Are you sure?  You want to be a housewife?  A mother?  A stay-at-home mom?  Homeschool the kids?

There was a pause.  A long, thoughtful pause.  Jen looked down, twisting her fingers in her lap, and then looked back up at him.

**JEN:** (quiet, firm)  
There’s no higher calling.

Jeff swallowed hard.

**JEN:** (steady)  
I mean… I could be pretty good at other things.  I could probably be a teacher.  Maybe a principal, if I worked at it.

She smiled a little, almost embarrassed.

**JEN:** (small laugh)  
If I put my mind to it, I could even run a rock band.  I could balance the books.  I could be a sharp little accountant if I had to.

She leaned forward, her hands resting lightly on his knees.

**JEN:** (soft but blazing)  
But there's a higher calling. And it calls to me.

Jeff stared at her — his wife, his heart, this stunning little bolt of lightning wrapped up in a sundress —  and realized:  she wasn't choosing the "easy" path at all.  She was choosing the hardest one.  And she would do it with joy.

He whispered:

**JEFF:** (in awe)  
Then we’re gonna build a world for you to reign in, Jen.  A house filled with life.  With noise, and prayers, and kids flying through the kitchen.

Jen blinked, and her eyes glittered.

**JEN:** (whispering back)  
And love.  So much love.

And they both knew —  this was their real honeymoon vow.  The unspoken one.  The one that would carry them all the way into forever.

---

Jeff finally grinned, shaking his head like a man already defeated by love.

**JEFF:** (mock despair)  
Okay, wise girl.  Where’s the nearest Tower Records?

Jen just shrugged, smug as a cat.

**JEFF:** (pretending to grumble)  
Where can we even get a CD player in this town?  Maybe I ought to talk to the concierge.  "*Hi, can you help me? I need to buy my wife a rock album and the machine to play it on.*"

Jen laughed, the sound high and musical in the room.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
You should ask them if they sell left-handed nail polish, too.  You know — in case I want to really join the Convicted.

Jeff snorted, grabbing his notebook from the nightstand.

**JEFF:** (mock serious)  
Step one: Find Tower Records.  Step two: Find a Sony CD player.  Step three:  Convict my wife.

Jen beamed at him —  and somewhere deep inside, Jeff Cremeans made a vow:  
Whatever the world threw at them,  whatever chaos waited outside those hotel doors,  
he would find a way to give this woman everything she dreamed of.  And a little more, too.

---

Jeff caught her hand in his and tugged.

**JEFF:** (grinning wide)  
Come on.  Get your shoes on.

Jen blinked, startled.

**JEFF:** (gruff but teasing)  
Okay, okay.  Go ahead — get your panties on.  No, scratch that — leave ’em off.  Just get moving, woman.

Jen burst out laughing, yanking a simple skirt and shoes on while Jeff grabbed his wallet and scribbled something quick in his notebook. They raced down the 74 floors like giddy teenagers, the elevator roaring around them. At the hotel lobby desk, Jeff strode straight up to the concierge, still breathing a little heavy from their mad dash.

**JEFF:** (professional, polite)  
Excuse me —  Where can I find western music on compact disc?  And maybe a CD player to go with it?

The concierge, a middle-aged man with excellent English, smiled warmly.

**Concierge:**  
Ah, yes, sir.  You want the Akihabara district.  We call it Akiba.  Electronics, gadgets, music — all the best.

Jeff thanked him — and turned back to Jen with a look.

**JEFF:** (grinning wide)  
Field trip, Mrs. Cremeans.  You and me.  Gadgetland.

Jen was practically vibrating with excitement.

**JEN:** (delighted)  
Let’s go!

They practically skipped through the hotel lobby like a couple of kids,  ready to take on a slice of Tokyo neither one of them would ever forget.

---

The bus ride was a blur.  The city never stopped.  It was all neon signs, tiny alleys, whizzing bicycles, women in perfect business suits, men with briefcases sprinting full-tilt…  Jen clung to Jeff’s arm the whole way, watching wide-eyed like she’d just been dropped onto another planet.

In what felt like no time at all, they pulled into Akihabara — Akiba.

And Jeff grinned like a kid at Christmas.

**JEFF:** (low, thrilled)  
Welcome to Nerd Heaven.

Jen laughed — and then promptly stopped in her tracks.  
She stared, stunned, at the sheer riot of color, flashing lights, booths crammed with electronics, stacks of video games, anime posters, CDs, flashing signs, vending machines, hand-lettered cardboard signs screaming "SALE" in English and Japanese both.

It was… glorious.

**JEN:** (in awe)  
This is like…  
  
This is like five flea markets and two amusement parks smashed together.

Jeff squeezed her hand.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
And every booth’s got a stereo playing something different.  
  
You’re gonna love this.

They started walking, weaving through crowds of teenagers, businessmen, tourists.  
Vendors called out in rapid-fire Japanese, some words recognizable, most not.

Within minutes, they found a little shop — stacked floor to ceiling with CDs.  
Not just Japanese pop, either — there were whole sections labeled "Western Rock," "American Pop," "British Invasion."

Jeff made a beeline for the Western Rock section while Jen just stood there soaking it in.

**JEN:** (laughing)  
I feel like we’re hunting buried treasure.

**JEFF:** (serious)  
We are.

They dug through bins — and sure enough, there it was:  
Commuted — 69 Reasons  
Japanese special edition.  
The jewel case was slightly different — the liner notes translated, the cover art just a hair altered — but it was their record.

Jeff held it up triumphantly.

**JEFF:** (mock reverent)  
Behold.

Jen giggled, and snatched it from him.

**JEN:** (playful)  
Mine now.  
  
You’ll have to pry it from my cold, dead fingers.

Jeff mock-sighed.

**JEFF:** (teasing)  
Marriage is already so hard.

They moved to the electronics side, and after some hilarious mime-based negotiations, managed to buy a portable Sony Discman — sleek, black, very 1994.

Jen cradled both like treasures as they made their way back outside.

And just when Jeff thought the day couldn’t get any better, Jen darted into a side booth —  and came out five minutes later holding a ridiculous, adorable little keychain:  a tiny pink plastic sushi roll with a smiling face.

**JEN:** (beaming)  
For the future minivan keys.

Jeff blinked —  and laughed.  Big, belly-deep laughter that made passing Japanese businessmen turn and stare in mild amusement. They were building a life.  Piece by piece.  And it was going to be magnificent.

Jeff turned the jewel case over in his hands, frowning thoughtfully.

**JEFF:** (half-amused, half-bewildered)  
Huh.  They didn’t crop it.

Jen leaned over, squinting at the glossy cover.

**JEN:** (curious)  
What do you mean?

Jeff tapped the photo gently with his index finger.

**JEFF:** (explaining)  
In the U.S., they cropped it higher.  Made it imply she was nude — tasteful, suggestive. Here…  Nipples.  Plain as day.

Jen blinked — then laughed in shock.

**JEN:** (teasing)  
You can't get away with that back home, can you?

**JEFF:** (wry)  
Nope.  They’d have a congressional hearing.  Probably name a committee after it.

Jen snickered and traced the edge of the jewel case with her finger, considering.

**JEN:** (thoughtful)  
So… they just… don’t care here?

**JEFF:** (shrugging)  
Different standards.  Different culture.  Different relationship to nudity.  I deal with the States. Maybe a little Western Europe.  But once you get into Asia, Australia…  I let the local teams handle localization.  They know their people better than we ever could.

Jen cradled the case and gave a little mock gasp.

**JEN:** (mock scandalized)  
Does Kathy know?

Jeff barked a laugh.

**JEFF:** (grinning)  
Oh, she knows.  She just doesn’t care.  She likes pushing people’s buttons.

Jen looked at the CD again — then looked up at her husband —  and smiled.

**JEN:** (softly)  
It’s weird.  But it’s beautiful too.

Jeff tucked a stray strand of her hair behind her ear.

**JEFF:** (gentle)  
Exactly like you.

They stood there, surrounded by a million flashing lights, a million strangers, a million different worlds crammed into one street corner. And in that moment, the only thing that mattered was the little redhead on the cover —  and the way Jen looked at him like he was the only man on Earth.

---

Jeff sifted through the racks, flipping cases over with steady hands —  and there it was.

*Shall I Beg.*

He froze, studying the cover carefully.

It was the cover —  the one he'd approved back in New York, months ago —  the woman in the white T-shirt, walking away under the soft gold glow of a porch light.  Simple.  
Elegant.  Devastating.

**JEFF:** (low, relieved)  
Thank God.

Jen leaned over his arm, peeking.

**JEN:** (curious)  
What were you worried about?

Jeff gave a little shrug, still staring at the familiar photo.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
I was worried they’d… tweak it.  Japan sometimes localizes things differently.  Sometimes they think they need to sex it up.  But this…  This was a brand decision.  
A global image.

He turned the jewel case over — checking, double-checking —  the art, the liner notes, the layout —  all matched.

**JEFF:** (satisfied)  
It’s the same.  All over the world, it’s this image.

Jen tilted her head, studying it. The girl on the cover wasn’t flashy.  She wasn’t dramatic.  
She was just… leaving. It hit harder because it wasn’t sensationalized.

**JEN:** (softly)  
It’s sad.  But it’s beautiful too.

Jeff nodded.

**JEFF:** (serious)  
That’s the whole record.  
  
Betrayal.  Loss.  Forgiveness…  and maybe — maybe —  a second chance if you survive the fallout.

He slipped the CD into their little wire basket with the Discman already tucked inside. They had everything they needed now.  Music.  A player.  And each other.

**JEFF:** (gentle)  
You ready to listen to the real heart of it all?

Jen smiled at him — a big, bright, hungry grin.

**JEN:** (whispering)  
Let’s find a quiet place.  
  
And you can show me what your band really sounds like.

---

Jeff hefted the Discman carefully into the basket and turned back toward Jen, his expression serious.

**JEFF:** (emphasizing)  
*Shall I Beg?* It’s from a man's point of view.  A man watching the woman he loves walk away.  And he’s wondering —  should I drop to my knees and beg her to stay?  Would it even matter?

Jen’s brow furrowed.  
She mulled that over, turning it slowly in her mind.

**JEN:** (thinking aloud)  
I…I never thought your band put that much thought into it.  I mean —  I guess I always figured it was just… rock and roll.  Loud.  Angry.  Halfway to pornography sometimes.

Jeff gave a soft huff of laughter, not offended in the least.

**JEFF:** (gently)  
Yeah, we do sound angry sometimes.  But it’s earned anger.  It’s not random.

He tilted his head, studying her.

**JEFF:** (serious)  
When the band’s in a groove —  when we’re locked in?  We’re working 80, 90 hours a week.  Writing.  Rehearsing.  Rewriting.

Jen blinked at him, surprised.

**JEN:** (quiet)  
That much?

Jeff chuckled, but there was no real humor in it.

**JEFF:** (dry)  
And that’s the easy part, sweetheart.  Touring?  Don’t even get me started. You think it’s glamorous?  Try riding fifteen hours a day in a bus that smells like old socks and road dust.  Try getting up at 5 AM for sound check when you went to sleep at 3.  Try smiling for fifteen straight radio station meet-and-greets when you haven't eaten anything but gas station peanuts for two days.  Try living in a world where every mistake you make, every bad photo, every missed note —  it’s all immortalized.

Jen bit her lip, absorbing that.

**JEN:** (softly)  
It’s hard.  Harder than I thought.

Jeff nodded.

**JEFF:** (sincere)  
Harder than anyone outside the industry ever thinks.

They stood in the aisle, surrounded by racks of flashing electronics and bright neon signs.  And for a moment — just a moment —  the world went silent around them. 
It was just a man trying to explain to his wife why music, real music, mattered so much.

**JEFF:** (quiet)  
It’s work, Jen.  It’s a craft.  We don’t always get it right.  But when we do… it’s magic.

---

**JEFF:** (serious):  
"You remember how you were walking around nude yesterday, free as a bird, loving life?"

**JEN** (fondly):  
"Yeah… that was lovely. Even the public bath was lovely."

**JEFF:** (grim, steady):  
"Now, imagine if you’re Kathy Espich. You try the same thing. You’re just trying to live. Just breathe. And then two paparazzi with long lenses track your every move. They snap your picture. They capture your body without your consent. They strip your dignity one shutter click at a time. And then… they sell it."

(He pauses. His voice grows harder.)

**JEFF:** (furious, but controlled):  
"They sell it to tabloids. They sell it to scumbag rags. They sell it to people who think they own you. And you know what’s worse than not controlling your own image, your own body? It’s being enslaved. The moment you lose that control? You’re no longer free. You’re a product."

(Jeff exhales, forces a breath through his nose.)

**JEFF:** (quiet, seething):  
"Kathy’s not a whore. She’s not a toy. She’s not a body to be bought. She's a person. And when they steal her image, they steal her freedom. And when they steal her freedom… they make her a slave."

(There’s a long, aching silence.)

**JEN** (softly, deeply moved):  
"I… I never thought about it that way before."

---

**Jeff** (leaning in, handing the printed lyrics over):  
"Here you go. Start with this one, Jen. This is '*The Left Hand*.' It's probably the single most important thing to understand about Commuted if you want to get the real heart of what we’re doing."

**Jen** (taking the page carefully, scanning the first lines):  
"*In the shadows of the night, a fire ignites*…" (she murmurs) "*Passions swirling like a tempest… endless flights*."  
(she glances up at him, wide-eyed) "This is… more poetic than I thought it'd be."

**Jeff** (smiling faintly, watching her closely):  
"That's Jeff and Kathy for you. Bill builds the storm with his meter. Kathy rides the hurricane with her voice."

**Jen** (reading further, voice catching a little at the pre-chorus):  
"*She dances with the flames, unchained and free*…"  
(softly) "*An insouciant spirit, lost in ecstasy*…"  
(whispering) "Jeff… this isn’t just a song about sex, is it?"

**Jeff** (quietly):  
"No. It's about what happens after you’ve been betrayed. It’s about reclaiming yourself. It’s about surviving the aftermath."  (he taps the lyric sheet gently) "The 'lover' in the story? Long gone. The only one left is her. Her hands. Her left hand."

**Jen** (realization dawning, whispering):  
"Oh." (long pause) "Masturbation… from grief. From rage."

**Jeff** (nodding grimly):  
"Yeah. And nobody outside the band really knows. They hear the beat, they hear Kathy howling it into a mic, and they think it's just sex. But it's deeper. It’s grief weaponized into pleasure."

**Jen** (turning back to the sheet, tracing the chorus with her fingertip):  
"*Love’s a blade that cuts so deep… In the masquerade, where angels weep*…"  
(quiet, emotional) "That’s… devastating."

**Jeff** (watching her, voice low and serious):  
"Exactly why we don't censor ourselves. We sing what’s true, no matter how messy or dark or misunderstood it gets."

**Jen** (still reading, then chuckling darkly):  
"‘*The weight of the world dissolving like rain… Fingers weave a tapestry of sin*…’"  
(half to herself) "Kathy… Kathy doesn’t pull punches."

**JEFF:**  
"She can’t. Neither can Jeff Evans when he’s writing with her. Neither can Gilley. Neither can Bill. That’s the whole point of Commuted. We go there. We go all the way there."

**Jen** (meeting his eyes, fierce and proud):  
"Good. Don’t ever stop."  
(then, with a teasing grin)  
"But…maybe next time you write about a girl, at least give her a happy ending?"

**Jeff** (laughing, shaking his head):  
"Baby, if we did that… it wouldn’t be rock and roll anymore."

---

**Jeff** (leaning forward, voice low and intensely serious):  
"Jen, we go to great… obsessive lengths."  
(he taps two fingers lightly on the table, mimicking a slow, relentless beat)

**Jeff** (continuing, with heat behind his words):  
"When you listen to the rhythm of '*The Left Hand*' — really listen — imagine that beat was the pace you were pressing your clitoris."  
(he holds her gaze, daring her to flinch)  
"Now you tell me: what would happen to you in 3 minutes and 17 seconds?"

**Jen** (breath catching slightly, the flush creeping up her cheeks):  
(whispering) "I'd…I'd come."

**Jeff** (nodding, almost grimly):  
"Exactly. We are that obsessive. We're not kidding. Every single drum kick, every synth build, every line Kathy howls… it's calibrated."  
(he leans back a little, letting it sink in)  
"It’s not random. It’s warfare. Emotional and sexual warfare. And it’s all timed to the body. To the flesh. To the pulse that makes you human."

**Jen** (softly, still a little stunned):  
"You engineered a female orgasm… into a song?"

**Jeff** (grinning crookedly):  
"Welcome to Commuted, sweetheart."

---

**Jeff** (checking the back of the jewel case quickly, flipping it over and squinting):  
"Okay… still track six. Good. Didn't think they'd screw that up, but… you never know."  
(he slides the disc into the portable player they just bought, feeling a little thrum of anticipation)

**Jeff** (handing her the headphones, voice gentle but commanding):  
"Press play. Just… press play. Come back to me in three and a half minutes."  
(he leans back in the chair, folds his arms across his chest, and smiles)  
"I'm not going anywhere. I'm just gonna watch you."

**Jen** (nervous little laugh, cheeks already flushing):  
"You make it sound like I'm about to go through something…"

**Jeff** (grinning, warm but a little wicked):  
"You are."

**Jen** (putting the headphones on, taking a breath, pressing play):  
(silence falls, broken only by the tinny murmur of music he can almost imagine bleeding through)

**Jeff** (thinking, watching her):  
He watches her shoulders tighten slightly as the first drum hits —  
watches her eyes flutter closed —  watches the little swallow bob her throat as Kathy’s voice pours into her head, urgent, hungry, raw.  He watches the first quiver start in her hands, resting innocently on her lap.  He watches her breathing shift — a little faster, a little more shallow —  and a tiny, tiny involuntary shift in her hips, almost imperceptible unless you knew what to look for.

Jeff sees it all. And he knows —  he knows —  that the beat, the words, the throb of it is doing exactly what they designed it to do.

**(three minutes and seventeen seconds have never moved so slowly for either of them.)**

---

**Jen** (yanking the headphones off as the final pulse of sound fades, voice shaking, eyes bright and glassy):  
"Holy…holy Lord…"  
(her hands are trembling, her thighs clenched tight, she’s breathing like she just ran a race)

**Jeff** (quiet, deadly serious, leaning forward):  
"Tell me what you felt, baby. Don’t edit it. I need to know."

**Jen** (no hesitation, no filter, voice low and almost growling with the intensity of it):  
"It went straight to my clit. I couldn't even think. It’s… it’s that drum, Jeff. That beat. It's like my body knew what to do before I even thought about it. I didn’t even have to touch myself. I could feel it. Pounding into me. The words, the way Kathy sings them—"  

(she sucks in a sharp breath, shaking her head like she can’t even believe herself)  

"It's not even pornographic. It's worse. It's so true, it’s so raw, it just opens you up and leaves you standing there naked. Like you want something. Like you need something right now."  

(her voice breaks on that last word, her body betraying just how close she is to breaking)

**Jeff** (voice a low rumble, almost reverent):  
"That's exactly what we wanted."  

(he reaches out slowly, runs the back of his fingers lightly up her inner thigh)  
"We wanted truth, Jen. Not filth. Not titillation. Truth. The need… the ache… the loneliness… the hunger…"  

(he strokes higher, but doesn’t touch where she’s throbbing most)

**Jen** (choking a soft little moan, legs falling wider apart, whispering):  
"Jeff… if you don't touch me properly in the next ten seconds…"

**Jeff** (smiling, wicked, loving her wrecked, undone state):  
"Oh, I'm going to touch you, Mrs. Cremeans. I'm going to answer that song in your body the way it was always meant to be answered."

(and he rises up from his chair, pulls her to him, and her arms go around his neck without even thinking, clutching him, the music still ringing in her bones.)

**Jen** (murmuring against his skin, desperate and grateful and so, so his):  
"You were right. You were right about everything. I'm yours. I'm so yours."

**Jeff** (whispering into her ear, hoarse):  
"Good. Because I'm about to prove it to you again. And again. And again.
